Three Orthodox Views on Ambiguous Attributes
Sanusi presents three scholarly opinions on interpreting istiwa, hand, eye, and face.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three orthodox Sunni positions on interpreting ambiguous divine attributes and their shared commitment to transcendence (tanzih).

Core Idea
Three views, one principle: negate impossible literalism before interpreting or entrusting.

Sanusi introduces a foundational classification in Sunni theology: how to understand scriptural terms like 'hand,' 'eye,' and 'face' as applied to God. Before diving into proofs for each position, he first maps the three main scholarly approaches—Ash‘ari, Juwayni, and the Salaf—noting that all agree on a critical preliminary step. This lesson will orient you to these three positions and their shared foundation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the overall structure of three opinions.
Observe how the author lists the three views in a single sentence.
2
Identify the three opinions
Locate the three positions: Ash‘ari (attributes beyond eight), Juwayni (metaphorical interpretation), and Salaf (consigning meaning). Notice the names attached to each.
3
Notice the common ground
All three opinions begin with negating literal senses that are impossible for God. This is the shared principle of tanzih.
The text says 'after removing them from their literal senses which are impossible [for God] by consensus'.
4
Reflect on significance
Ask: Why does Sanusi present all three as valid? What does this teach about Sunni methodology? The commentary will help.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي كون الاستواء واليد والعين والوجه أسماءً لصفات غير الثمانية ، أو مُؤوّلةً بالاستيلاء والقدرة والبصر والوجودِ ، أو يُوقَفُ عن تأويلها وتُفوَّضُ معانيها إلى اللهِ تعالى ، بعد التنزيه عن ظواهرها المستحيلة إجماعاً . . ثلاثة أقوال ؛ للشيخ الأشعري ، وإمام الحرمين ، والسلف
And concerning whether al-istiwa, the hand, the eye, and the face are names for attributes other than the eight [essential attributes], or are interpreted metaphorically as domination, power, sight, and existence, or one refrains from their interpretation and consigns their meanings to God the Most High — after removing them from their literal senses which are impossible [for God] by consensus — there are three statements: belonging to al-Shaykh al-Ashʿari, Imam al-Haramayn, and the Salaf.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage presents three distinct scholarly positions on how to understand the scriptural terms 'istiwa' (establishing Himself over the Throne), 'hand', 'eye', and 'face' as they appear in the Quran and Hadith. The first view, attributed to Shaykh al-Ashʿari, holds that these terms are names for real attributes of God beyond the eight essential attributes (life, knowledge, will, power, hearing, sight, speech, and creativity). The second view, attributed to Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni, interprets them metaphorically: 'istiwa' as domination, 'hand' as power, 'eye' as sight, and 'face' as existence. The third view, attributed to the Salaf (early Muslims), is to refrain from any interpretation and consign the true meanings to God, while still negating any literal anthropomorphic senses that are impossible for God by consensus. The author presents these as three valid options within Sunni orthodoxy, all of which agree on the principle of tanzih (transcendence).

Key Terms
استواء
يد
عين
وجه
تأويل
تفويض
تنزيه
صفات خبرية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only one interpretation of ambiguous attributes is acceptable in Sunni Islam.
Correction: The passage presents three equally orthodox positions, all beginning with negating impossible literal senses.

Checkpoint
What is common to all three opinions on the ambiguous attributes?
A) They all interpret the verses metaphorically
B) They all affirm the literal meaning without qualification
C) They all negate any literal senses that are impossible for God by consensus
D) They all consign the meaning to God

Key Takeaway
Sunni orthodoxy allows three approaches to ambiguous attributes—affirmation of real attributes, metaphorical interpretation, or consigning meaning to God—as long as impossible literal senses are negated first.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite verses describing Allah's hand or face, do you automatically form a mental image? Have you ever consciously paused to negate the impossible literal sense, as this passage insists all must do? If not, what does that reveal about your reverence for Allah's transcendence?
?
Which of the three positions feels most natural to you? Could your preference be driven by a need for intellectual control or clarity, rather than humble submission to Allah's unknowable essence? How will you check your heart the next time you encounter an ambiguous attribute?
?
The Salaf chose to consign the meaning entirely to Allah, trusting Him without demanding a human explanation. Are you willing to admit that you do not fully understand some of Allah's attributes, or does your pride demand a definitive answer? What step will you take today to cultivate that trust?

Refuting the Qadariyya: Human Power Has No Effect
Sanusi refutes Qadariyya and distinguishes true school from two corrupt schools.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi refutes the Qadariyya by denying any causal effect of human power and how he distinguishes the true Ash‘arī school from both Jabriyya and Qadariyya.

Core Idea
Human power accompanies action but does not cause it; reward and punishment are conventional signs, not rational causes.

In this passage, Sanusi takes on a major theological opponent: the Qadariyya, who claim that humans create their own actions. He sharply refutes them by reiterating that contingent power has no effect—it merely relates to and accompanies the act. He also recalls a key principle: reward and punishment have no rational cause; they are conventional signs set by Allah. This lesson explores how this doctrine distinguishes the true school from two corrupt extremes.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation. Let the author's own words and tone come through before you interpret.
Notice the strong polemical term 'Magians of this community'.
2
Identify the two claims of the Qadariyya
The Qadariyya claim that the servant invents his own actions by his contingent power according to his will, and that reward and punishment follow from that.
These claims directly oppose the Ash‘arī position.
3
Understand the Ash‘arī counter: no causal effect
Sanusi states that contingent power has no effect in the act—it only relates to and accompanies it. Reward and punishment are conventional signs, not caused by the act itself.
This is the key point that separates the true school from Qadariyya.
4
See how this distinguishes the true school
By denying both absolute compulsion (Jabriyya) and human creation of acts (Qadariyya), the true school is distinguished. Sanusi notes this distinction is subtle and often confusing.
This completes the refutation and clarification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبقولنا : ( ليس لتلك القدرةِ الحادثة تأثير في الفصل أصلاً ، وإِنَّما تتعلَّقُ بهِ وتصاحبه فقط ) .. انفصلنا عن مذهب القدريَّةِ مجوس هذهِ الأمَّةِ القائلينَ بأنَّ تلك القدرة الحادثة في العبدِ بها يخترعُ العبد أفعاله على حسَبِ إرادتِهِ ، قالوا : وبذلك أطاع وعصى ، وعليهِ أُثيب وعُوقبَ ! وقد سبقَ لكَ : أنَّ الثواب والعقاب لا سبب لهما عقلاً عند أهل الحقِّ ، وإنَّما الطاعات والمعاصي أمارات جَعْليَّةٌ ، لا علل عقليَّةٌ. فتحقق بهذا : تمييز المذهب الحقِّ عن المذهبينِ الفاسدين ؛ وهما مذهبا الجبريَّةِ والقدريَّةِ ؛ فإنَّ تمييزه عنهما مما يلتبس على كثيرٍ
And by our saying: 'That contingent power has no effect in the act at all, rather it only relates to it and accompanies it'—we have separated from the school of the Qadariyya, the Magians of this community, who say that by that contingent power in the servant, the servant invents his actions according to his will. They said: 'And thereby he obeys and disobeys, and for that he is rewarded and punished!' And it has preceded for you that reward and punishment have no rational cause according to the people of truth, rather acts of obedience and disobedience are conventional signs, not rational causes. So it is realized by this the distinction of the true school from the two corrupt schools—namely the schools of the Jabriyya and the Qadariyya—for distinguishing it from them is something that is confusing for many.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Qadariyya (who affirm human power to create acts) and a summary distinguishing the true Ash‘arī school from both Jabriyya and Qadariyya. The author first states that by denying any effect of the contingent power in the act and affirming only relation and accompaniment, they separate from the Qadariyya, whom he harshly calls the 'Magians of this community' (majūs hādhihi al-umma). The Qadariyya claim that the servant invents (yakhtari‘u) his own actions by this power according to his will, and thus he deserves reward or punishment. The author counters by reiterating a previous point: reward and punishment have no rational cause; rather, obedience and disobedience are merely conventional signs (amārāt ja‘liyya), not rational causes. Therefore, the true school (al-madhhab al-ḥaqq) is distinguished from the two corrupt schools: Jabriyya (who deny any human power) and Qadariyya (who affirm creating power). The author notes that this distinction is subtle and often confusing for many people.

Key Terms
قدريّة
مجوس
أمارة جعليّة
مذهب حق
مذهب فاسد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Ash‘arī position is a vague middle ground that both affirms and denies human power ambiguously.
Correction: Sanusi clearly denies any causal effect of human power; power only accompanies the act. Reward and punishment are conventional, not rational consequences. This is a precise doctrine, not an ambiguous compromise.

Checkpoint
How does the author describe the Qadariyya in this passage?
A) The saved sect
B) The Magians of this community
C) Followers of the true school
D) Those who deny any human power

Key Takeaway
Sanusi denies any causal effect of human power, affirming that reward and punishment are conventional signs, thereby distinguishing the true school from both Jabriyya and Qadariyya.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you succeed in an act of worship, do you tend to feel a sense of personal achievement? How does knowing that your power has no effect in producing the act challenge that feeling? Will you now attribute every success and failure solely to Allah?
?
If reward and punishment are conventional signs rather than rational consequences, do you still feel the weight of your sins? Or does this make you rely more on Allah's mercy and less on your own deeds? How will this reshape your daily repentance?
?
Are there areas of your life where you quietly believe you are the 'creator' of your own actions—your career, your relationships, your character? How can you train yourself to see Allah's exclusive power in every moment, and what would change if you truly did?

The Danger of Blind Imitation and Corrupt Scholars
Author describes the corruption of people and scholars, then quotes Ibn al-Mubarak's poetry.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's critique of blind imitation and the misuse of religious authority as tools of Satan.

Core Idea
Blind imitation and corrupt scholars are tools Satan uses to block the path of salvation.

After establishing the importance of rational proof, the author turns to a lament about his own time. He describes how most people find truth burdensome and are instead deceived by Satan into thinking their blind imitation of popular beliefs is sufficient. He identifies the culprits—evil scholars and ignorant monks—who reinforce this delusion. The passage culminates in a poetic condemnation of corrupt religious and political leaders, reminding the student of kalam to beware of false certainty.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the tone
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the author's passionate tone—he speaks of 'blind jealousy' and 'foolish compassion.' This is a personal lament, not a dry argument.
The sentence is cut off at the end because the page ends; do not worry about the missing part.
2
Identify the mechanism of deception
Find where the author explains how Satan cuts off the path of salvation. Look for the phrase 'in order to make them see that they are in the most perfect state' and the role of blind imitation (taqlīd).
The Arabic phrase 'ولو بمحض التقليد' (even if by mere blind imitation) is key.
3
Understand the role of the scholars
Notice that Satan uses 'helpers'—evil scholars and ignorant monks—to confirm the delusion. The author distinguishes between good and bad scholars, so not all religious authority is trustworthy.
4
Reflect on Ibn al-Mubarak's poem
Read the poem carefully. It condemns kings and corrupt religious leaders. What does the line 'they sold their souls and did not profit' imply about their intentions?
The poem reinforces the idea that corruption comes from power and misplaced trust.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا مع علمي بما عليه أكثر أهل الزمان من ثقل الحق على قلوبهم والإصغاء بها إلى غرور زخارف الشيطان فيقطع عليهم طريق النجاة بأن يريهم أنهم على أكمل حالة في عقائد الإيمان وأن جزمهم بما اشتهر منها ولو بمحض التقليد هو غاية العرفان ويؤكد في قلوبهم هذا الغرور بأن يقودهم إلى سماع نحو ذلك من أعوانه من علماء السوء وجهلة الرهبان ولقد صدق ابن المبارك رضي الله عنه في قوله وهل أفسد الدين إلا الملوك وأحبار سوء ورهبانها فباعوا النفوس ولم يربحوا ولم تغل في البيع أثمانها لقد رتع القوم في جيفة يبين لذي العقل إنتانها ولقد كنت أدركتني غيرة عمياء وشفقة حمقاء على عوام المسلمين بل وعلى كثير من الطلبة المتفقهين لما رأيت من
This is with my knowledge of what most of the people of the time are upon: the heaviness of truth upon their hearts, and their inclination to the delusion of the embellishments of Satan, so he cuts off from them the path of salvation by making them see that they are in the most perfect state in the beliefs of faith, and that their certainty (jazm) about what is well-known among them, even if by mere blind imitation (taqlīd), is the ultimate knowledge. And he confirms this delusion in their hearts by leading them to listen to similar things from his helpers among the evil scholars (ʿulamāʾ al-sūʾ) and ignorant monks (ruhbān). And indeed Ibn al-Mubārak, may Allah be pleased with him, spoke the truth in his poem: 'What ruined the religion except the kings and the evil rabbis and monks? They sold their souls and did not profit, and their prices were not high in the sale. The people have frolicked in a carcass whose stench is clear to the intelligent.' And truly, I was overtaken by blind jealousy and foolish compassion for the common Muslims, and even for many of the students of jurisprudence (ṭalaba al-mutafaqqihīn), because of what I saw of...
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
In this passage, the author laments the spiritual state of his time. He notes that most people find truth burdensome and are instead attracted to Satan's deceptions. Satan misleads them by making them believe their blind imitation (taqlīd) of popular beliefs suffices for true knowledge. He uses evil scholars and ignorant monks to reinforce this delusion. The author then quotes Ibn al-Mubārak's poetry, which condemns kings and corrupt religious leaders for ruining the religion. The poem highlights how they sold their souls without profit. Finally, the author expresses personal concern for common Muslims and even many students of fiqh, but the sentence is cut off mid-thought as the page ends.

Key Terms

علماء السوء
رهبان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All religious scholars are trustworthy guides to the truth.
Correction: The author explicitly distinguishes between sincere scholars and 'evil scholars' and 'ignorant monks' who aid Satan in deluding people. One must use reason and discernment, not accept authority blindly.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what does Satan use to cut off the path of salvation from people?
A) Direct revelation from angels
B) Making them see themselves as perfect and relying on blind imitation
C) Forcing them to abandon prayer
D) Causing them to disbelieve in Allah

Key Takeaway
This passage warns that blind imitation and corrupt religious authority are major obstacles to true faith, and that sincere seekers must rely on rational proof rather than popular acceptance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear the truth but find it heavy upon your heart, do you turn away to what is easier, or do you strive to embrace it, even if it costs you your comfort and social standing? This lesson forces you to examine your own sincerity—are you willing to let go of every belief or habit that does not stand on proof, no matter how widely accepted it is?
?
The poet says the kings and evil scholars sold their souls and did not profit. Reflect on yourself: What have you sold your soul for? A reputation, a following, a comfortable life? Will you be among those who sell their souls cheaply, or will you hold firm to the truth even if it makes you unpopular?
?
Satan makes people see themselves as perfect in faith. Look at your own heart: do you assume you are on the right path just because you follow a group or a teacher? What if your certainty is actually a delusion? What concrete steps will you take today to ensure your faith is built on solid proof, not mere imitation?

Mu'tazili and Philosopher Views on Knowledge from Reflection
Sanusi explains Mu'tazili and Philosopher theories and states the refutation will follow

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazili theory of generation (tawallud) and the Philosophers' claim of reflection as an independent cause, and why the Ash'ari response rejects both.

Core Idea
Only Allah creates all things directly, not through generated powers or independent causes.

Sanusi now addresses two deviant theories about how reflection produces knowledge. The Mu'tazila propose a generated effect (tawallud) where the servant invents the reflection and resulting knowledge. The Philosophers go further, claiming reflection alone is sufficient. Both deny that Allah creates every event directly. As you read, note how each view undercuts tawhid, and that the refutation will follow from the principle that all beings are created by Allah without intermediary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Mu'tazili position
Read the first part where Sanusi explains the Mu'tazili theory of tawallud. Notice that they affirm Allah creates the power to reflect, but then the servant invents the reflection and knowledge.
2
Identify the Philosopher position
Read the second part where Sanusi states that the Philosophers claim reflection alone is an independent cause of knowledge.
3
Understand the refutation's basis
Read the final sentence where Sanusi indicates that the refutation will come from the principle that all beings must be attributed directly to Allah without intermediary.
This principle is the Ash'ari position that Allah is the sole creator of all actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما المعتزلة فقالوا: إنَّ العلمَ مُتولّد عنِ النظرِ؛ بمعنى: أَنَّ قدرة الناظرِ أثَرَتْ في العلم بواسطة تأثيرها في النظر الموصل إليه، وحقيقة التولُّدِ عندَهم: وجود حادث عن مقدور بالقدرة الحادثة، فغاية ما خلق الله تعالى للعبدِ عندَهم القدرة على النظرِ، أمَّا نفس النظرِ والعلم الحاصل بعدَهُ.. فالعبد عندَهم هو الذي اخترعهما بتلك القدرةِ التي خلق الله تعالى له، إلا أنَّهُ اخترعَ النظر بلا واسطة، والعلم بواسطة آلة النظر. وقالَتِ الفلاسفةُ: النظرُ وحدَهُ علَّةٌ مُستقِلَّةٌ لوجودِ العلم. والردُّ على هذين المذهبين بما تقرَّرَ، وسيأتي برهانهُ مِنْ وجوب إسنادِ الكائناتِ كلَّها إلى الله تعالى ابتداءً بلا واسطة.
As for the Mu'tazila, they said: Knowkledge is generated (mutawallid) from reflection, meaning that the power of the reflector acted upon knowkledge through its effect on the reflection that leads to it. And the reality of generation (tawallud) in their view is: the existence of an event (hadith) from something that is within power (maqdur) by created power. So the utmost that Allah Most High created for the servant in their view is the power to reflect; as for the reflection itself and the knowkledge resulting after it—the servant in their view is the one who invents both by means of that power which Allah Most High created for him, except that he invents reflection without intermediary, and knowkledge through the instrument of reflection. And the Philosophers said: Reflection alone is an independent cause (ʿilla mustaqilla) for the existence of knowkledge. And the refutation of these two schools of thought is by what has been established, and its proof will come from the obligation of attributing all beings entirely to Allah Most High initially without intermediary.
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage presents the views of the Muʿtazila and the Philosophers on the origin of knowkledge from reflection, then indicates that a refutation will come later. The Muʿtazilī theory of generation (tawallud) holds that the servant's power (qudra) acts upon reflection to produce knowkledge. Specifically, Allah creates only the power to reflect in the servant; then the servant, using that power, invents (ikhtaraʿa) both the act of reflection and the resulting knowkledge—reflection directly, and knowkledge through the instrument of reflection. The Philosophers go further, claiming that reflection alone is the independent cause (ʿilla mustaqilla) of knowkledge, meaning no divine intervention is needed. Sanusi states that the refutation of both positions is already implicit in what has been established (presumably the earlier proof that all things are created by Allah without intermediary) and that a more explicit proof will follow later. This sets up the positive Ashʿarī position that all events, including reflection and knowkledge, are directly created by Allah.

Key Terms
المعتزلة
التولد
القدرة الحادثة
اخترع
الفلاسفة
علة مستقلة
إسناد الكائنات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazili view holds that the servant's power can generate effects independently of Allah's direct creation.
Correction: The Mu'tazili affirm that Allah creates the power, but then the servant uses that power to produce effects, still ascribing some creatorship to the servant.

Checkpoint
According to the Mu'tazila, how does the servant obtain knowledge through reflection?
A) Allah creates reflection and knowledge directly
B) The servant's power generates knowledge by affecting reflection, which then produces knowledge
C) Reflection is the independent cause of knowledge
D) Knowledge is innate and does not require reflection

Key Takeaway
Both the Mu'tazili and Philosopher views deny that Allah directly creates every event, and the Ash'ari response is that all beings are created by Allah without intermediary.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every moment of understanding you have—even now, reading this—is directly created by Allah? Or do you, like the Mu'tazila, secretly think your own intelligence or effort is the real cause of your insight? Search your heart: when you study and grasp a concept, whom do you thank first? Yourself, or the One who gave you that moment of clarity?
?
If reflection alone could produce knowledge, as the Philosophers claim, then why do you sometimes struggle to understand something even after intense effort? Could it be that Allah withholds understanding until He wills it? Will you now repent of any pride you have taken in your own reasoning and acknowledge that your very ability to think is a direct gift from Him?
?
The Ash'ari principle says all beings come directly from Allah without any intermediary. Does your life reflect this belief? When you learn, do you act as if you are the one causing the learning, or do you constantly turn to Allah in dependence? Commit to one specific change today: after every study session, pause and sincerely say, 'All praise is due to Allah, who created this understanding in me.'

Refuting Those Who Forbid Nazar in Theology
Refutes the Hashwiyyah and defends the Companions' knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the claim that theological inquiry is forbidden is false, and how the Qur'an and the Companions' practice prove its legitimacy.

Core Idea
The Qur'an itself is filled with proofs of tawhid, and the Companions mastered them intimately.

This lesson tackles a common objection against kalam: that rational inquiry into theology is forbidden. The Hashwiyyah claimed that even the Companions avoided such discussion. Sanusi refutes this by pointing to the Qur'an's own arguments and the Companions' deep knowledge gained from sitting with the Prophet. The passage defends both nazar and the Companions' theological sophistication.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage begins by declaring the falsehood of the Hashwiyyah's claim.
2
Identify the two refutations
The passage refutes two related claims: (1) that nazar is forbidden, and (2) that the Companions did not engage in theological discourse. Find where each refutation occurs.
The refutation of the Companions' silence is introduced with 'وما يخلطون به...'
3
Reflect on the Companions' knowledge
Consider how the author argues that the Companions had superior theological knowledge. What specific reasons does he give? How does he connect it to the Prophet's own knowledge?
The passage mentions the Prophet seeing Allah during the Night Journey.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرد على الحشوية المانعين من النظر وأما ما يحكى عن بعض المبتدعة كالحشوية ونحوهم من أن النظر في علم التوحيد حرام.. فلا يخفى فساده وضلال معتقده لكل عاقل، إذ هو مصادم للكتاب والسنة وإجماع المسلمين الذين يعتد بهم. وما يخلطون به من أن الصحابة رضوان الله عليهم لم يتكلموا فيه.. فكذب منهم وافتراء، وكيف لا والقرآن مملوء بعقائد التوحيد وتقرير حججها على أكمل وجه؟! وفهم آية واحدة من آيات التوحيد لمن فتح له اليوم يتضمن حصول المعرفة بعقائد التوحيد كلها مع براهينها، فكيف بأولئك السادات الذين نزل القرآن على ألسنتهم، وإليهم المرجع فيما أشكل من معانيه، مع مجالستهم أعرف الخلق بالله تعالى وأكرمهم عليه، وصقالة قلوبهم وفيضان شموس المعارف عليها كإشارة [؟] إلى مشاهدة تلك الذات المرفعة، وسماعهم بآذانهم جوامع كلمه صلى الله عليه وسلم؟! وكيف تكون قوة معرفة من جالس من تتنزل عليه الملائكة من قبل الله تعالى في كل ساعة، ومن علمه بالله تعالى علم عيان ومشاهدة؟! إذ الصحيح أنه صلى الله عليه وسلم رأى ربه ببصره في الإسراء، ولو فرضنا إنساناً رأى ملكاً من الملوك بعينه، وكان أقرب
The refutation of the Hashwiyyah who forbid inquiry [in theology]. And as for what is related from some innovators like the Hashwiyyah and their ilk—that inquiry into the science of tawhid is forbidden—its corruption and the error of its believer are not hidden from any rational person, for it contradicts the Book, the Sunnah, and the consensus of Muslims whose opinion counts. And their mixing in that the Companions—may Allah be pleased with them—did not speak about it... That is a lie and slander from them. How could that be, when the Qur'an is filled with doctrines of tawhid and the establishment of their proofs in the most perfect manner? The understanding of a single verse of the verses of tawhid for one to whom it is opened today entails obtaining knowledge of all doctrines of tawhid along with their proofs. Then how about those masters upon whose tongues the Qur'an descended, and to whom is the reference for what is ambiguous of its meanings, along with their sitting with the most knowledgeable of creation of Allah and the most honorable to Him, and the polishing of their hearts and the flooding of the suns of knowledge upon them as an indication [?] to the vision of that elevated Essence, and their hearing with their ears the comprehensive words of him (peace be upon him)?! And how strong is the knowledge of one who sat with one upon whom the angels descend from Allah every hour, and whose knowledge of Allah is knowledge of direct vision and observation? For the correct view is that he (peace be upon him) saw his Lord with his sight during the Night Journey. And if we suppose a person saw a king with his own eye, and he was closer...
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Hashwiyyah (a group among the innovators) who claim that rational inquiry (nazar) into tawhid is forbidden. The author first declares the absurdity of this claim: it contradicts the Qur'an, the Sunnah, and the consensus of reliable Muslims. Then he addresses their argument that the Companions (sahabah) did not engage in theological discourse. The author calls this a lie, pointing out that the Qur'an itself is filled with tawhid doctrines and their proofs. He argues that understanding even one verse of tawhid—for those whom Allah opens—implies attaining all doctrines of tawhid with their proofs. He then extols the Companions' knowledge: the Qur'an was revealed in their language, they were the reference for ambiguous meanings, they sat with the Prophet (the most knowledgeable of Allah), their hearts were polished, and they heard the Prophet's comprehensive words. He emphasizes the strength of knowledge gained from being with the Prophet, who received angelic revelations hourly, and whose knowledge of Allah was direct vision (based on the view that the Prophet saw Allah with his sight during the Isra'). The passage thus defends both the legitimacy of nazar and the deep theological knowledge of the Companions.

Key Terms

النظر
التوحيد
الصحابة
رؤية الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Companions were simple-minded and avoided theological reflection.
Correction: The passage shows they mastered tawhid intimately through direct contact with the Prophet and the Qur'an.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the source of the Companions' deep knowledge of tawhid?
A) They studied books of kalam.
B) They directly witnessed the Prophet receiving revelation and heard his words.
C) They memorized hadith only.
D) They invented theological arguments.

Key Takeaway
The prohibition of theological inquiry contradicts the Qur'an and the example of the Companions, who acquired deep tawhid knowledge through direct contact with the Prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to follow the Qur'an, but do you shy away from using your intellect to understand its proofs of tawhid? What excuse will you give when asked why you never sought deeper knowledge?
?
The Companions mastered tawhid because they sat with the Prophet. You have the Qur'an and hadith—are you making the same effort to understand the doctrines of tawhid, or are you content with superficial belief?
?
If a person who saw a king with his own eye would have stronger knowledge, how strong is your knowledge of Allah when you have not even pondered His signs? What change will you make today to increase your certainty?

Refuting the Hashwiyya on Nazar and Defending the Companions' Knowledge
Sanusi refutes the Hashwiyya's prohibition of nazar and defends the Companions' theological knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Hashwiyya's claim that nazar is forbidden is false and how the Companions' deep knowledge of tawhid refutes their position.

Core Idea
The Quran itself commands reflection, and the Companions mastered tawhid through direct contact with revelation.

Sanusi turns to refute a dangerous innovation: the claim that rational speculation in theology is forbidden. He shows that this contradicts scripture and consensus, and that the Companions—whom the Hashwiyya cite—were actually the greatest practitioners of theological reflection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two claims
Read the passage and identify the two main claims of the Hashwiyya: that nazar is forbidden and that the Companions did not engage in it.
The author calls the first claim corrupt and the second a lie.
2
Refutation of the prohibition
Notice how Sanusi refutes the first claim by stating it contradicts the Quran, Sunna, and consensus.
He uses strong language: 'its corruption and misguidance is not hidden to any rational person.'
3
Refutation of the Companion claim
Examine how he refutes the second claim: the Quran is filled with tawhid proofs, and the Companions understood them best. He uses an analogy about a king's close associate.
The analogy shows that closeness to the Prophet yields knowledge akin to witnessing Allah.
4
Scriptural evidence
Observe the Quranic verses and hadith that praise the Companions, reinforcing their authority and knowledge.
These citations serve as direct textual proof against the Hashwiyya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الردُّ على الحشوية المانعينَ مِنَ النظر
وأما ما يُحكى عن بعض المبتدعة ـ كالحشوية ونحوهم ـ مِنْ أَنَّ النظر في علم التوحيد حرام .. فلا يخفى فساده وضلالُ مُعتقِدِهِ لكلِّ عاقل ، إذ هو مصادمٌ للكتاب والسنَّةِ وإجماع المسلمين الذينَ يُعتد بهم .
وما يُخلطون به من أن الصحابة رضوان الله عليهم لم يتكلموا فيه .. فكذب منهم وافتراء ، وكيف لا والقرآنُ مملوء بعقائدِ التوحيدِ وتقرير حججها على أكمل وجه ؟! وفهم آية واحدة مِنْ آيَاتِ التوحيد لمَنْ فُتِحَ لهُ اليومَ يتضمَّنُ حصول المعرفة بعقائدِ التوحيد كلها معَ براهينها ، فكيف بأولائك الساداتِ الذين نزل القرآنُ على ألسنتهم ، وإليهم المرجع فيما أشكلَ مِنْ معانيه ، مع مجالستهم أعرف الخلْقِ باللهِ تعالى وأكرمهم عليه ، وصقالة قلوبهم وفيضانِ شموس المعارفِ عليها كمشاهدة تلكَ الذاتِ المُرفَّعةِ ، وسماعهم بآذانهم جوامع كَلِمِهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ؟!
وكيف تكونُ قوَّةُ معرفةِ مَنْ جالسَ مَنْ تَنَزَّلُ عليه الملائكةُ مِنْ قِبَلِ الله تعالى في كلِّ ساعةٍ ، ومَنْ علمُهُ بِاللهِ تعالى علمُ عِيانٍ ومشاهدة ؟! إذ الصحيحُ أَنَّهُ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ رأى رَبَّهُ ببصرِهِ في الإسراء ، ولو فرضنا إنساناً رأى مَلِكاً مِنَ الملوكِ بعينه ، وكان أقربَ الناس إليه .. لكانَ أصحابُ ذلك الإنسان المجالسونَ لهُ أعرف بالمَلِكِ مِنْ غيرهم وإن لم يكونوا شاهدوا المَلِكَ ، وأنهم يصيرون في المعرفة به لقربهم مِنَ الأقرب إليه ومجالستهم له في حكم المشاهدين للمَلِكِ ؛ لقوَّة معرفتهم به .
فافهم بهذا المثالِ قوَّة معرفة الصحابة رضى الله تعالى عنهم لمولاهم جلَّ وعزَّ ، الذي أهَلَهم لمجالسة أكرم الخلْقِ عليه وأقربهم لديهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، بل أثنى عليهم مولانا جل وعزَّ في القرآنِ ثناءً عظيماً يُؤذِنُ بعلو مكانتهم عندَهُ ، وعظيم قربهم منه ، وأثنى عليهم نبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ وعَظَّمهم ؛ فقال تعالى : ﴿مُحَمَّدٌ رَسُولُ اللهِ وَالَّذِينَ مَعَهُ﴾ [الفتح : ٢٩] الآية . وقالَ : ﴿وَالسَّبِقُونَ الْأَوَّلُونَ﴾ [التوبة : ١٠٠] الآية . وقالَ : ﴿لَقَدْ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ إِذْ يُبَايِعُونَكَ تَحْتَ الشَّجَرَةِ﴾ [الفتح : ١٨] الآية . وقالَ : ﴿رِجَالٌ صَدَقُوا مَا عَهَدُوا اللَّهَ عَلَيْهِ﴾ [الأحزاب : ٢٣] الآية . وقال صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ : «أَقْتَدُوا بِاللَّذَيْنِ مِنْ بَعْدِي : أَبِي بَكْرٍ وَعُمَرَ» . وقالَ : «أَصْحَابِي كَالنُّجُومِ ، بِأَيِّهِمُ اقْتَدَيْتُمُ اهْتَدَيْتُمْ» .
The refutation of the Hashwiyya who prevent from speculation. As for what is reported from some innovators—like the Hashwiyya and their likes—that speculation in the science of tawḥīd is forbidden, then its corruption and the misguidance of its adherent is not hidden to any rational person, for it contradicts the Book, the Sunna, and the consensus of Muslims whose opinion is regarded. And what they mix in it, that the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) did not speak about it, is a lie and slander from them. How could that be when the Quran is filled with the doctrines of tawḥīd and the establishment of its proofs in the most perfect manner?! And understanding one verse from the verses of tawḥīd for one for whom it is opened today entails obtaining knowledge of all the doctrines of tawḥīd along with their proofs. How then with those masters upon whose tongues the Quran descended, and to whom is the reference for what is problematic of its meanings, along with their sitting with the most knowledgeable of creation about Allah Most High and the most honored by Him, and the polishing of their hearts and the overflowing of the suns of knowledge upon them like the witnessing of that exalted Essence, and their hearing with their ears the comprehensive words of him (peace and blessings be upon him)?! How can be the strength of knowledge of one who sat with one upon whom the angels descend from Allah Most High at every hour, and whose knowledge of Allah Most High is knowledge of direct sight and witnessing?! For the correct view is that he (peace and blessings be upon him) saw his Lord with his sight on the Night Journey. And if we suppose a person saw a king from among the kings with his own eye, and he was the closest of people to him, then the companions of that person who sit with him would be more knowledgeable of the king than others even if they had not seen the king, and they become in knowledge of him due to their closeness to the one closest to him and their sitting with him in the status of those who witnessed the king, due to the strength of their knowledge of him. So understand from this example the strength of the knowledge of the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) of their Lord (mighty and majestic), who qualified them to sit with the most honored of creation to Him and the closest to Him (peace and blessings be upon him). Rather, our Lord (mighty and majestic) praised them in the Quran with great praise indicating the highness of their station with Him and the greatness of their closeness to Him, and our Prophet and Master Muḥammad (peace and blessings be upon him) praised them and magnified them. He Most High said: {Muḥammad is the Messenger of Allah and those who are with him} [al-Fatḥ: 29]; and He said: {And the foremost forerunners} [al-Tawbah: 100]; and He said: {Truly Allah was pleased with the believers when they pledged allegiance to you under the tree} [al-Fatḥ: 18]; and He said: {Men who fulfilled what they had covenanted with Allah} [al-Aḥzāb: 23]; and the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) said: 'Follow the two after me: Abū Bakr and 'Umar'; and he said: 'My Companions are like stars; by whichever of them you follow, you will be guided.'
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Hashwiyya (a group of innovators) who claim that rational speculation (النظر) in the science of tawḥīd is forbidden. The author begins by stating that this claim is clearly corrupt and that its adherents are misguided, because it contradicts the three primary sources of Islamic law: the Quran, the Sunna, and the consensus of mainstream Muslims. The author then addresses a second objection often mixed in with the first: that the Companions of the Prophet did not engage in such speculative discourse. The author calls this a lie and slander, arguing that the Quran itself is filled with the doctrines of tawḥīd and their proofs in the most perfect manner. If a single verse of the Quran can, for one who understands it, yield knowledge of all tawḥīd doctrines and their proofs, then how much more would this apply to the Companions, upon whose tongues the Quran was revealed and to whom the community turns for clarification of difficult passages. The author then enumerates additional factors that elevated the Companions' knowledge: they sat with the Prophet, who was the most knowledgeable of creation about Allah; their hearts were polished; the suns of knowledge overflowed upon them as if they were directly witnessing the Divine Essence; and they heard the Prophet's concise words. Next, the author argues by analogy: if someone sees a king and is the closest person to him, then those who sit with that person gain such strong knowledge of the king that they become like eyewitnesses. Similarly, the Prophet saw his Lord (according to the correct view, with his sight during the Mi'raj), and the Companions sat with him, so their knowledge of Allah is exceptionally strong. The author concludes by citing Quranic verses and hadith that explicitly praise the Companions, showing their high rank and closeness to Allah. The overall argument is that both rational speculation and the Companions' authority are sound, and the Hashwiyya are refuted on both counts.

حشوية
صحابة
توحيد
إسراء
معرفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some claim that rational speculation (nazar) in theology is forbidden and that the Companions did not engage in it.
Correction: Sanusi shows that nazar is obligatory based on Quran and Sunna, and that the Companions were deeply engaged in theological reflection.

Checkpoint
What does the author use to refute the claim that the Companions did not engage in speculative thought about tawḥīd?
A) The Companions were too busy with military campaigns.
B) The Quran is filled with doctrines of tawḥīd and their proofs, and the Companions were the ones who understood it best.
C) The Prophet forbade them from discussing theology.
D) The later generations are more knowledgeable than the Companions.

Key Takeaway
The Hashwiyya's rejection of nazar is baseless, and the Companions are models of deep theological reasoning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Hashwiyya claimed that thinking deeply about Allah is forbidden. Do you ever avoid pondering the verses of the Quran because you feel it's too deep or not your responsibility? Will you commit to spending 10 minutes this week reflecting on one verse of tawhid until you understand its proof?
?
The Companions gained their knowledge by sitting with the Prophet. Who are the scholars you sit with—either physically or through their books and lectures? Are you actively seeking knowledge from those who truly inherit the Prophet's legacy, or are you content with superficial faith?
?
Sanusi uses the analogy of a king: those close to the king's confidant gain strong knowledge. Ask yourself: are you close to the people of knowledge? Do you prioritize sitting with them, or do you let distractions keep you from seeking the knowledge that brings you closer to Allah?

The Companions: Salt of the Religion and Warning Against Harming Them
The author narrates two hadiths on the stature of the Companions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the unique status of the Prophet's Companions as conveyed through two key hadiths and the severe consequences of opposing them.

Core Idea
The Companions are indispensable to Islam, and harming them is like harming Allah.

In this passage, the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) uses powerful imagery and a stern warning to establish the irreplaceable role of his Companions. The first hadith compares them to salt, essential for the preservation of the religion. The second hadith delivers a chain of consequences: harming a Companion is equivalent to harming the Prophet and Allah, inviting divine punishment. These teachings form a cornerstone of Sunni reverence for the Sahaba.

Guided Path
1
Read the two hadiths carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the simile in the first and the escalating warning in the second.
The superscript numbers indicate separate hadiths.
2
Reflect on the salt simile
Consider why salt is used. Salt preserves and gives flavor; without it, food is spoiled. Similarly, the Companions are essential for preserving and transmitting the faith.
This analogy emphasizes their indispensable role.
3
Trace the chain of harm
In the second hadith, note the progression: harming a Companion → harming the Prophet → harming Allah → divine punishment. Understand the gravity.
This chain shows the direct link between respect for Companions and respect for Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقالَ : « مَثَلُ أَصْحَابِي كَمَثَلِ الْمِلْحِ فِي الطَّعَامِ ، لَا يَصْلُحُ الطَّعَامُ إلا به (( ۱)
وقالَ : « اللَّهَ اللَّهَ فِي أَصْحَابِي ، لا تَتَّخِذُوهُمْ غَرَضاً مِنْ بَعْدِي ؛ فَمَنْ أَحَبَّهُمْ فَبِحُبِّي أَحَبَّهُمْ ، وَمَنْ أَبْغَضَهُمْ فَبِبُغْضِي أَبْغَضَهُمْ ، وَمَنْ آذَاهُمْ فَقَدْ آذَانِي ، وَمَنْ آذَانِي فَقَدْ أَذَى اللَّهَ ، وَمَنْ آذَى اللَّهَ سُبْحَانَهُ يُوشِكُ أَنْ يَأْخُذَهُ » (۲)
And he said: 'The example of my Companions is like the example of salt in food; food is only good with it.' (1) And he said: 'Fear Allah, fear Allah regarding my Companions; do not take them as targets after me. Whoever loves them loves them out of love for me, and whoever hates them hates them out of hatred for me, and whoever harms them has harmed me, and whoever harms me has harmed Allah, and whoever harms Allah—glory be to Him—He is about to seize him.' (2)
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage presents two hadiths from the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) concerning the high status of his Companions. The first hadith uses a simile: the Companions are like salt in food—just as food is ruined without salt, the religion (or the community) is not sound without the Companions. This emphasizes their indispensable role in preserving and transmitting the faith. The second hadith is a stern warning: the Prophet commands reverence for his Companions and prohibits treating them as targets for criticism. It explains that loving or hating them is directly linked to loving or hating the Prophet himself, and harming them is equivalent to harming Allah, which invites divine punishment. The passage thus establishes the unique honor of the Companions and the severe consequences of opposing them.

Key Terms
أصحابي
الملح
الطعام
آذاهم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Companions are fallible in a way that diminishes their unique virtue; they can be criticized freely.
Correction: These hadiths show their essential role and that harming them is equivalent to harming Allah, so they deserve utmost respect.

Checkpoint
According to the first hadith, what are the Companions compared to?
A) The stars
B) Salt in food
C) The pillars of Islam
D) The keys of Paradise

Key Takeaway
The Companions are essential to Islam—like salt to food—and harming them is a grave sin leading to divine punishment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever harbored any negative feeling or spoken ill of any Companion, even in jest? Given that the Prophet says harming them is harming him, what must you do to repent and change your heart?
?
The Prophet's Companions are like salt—indispensable. But do you truly treat them as essential to your faith? When you learn about their lives, do you admire them, or do you allow yourself to be influenced by modern criticisms? What one step can you take this week to increase your love and respect for them?
?
If loving the Companions is a sign of loving the Prophet, examine your heart: do your emotions and words towards the Sahaba reflect love for the Prophet? If not, what does that say about your claim to love him? Commit to memorizing and acting upon this hadith.

Prohibition of Reviling the Companions
The author narrates two hadiths forbidding reviling Companions and stating the punishment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the severe prohibition against reviling the Companions as established by two authentic hadiths, and why even great deeds cannot match their status.

Core Idea
Reviling the Companions incurs a curse and nullifies all deeds.

The author presents two powerful hadiths from the Prophet ﷺ that establish the inviolability of the Companions. The first warns that no amount of charity can equal their merit; the second pronounces a curse and rejection of deeds on anyone who reviles them. Together, they form a clear prohibition.

Guided Path
1
Read the two hadiths
Read the Arabic and translation of both hadiths carefully, noting their strong language.
The hadiths use emphatic terms like 'curse' and 'not accept any deed.'
2
Understand the severity
Reflect on the punishment: curse from Allah, angels, and people, and non-acceptance of deeds. Consider why such a severe warning is given.
This shows the high rank of the Companions.
3
Connect to the broader lesson
Consider how this prohibition is part of upholding the honor of the Companions and why it is important for correct belief.
It guards against sectarian discord.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال : ( لا تَسُبُّوا أَصْحَابِي ، فَلَوْ أَنْفَقَ أَحَدُكُمْ مِثْلَ أُحُدٍ ذَهَباً مَا بَلَغَ مُدَّ أَحَدِهِمْ وَلَا نَصِيفَهُ (۳) .
وقالَ : ( مَنْ سَبَّ أَصْحَابِي فَعَلَيْهِ لَعْنَةُ اللَّهِ وَالْمَلَائِكَةِ وَالْنَّاسِ أَجْمَعِينَ ، وَلا يَقْبَلُ اللهُ مِنْهُ صَرْفاً وَلا عَدْلاً (٤)
And he said: 'Do not revile my Companions, for if any of you were to spend gold equivalent to Mount Uhud, it would not reach a mudd of one of them nor even half of it.' (3) And he said: 'Whoever reviles my Companions, upon him is the curse of Allah, the angels, and all people; and Allah will not accept from him any compulsory or voluntary deed.' (4)
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage contains two further hadiths that explicitly prohibit reviling the Companions. The first hadith explains that no amount of voluntary charity can match the status of the Companions—even spending gold as much as Mount Uhud cannot equal what they sacrificed, highlighting their unique excellence. The second hadith pronounces a severe curse on anyone who reviles them, stating that such a person will not have any deeds accepted by Allah, whether obligatory (ṣarf) or supererogatory (ʿadl). The term ṣarf is interpreted as obligatory deeds and ʿadl as supererogatory, or vice versa; in either case, it means no good deed is accepted from them. This reinforces the gravity of disrespecting the Companions.

Key Terms
تسبوا
لعنَة
صرفاً
عدلاً

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that criticism of Companions is permissible if based on historical facts; these hadiths show it is categorically forbidden.
Correction: The hadiths use absolute terms—'whoever reviles'—without exception, indicating that any reviling, regardless of intent, incurs punishment.

Checkpoint
According to the second hadith, what is the consequence for one who reviles the Companions?
A) They will be forgiven if they repent
B) They will be cursed and their deeds will not be accepted
C) They will be fined compensation
D) They will be expelled from the community

Key Takeaway
Reviling the Companions is a grave sin that incurs a curse and renders all deeds unacceptable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever spoken ill of a Companion, even in jest or as part of idle talk? How does this hadith change your view of that action? Will you now repent and make a firm resolve to guard your tongue?
?
You may rely on your good deeds to secure Paradise. But if you harbor any resentment or contempt for a Companion, this hadith says your deeds will not be accepted. Are you willing to examine your heart and seek forgiveness?
?
The curse of Allah, angels, and all people is upon the one who reviles the Companions. Do you truly internalize that weight? When you hear others reviling them, will you remain silent or will you speak up in their defense?

The Superiority of the Companions and Their Chosen Ones
Two hadiths on the Companions and the four chosen caliphs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the importance of refraining from speaking about the Companions and the special rank of the first four caliphs as chosen by Allah.

Core Idea
When Companions are mentioned, hold your tongue; Allah chose them and singled out four as best.

In this lesson, Sanusi presents two prophetic hadiths that define our attitude toward the Companions. The first commands silence in their regard to avoid disrespect. The second affirms their unique status and highlights the four rightly-guided caliphs as the best among them. Let's read and reflect.

Guided Path
1
Read the two hadiths carefully
Read the Arabic text and English translation, noting the clarity of the Prophet's instruction.
The first hadith is a short imperative; the second is a longer declaration.
2
Compare the two hadiths
Notice the difference: one is a prohibition, the other an affirmation. Ask yourself why both are needed.
3
Reflect on the doctrinal implication
Understand that this passage establishes the rank of all Companions and the specific virtue of the four caliphs.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقالَ : « إِذَا ذُكِرَ أَصْحَابِي فَأَمْسِكُوا (۱)
وقال : ( إِنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى اخْتَارَ أَصْحَابِي عَلَى جَمِيعِ الْمُسْلِمِينَ سِوَى « النَّبِيِّينَ وَالْمُرْسَلِينَ ، وَاخْتَارَ لِي مِنْهُمْ أَرْبَعَةً : أَبَا بَكْرٍ وَعُمَرَ وَعُثْمَانَ وَعَلِيّاً ، فَجَعَلَهُمْ خَيْرَ أَصْحَابِي ، وَفِي أَصْحَابِي كُلِّهِمْ خَيْرٌ (۲)
And he said: 'When my Companions are mentioned, then refrain.' (1) And he said: 'Indeed Allah Almighty chose my Companions over all Muslims except the prophets and messengers, and He chose for me from them four: Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, and Ali, and He made them the best of my Companions, and in all my Companions there is goodness.' (2)
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage contains two more hadiths. The first is a directive: when the Companions are mentioned, one should refrain from speaking (i.e., from saying anything negative or engaging in disputes about them). The second hadith states that Allah chose the Companions over all other Muslims, except the prophets and messengers, giving them a unique rank. Furthermore, Allah specifically chose four—Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, and Ali—as the best of the Companions. However, the hadith also affirms that all the Companions are good. This reinforces the doctrine of the superiority of the Companions and the special virtue of the first four caliphs (al-Khulafa' al-Rashidun).

Key Terms
أمسكوا
اختار
أربعة
خير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think only the four caliphs are worthy or that all Companions are equal.
Correction: The hadith states that all Companions have goodness, but the four are the best. So there is hierarchy among them, yet all are good.

Checkpoint
According to the second hadith, who are the four Companions specifically chosen as the best?
A) Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, and Ali
B) Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, and Talha
C) Abu Bakr, Umar, Ali, and Ibn Abbas
D) Abu Bakr, Uthman, Ali, and Zubayr

Key Takeaway
The Companions are all good, but the four caliphs are the best among them, and we must refrain from speaking ill of any Companion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear someone criticizing a Companion—whether in conversation, online, or in a book—do you immediately remain silent, or does your tongue rush to defend or debate? What is stopping you from obeying the Prophet's clear command to 'refrain'?
?
Do you genuinely believe that every single Companion—including those you may feel ambivalent about—is good? Have you ever harbored doubts about any of them? If so, what would it take for your heart to fully accept what Allah has declared?
?
The Prophet said that Allah chose the four caliphs as the best of the Companions. In your daily life, do you honor Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, and Ali as the rightful leaders and models after the Prophet, or are you influenced by modern narratives that downplay their status? Make a concrete change this week to increase your love and respect for them.

Loving the Companions: Statements of Malik and Ayyub
The author quotes Imam Malik and Ayyub al-Sakhtiyani on the obligation to love the Companions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the severe consequences of hating or belittling the Companions and the virtues of loving each of the four caliphs as taught by early scholars.

Core Idea
Hatred of the Companions disqualifies one from the Muslim community and can amount to disbelief.

The early scholars, including Imam Malik and Ayyub al-Sakhtiyani, made powerful statements about the status of the Companions. Their words, grounded in Quranic verses, show that love for the Companions is not optional but integral to faith. This passage presents their warnings and encouragements, drawing clear lines between true belief and hypocrisy.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without worrying about meaning. Let the rhythm of the scholars' words sink in.
The passage contains two separate sayings: one from Malik and one from Ayyub.
2
Identify Malik's two statements
Notice that Malik gives two conditions: one about hatred leading to loss of spoils, and another about anger leading to disbelief. Each is supported by a Quranic verse.
Quran 59:10 and 48:29 are cited.
3
List Ayyub's six virtues
Ayyub lists six outcomes of loving each of the four caliphs and praising all Companions. Read each one and consider what it means.
The sixth virtue is incomplete in the text.
4
Reflect on the implications
Think about how these statements draw a clear boundary: love of the Companions is a sign of faith; hatred or belittlement is a sign of hypocrisy or disbelief.
This lesson guards against the misconception that political disagreement with a Companion is acceptable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال مالك : ( مَنْ أبغض الصحابة فليسَ لهُ في فَيْء المسلمينَ حق ؛ لقوله تعالى : ( وَالَّذِينَ جَاءُو مِنْ بَعْدِهِمْ يَقُولُونَ ... [الحشر: : ﴿ ١٠] الآية ((٣)
وقالَ : ( مَنْ غاظَهُ أصحابُ محمدٍ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ فهو كافر ؛ لقوله تعالى : لِيَغِيظَ بِهِمُ الْكُفَّارَ ﴾ [الفتح : ٢٩] ( (٤)
وقالَ أيوبُ السَّخْتيانيُّ : ( مَنْ أحبَّ أبا بكر فقد أقامَ الدينَ ، ومَنْ أحبَّ عمر فقد أوضح السبيل ، ومَنْ أحبَّ عثمانَ فقد استضاءَ بنورِ اللهِ ، ومَنْ أحبَّ عليّاً فقد استمسك بالعروة الوثقى ، ومَنْ أحسنَ الثناء على الصحابة فقد بَرِئَ مِنَ النفاقِ ، ومَنِ انتقص واحداً منهم (۱)
And Malik said: 'Whoever hates the Companions has no right in the spoils of the Muslims, due to the saying of Allah Almighty: "And those who came after them say..." [al-Hashr: 10] the verse.' (3) And he said: 'Whoever angers the Companions of Muhammad (peace be upon him) is a disbeliever, due to the saying of Allah Almighty: "That He may enrage the disbelievers with them" [al-Fath: 29].' (4) And Ayyub al-Sakhtiyani said: 'Whoever loves Abu Bakr has established the religion; whoever loves Umar has made the path clear; whoever loves Uthman has been illuminated by the light of Allah; whoever loves Ali has held fast to the firmest handhold; whoever speaks well of the Companions is free from hypocrisy; and whoever diminishes any one of them...' (1)
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage quotes two early scholars—Imam Malik and Ayyub al-Sakhtiyani—on the severe consequences of opposing the Companions. Imam Malik states that anyone who hates the Companions has no share in the Muslim community's spoils of war, citing Quran 59:10 which asks for forgiveness for all believers who came before. He also declares that anyone who angers the Companions is a disbeliever, based on Quran 48:29 which mentions that the Companions enrage the disbelievers. Ayyub al-Sakhtiyani then lists the virtues of loving each of the four caliphs: loving Abu Bakr establishes the religion, loving Umar clarifies the path, loving Uthman brings divine light, and loving Ali holds the firmest handhold. He adds that praising all the Companions is a sign of freedom from hypocrisy. The passage ends by stating that diminishing any one of them is equivalent to hypocrisy. These statements emphasize that love and respect for all Companions are integral to faith, and hatred or belittlement leads to disbelief or loss of standing in the community.

Key Terms
أبغض
غاظ
أقام الدين
أوضح السبيل
استضاء بنور الله
العروة الوثقى
برئ من النفاق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Disagreeing with a Companion on a political issue is permissible and does not affect one's faith.
Correction: These texts show that even anger or hatred towards the Companions is condemned as disbelief or loss of community standing. The scholars' statements draw a clear line, warning that such attitudes contradict the Quranic command to respect and love them.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Malik, why does a hater of the Companions have no right in the spoils?
A) Because they are not Muslims
B) Because the Quran verse asks forgiveness for those who came before, implying unity with them
C) Because they are disqualified by their actions
D) Because the Prophet forbade it

Key Takeaway
Love and respect for all the Companions is a fundamental part of faith; hatred or belittlement leads to severe consequences including disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you find any trace of dislike or resentment in your heart when you hear the name of any Companion, even one you might disagree with politically? This lesson teaches that such anger can be disbelief. Will you sincerely check your heart and remove any ill feeling?
?
If someone asks you why you love Abu Bakr, could you explain it using the exact phrase from Ayyub: 'Whoever loves Abu Bakr has established the religion'? What does that mean for your daily life? Are you acting on that love by following the path he established?
?
Ayyub said that speaking well of all the Companions frees one from hypocrisy. Examine your speech: do you ever repeat negative anecdotes about any Companion? Starting today, will you commit to only speaking good of them, and if you hear something negative, will you reject it? Why or why not?

The Sanctity of the Companions
Collection of hadiths and scholarly statements on the sanctity of the Sahaba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scriptural and scholarly basis for the obligatory love and reverence of all the Prophet's Companions, and the severe consequences of failing in this duty.

Core Idea
Love for the Prophet's Companions is a sign of faith; hatred is a cause for disbelief.

This passage gathers multiple prophetic hadiths and statements from early scholars to establish a fundamental Sunni doctrine: the Companions as a group are chosen by Allah, and any form of disrespect or hatred towards them is a serious spiritual offense. As you read, notice how the evidence escalates from etiquette to creed, and from worldly consequences to eschatological ones.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then the English translation. Get a sense of the weight of each statement.
The passage is a chain of quotations; each one adds a layer of emphasis.
2
Identify the main categories of evidence
The passage contains hadiths from the Prophet and statements from Malik and Ayyub al-Sakhtiyani. Note how they reinforce each other.
The hadiths command refraining from criticism; the scholars warn of severe spiritual penalties.
3
Focus on the consequences
Each statement mentions a consequence: loss of booty, disbelief, innovation, ruin, being deprived of the Prophet's intercession. List these consequences.
This shows that the issue is not merely etiquette but a matter of faith (iman).
4
Reflect on the required attitude
The passage requires love for all Companions, not just some. Ayyub's statement explicitly says one must love them all for deeds to be accepted.
This counters the misconception that selective love is acceptable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقالَ : « إِذَا ذُكِرَ أَصْحَابِي فَأَمْسِكُوا (۱) وقال : ( إِنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى اخْتَارَ أَصْحَابِي عَلَى جَمِيعِ الْمُسْلِمِينَ سِوَى النَّبِيِّينَ وَالْمُرْسَلِينَ ، وَاخْتَارَ لِي مِنْهُمْ أَرْبَعَةً : أَبَا بَكْرٍ وَعُمَرَ وَعُثْمَانَ وَعَلِيّاً ، فَجَعَلَهُمْ خَيْرَ أَصْحَابِي ، وَفِي أَصْحَابِي كُلِّهِمْ خَيْرٌ (۲) وقال مالك : ( مَنْ أبغض الصحابة فليسَ لهُ في فَيْء المسلمينَ حق ؛ لقوله تعالى : ( وَالَّذِينَ جَاءُو مِنْ بَعْدِهِمْ يَقُولُونَ ... [الحشر: : ﴿ ١٠] الآية ((٣) . وقالَ : ( مَنْ غَاظَهُ أصحابُ محمدٍ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ فهو كافر ؛ لقوله تعالى : لِيَغِيظَ بِهِمُ الْكُفَّارَ ﴾ [الفتح : ٢٩] ( (٤) وقالَ أيوبُ السَّخْتيانيُّ : ( مَنْ أحبَّ أبا بكر فقد أقامَ الدينَ ، ومَنْ أحبَّ عمر فقد أوضح السبيل ، ومَنْ أحبَّ عثمانَ فقد استضاءَ بنورِ اللهِ ، ومَنْ أحبَّ عليّاً فقد استمسك بالعروة الوثقى ، ومَنْ أحسنَ الثناء على الصحابة فقد بَرِئَ مِنَ النفاقِ ، ومَنِ انتقص واحداً منهم فهو مبتدع، وأخافُ ألا يصعد لهُ عمل إلى السماء حتى يحبهم جميعاً ) (۱) وقالَ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ : ( أَيُّهَا النَّاسُ ؛ أَحْفَظُونِي فِي أَصْحَابِي وَأَصْهَارِي وَأَخْتَانِي ، لا يُطَالِبَنَّكُمْ أَحَدٌ مِنْهُمْ بِمَظْلَمَةٍ ؛ فَإِنَّها مَظْلَمَةٌ لا تُوهَبُ فِي الْقِيَامَةِ غَداً (٢) . وقال : « أَحْفَظُونِي فِي أَصْحَابِي وَأَنْصَارِي ؛ فَإِنَّهُ مَنْ حَفِظَنِي فِيهِمْ حَفِظَهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى فِي الدُّنْيَا وَالآخِرَةِ ، وَمَنْ لَمْ يَحْفَظُنِي فِيهِمْ تَخَلَّى اللهُ مِنْهُ ، وَمَنْ تَخَلَّى اللهُ مِنْهُ يُوشِكُ أَنْ يَأْخُذَهُ (۳) وعنهُ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ : ( مَنْ حَفِظَنِي فِي أَصْحَابِي كُنْتُ لَهُ حَافِظاً يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ (٤) ومَنْ حَفِظَنِي فِي أَصْحَابِي وَرَدَ عَلَيَّ الْحَوْضَ ، وَمَنْ لَمْ يَحْفَظْنِي فِي أَصْحَابِي لَمْ يَرِدْ عَلَيَّ الْحَوْضَ ، وَلَا يَرَانِي إِلا مِنْ بَعِيدٍ (٥)
And he said: 'When my Companions are mentioned, then refrain (1). And he said: 'Indeed Allah Almighty chose my Companions over all Muslims except the prophets and messengers, and He chose for me four of them: Abu Bakr, 'Umar, 'Uthman, and 'Ali, and made them the best of my Companions, and in all my Companions there is good (2). And Malik said: 'Whoever hates the Companions has no right to the Muslim war booty (fay')—due to His statement: And those who came after them say... [al-Hashr 59:10] (3). And he said: 'Whoever angers the Companions of Muhammad (peace be upon him) is a disbeliever (kafir)—due to His statement: to enrage the disbelievers through them [al-Fath 48:29] (4). And Ayyub al-Sakhtiyani said: 'Whoever loves Abu Bakr has established the religion; whoever loves 'Umar has clarified the path; whoever loves 'Uthman has been illuminated by the light of Allah; whoever loves 'Ali has grasped the firmest handhold; whoever speaks well of the Companions has been cleared of hypocrisy (nifaq); and whoever belittles any one of them is an innovator (mubtadi'), and I fear that his deed will not ascend to heaven until he loves them all (1). And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'O people, preserve me regarding my Companions, my in-laws, and my relatives through marriage; let none of them demand of you a wrong, for it is a wrong that will not be forgiven on the Day of Resurrection tomorrow (2). And he said: 'Preserve me regarding my Companions and my helpers (Ansar); for whoever preserves me regarding them, Allah Almighty will preserve him in this world and the Hereafter; and whoever does not preserve me regarding them, Allah will abandon him; and whoever Allah abandons is about to be seized (3). And from him (peace be upon him): 'Whoever preserves me regarding my Companions, I will be a protector for him on the Day of Resurrection (4). And whoever preserves me regarding my Companions will come to me at the Basin (al-Hawd), and whoever does not preserve me regarding my Companions will not come to me at the Basin, and will not see me except from afar (5).
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of prophetic hadiths and statements from early scholars (Malik, Ayyub al-Sakhtiyani) emphasizing the sanctity of the Companions (Sahaba) and warning against any form of disrespect towards them. The author (Sanusi or compiler) presents these as proofs for the Ahl al-Sunna position on the Companions. The first hadith (from the Prophet) commands silence when the Companions are mentioned, implying refraining from criticism or slander. The second hadith affirms that Allah chose the Companions over all Muslims except prophets, and specifies four as the best. Imam Malik then delivers a strong warning: hating the Companions disqualifies one from a share in the Muslim war booty (based on Qur'an 59:10 which prays for those who came after them). In a separate statement, Malik declares that angering the Companions amounts to disbelief (kufr), citing Qur'an 48:29 which states that disbelievers are enraged by the Prophet's followers. Ayyub al-Sakhtiyani provides a more detailed exhortation: loving each of the four caliphs brings specific spiritual benefits (upholding the religion, clarifying the path, etc.), and loving all Companions absolves one of hypocrisy; belittling any Companion makes one an innovator (mubtadi'), and such a person's good deeds may not be accepted until they love them all. Finally, several hadiths urge preserving the Prophet's charge regarding his Companions, helpers, and relatives, promising divine protection, the Prophet's intercession at the Reservoir (al-Hawd) on Judgment Day, and warning that failure to preserve this charge leads to abandonment and distance from the Prophet.

Key Terms
الصحابة (al-Sahaba - the Companions)
أمسكوا (amsikoo - refrain)
النفاق (nifaq - hypocrisy)
مبتدع (mubtadi' - innovator)
الحوض (al-Hawd - the Basin/Reservoir)
فيء (fay' - war booty)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That it is acceptable to love some Companions while hating or belittling others, especially those involved in historical conflicts.
Correction: Ayyub al-Sakhtiyani explicitly states that one must love all Companions; belittling even one makes one an innovator, and good deeds may not be accepted until one loves them all.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Malik, what is the ruling for one who hates the Companions?
A) He has no share in the Muslim war booty
B) He is a disbeliever
C) He is a hypocrite
D) Both A and B, based on two separate statements

Key Takeaway
Love and respect for all the Prophet's Companions is a foundational requirement of Sunni Islam, with severe worldly and eschatological consequences for those who fall short.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever, even in your heart, felt annoyance or criticism toward any of the Prophet's Companions because of something you heard about their actions? How does the severe warning of this lesson—that angering them is kufr—make you feel right now? What concrete step will you take to cleanse your heart of any such feeling?
?
The Prophet ﷺ promises divine protection and his own intercession at the Basin for those who 'preserve him' regarding his Companions. Ask yourself honestly: Do you truly honour and defend the Sahaba in your conversations and thoughts? If not, what is holding you back? Will you commit to learning more about their virtues until your love for them is firm?
?
Imam Malik said that the one who hates the Companions has no share in the Muslim war booty (fay'), and Ayyub al-Sakhtiyani said that belittling even one Companion makes one an innovator whose deeds may not ascend. Reflect: Are you willing to lose your good deeds and the blessings of this community because of a careless word or a lingering resentment? What change in your daily speech and inner attitude will you make starting today?
