Sects and Disagreements
beginner
6 min
The Companions' Knowledge of Tawhid: Evidence from Hadith and Reports
Sanusi compiles hadiths and reports to argue against the claim that the Companions were ignorant of tawhid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi uses hadiths and reports about the Companions' high status to argue that they possessed true knowledge (ma'rifa) of tawhid, not mere imitation (taqlid).

Core Idea
The Companions' lofty status proves they had true knowledge of tawhid, not blind imitation.

In this passage, Sanusi compiles a series of hadiths and sayings from early authorities that emphasize the obligation to love and honor the Companions of the Prophet. These texts underscore their unique spiritual rank and the severe consequences of opposing them. After presenting this evidence, Sanusi poses a rhetorical question: if the Companions are so exalted, can it really be that they only had a superficial, imitative understanding of tawhid? This lesson will guide you through the evidence and the conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the full literal translation. Let the force of the multiple hadiths and quotes sink in before interpreting.
Notice the rhetorical question at the end—it shapes the whole argument.
2
Identify the key hadiths
The passage begins with a warning about not loving all Companions, then presents several hadiths about 'preserving the Prophet' regarding his Companions. Note the common theme: protection and reward for honoring them, punishment for failing.
3
Examine the additional reports
Read the quotes from Malik, Ka'b, and Sahl al-Tustari. Each reinforces the Companions' high rank—from the Prophet's own practice, intercession, and the condition of faith.
These are from early authorities, adding weight to the argument.
4
Understand the conclusion
After marshaling the evidence, Sanusi declares it unfitting that these noble elite were ignorant of tawhid or mere blind followers. The conclusion is implied: they must have had true knowledge.
This is the key point: the Companions' status implies knowledge, not taqlid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فهو مبتدع، وأخافُ ألا يصعد لهُ عمل إلى السماء حتى يحبهم جميعاً ) (۱) وقالَ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ : ( أَيُّهَا النَّاسُ ؛ أَحْفَظُونِي فِي أَصْحَابِي وَأَصْهَارِي وَأَخْتَانِي ، لا يُطَالِبَنَّكُمْ أَحَدٌ مِنْهُمْ بِمَظْلَمَةٍ ؛ فَإِنَّها مَظْلَمَةٌ لا تُوهَبُ فِي الْقِيَامَةِ غَداً (٢) . وقال : « أَحْفَظُونِي فِي أَصْحَابِي وَأَنْصَارِي ؛ فَإِنَّهُ مَنْ حَفِظَنِي فِيهِمْ حَفِظَهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى فِي الدُّنْيَا وَالآخِرَةِ ، وَمَنْ لَمْ يَحْفَظُنِي فِيهِمْ تَخَلَّى اللهُ مِنْهُ ، وَمَنْ تَخَلَّى اللهُ مِنْهُ يُوشِكُ أَنْ يَأْخُذَهُ (۳) وعنهُ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ : ( مَنْ حَفِظَنِي فِي أَصْحَابِي كُنْتُ لَهُ حَافِظاً يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ (٤) وا مَنْ حَفِظَنِي فِي أَصْحَابِي وَرَدَ عَلَيَّ الْحَوْضَ ، وَمَنْ لَمْ يَحْفَظْنِي فِي أَصْحَابِي لَمْ يَرِدْ عَلَيَّ الْحَوْضَ ، وَلَا يَرَانِي إِلا مِنْ بَعِيدٍ (٥) قال مالك : ( كانَ النبيُّ يخرجُ للبقيع في جوف الليل فيدعو لهم ويستغفر لهم كالمودَّعِ ، وبذلك أمرَهُ الله تعالى ، وأمرَ عليهِ السلامُ بحبهم وموالاتهم ، ومعاداة مَنْ عاداهم ((۱) . وعن كعب : ( ليس أحدٌ مِنْ أصحاب محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ إلا وله شفاعة يومَ القيامةِ ) ، وطلبَ مِنَ المغيرة بن نوفل أن يشفع له يوم القيامة (٢) قال سهل التَّسْتَريُّ : ( لم يؤمن بالنبي صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ مَنْ لم يُوقِّرْ أصحابَهُ ((٣) فانظر هذا الذي ورد في هؤلاء الساداتِ الأشرافِ الخواص ، الذين اختارهم الله تعالى على جميع المسلمين سوى النبيين والمرسلينَ ، رضيَ الله تعالى عنهم ، ونفعنا بحبهم ، وحشرنا في زمرتهم .. هل يصلحُ أنْ يُدَّعى في حقهم أنَّهم كانوا غير عارفينَ بعقائدِ التوحيدِ ، وأنَّ ما حصل لهم مِنْ ذلكَ إنَّما حصل لهم بمُجرَّدِ التقليدِ ؟!
He is an innovator, and I fear that no deed of his will ascend to heaven until he loves them all. (1) And the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, said: 'O people, preserve me concerning my Companions, my in-laws, and my relatives by marriage; let none of them demand from you an injustice, for it is an injustice that will not be forgiven on the Day of Resurrection tomorrow.' (2) And he said: 'Preserve me concerning my Companions and my supporters; for whoever preserves me concerning them, God Almighty will preserve him in this world and the Hereafter, and whoever does not preserve me concerning them, God will abandon him, and whoever God abandons is about to be seized.' (3) And from him, may God bless him and grant him peace: 'Whoever preserves me concerning my Companions, I will be a preserver for him on the Day of Resurrection.' (4) And: 'Whoever preserves me concerning my Companions will come to me at the Basin, and whoever does not preserve me concerning my Companions will not come to me at the Basin, nor will he see me except from afar.' (5) Malik said: 'The Prophet used to go out to al-Baqi' in the middle of the night and pray for them and ask forgiveness for them like one bidding farewell, and God Almighty commanded him to do so, and peace be upon him commanded love and allegiance to them and enmity toward those who show enmity to them.' (1) And from Ka'b: 'There is none of the Companions of Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, but he will have intercession on the Day of Resurrection,' and he asked al-Mughira ibn Nawfal to intercede for him on the Day of Resurrection. (2) Sahl al-Tustari said: 'He has not believed in the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, who does not honor his Companions.' (3) So look at what has been transmitted concerning these noble lords, the elite, whom God chose above all Muslims except the prophets and messengers, may God be pleased with them, and benefit us through love of them, and gather us in their company. Is it fitting that it be claimed concerning them that they were not knowers of the doctrines of tawhid, and that what they obtained of that was only obtained by mere taqlid?
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is an argument by the author (likely Sanusi or a later commentator) defending the knowledge of the Companions of the Prophet (s) concerning tawhid. The author first presents a series of hadiths and reports that establish the high standing of the Companions and the obligation to love and respect them. The first hadith (from an unnamed source) warns that whoever does not love all the Companions is an innovator and his deeds are in peril. Then several hadiths from the Prophet (s) command the community to 'preserve' him regarding his Companions, in-laws, and supporters, threatening that any injustice against them will not be forgiven, and promising preservation for those who honor them. Another hadith promises that those who honor the Companions will meet the Prophet at the Heavenly Basin (al-Hawd). Next, the author quotes Malik ibn Anas, who describes the Prophet's practice of visiting the cemetery of al-Baqi' at night to pray for the deceased Companions, and stresses the command to love them and oppose their enemies. Then a report from Ka'b al-Ahbar states that every Companion will have the power of intercession on Judgment Day, and he asked a Companion to intercede for him. Finally, Sahl al-Tustari declares that faith is incomplete without honoring the Companions. After marshaling these evidences, the author makes his point: given all this, how could anyone claim that the Companions were merely ignorant imitators (muqallidun) in matters of tawhid, and that their belief was mere blind following? The implication is that their elevated status and the Prophet's commands about them prove they possessed certain knowledge (ma'rifa) of tawhid, not just taqlid. The passage thus defends the Companions against accusations of ignorance and underscores the Sunni doctrine that the Companions are all reliable and possess true faith.

Key Terms
الصحابة
التوحيد
التقليد
المحبة
الموافاة
الشفاعة
االحوض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Honoring the Companions is merely a social or emotional obligation, not tied to the correctness of faith.
Correction: The author shows that honoring the Companions is tied to the very correctness of one's faith and the validity of one's deeds; it is a matter of theological importance.

Checkpoint
What is the main conclusion the author draws from the hadiths and reports about the Companions?
A) The Companions were all prophets.
B) The Companions were ordinary Muslims who learned through imitation (taqlid).
C) The Companions had true knowledge (ma'rifa) of tawhid and were not mere imitators.
D) The Companions should be loved but their knowledge is irrelevant.

Key Takeaway
The Companions' exalted status, confirmed by numerous Prophet hadiths, makes it untenable to claim they held only a blind imitation of tawhid; they possessed true knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider your own faith in tawhid, is it based on personal certainty and deep reflection, or have you simply adopted it from your environment? What specific step can you take today to move from taqlid to ma'rifa?
?
The Prophet commanded us to 'preserve him' regarding his Companions. Think of a time you heard a negative comment about a Companion—did you remain silent or defend them? How will you respond next time to fulfill this command?
?
If you were to meet the Prophet at the Heavenly Basin tomorrow, could you truthfully say you honored his Companions as he instructed? What is one concrete change you will make in your speech or heart toward the Sahaba starting now?

Sects and Disagreements
intermediate
6 min
The Companions' Perfect Knowledge of Tawhid
The author refutes the false claim that the Companions were ignorant of tawhid and affirms their perfect knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the claim that the Companions were ignorant of tawhid is false and how the author refutes it using evidence from early authorities.

Core Idea
The Companions were masters of tawhid; denying this is slander.

In this passage, the author tackles a serious accusation: that the Companions of the Prophet ﷺ were not truly knowledgeable in tawhid and merely followed blind taqlid. He marshals the words of early Muslim scholars to affirm their lofty status, then delivers a sharp refutation. This lesson will help you appreciate the high regard for the Companions in Sunni theology and understand the consequences of detracting from them.

Guided Path
1
Read the three authorities' statements
Begin by reading the quotes from Imam Malik, Ka'b al-Ahbar, and Sahl al-Tustari. Each one highlights a different aspect of the Companions' excellence.
Notice how the author uses these to build a cumulative case.
2
Ponder the rhetorical question
After presenting the evidence, the author asks a rhetorical question: 'Is it fitting to claim they were not knowers of tawhid?' Reflect on how this question forces the reader to reevaluate the accusation.
This is a common kalam technique to expose the absurdity of a claim.
3
Understand the condemnation
The author then declares that anyone who makes such a claim is a slanderous liar and an innovator. Understand the gravity of this label and the required response (shunning until repentance).
This shows the seriousness of defaming the Companions.
4
Trace the argument's flow
Map how the author moves from evidence to conclusion. The quotes support the claim of the Companions' perfection, leading to the rhetorical challenge and finally the condemnation.
This logical flow is typical of refutations in kalam texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال مالك : ( كانَ النبيُّ يخرجُ للبقيع في جوف الليل فيدعو لهم ويستغفر لهم كالمودَّعِ ، وبذلك أمرَهُ الله تعالى ، وأمرَ عليهِ السلامُ بحبهم وموالاتهم ، ومعاداة مَنْ عاداهم ((۱) . وعن كعب : ( ليس أحدٌ مِنْ أصحاب محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ إلا وله شفاعة يومَ القيامةِ ) ، وطلبَ مِنَ المغيرة بن نوفل أن يشفع له يوم القيامة (٢) قال سهل التَّسْتَريُّ : ( لم يؤمن بالنبي صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ مَنْ لم يُوقِّرْ أصحابَهُ ((٣) فانظر هذا الذي ورد في هؤلاء الساداتِ الأشرافِ الخواص ، الذين اختارهم الله تعالى على جميع المسلمين سوى النبيين والمرسلينَ ، رضيَ الله تعالى عنهم ، ونفعنا بحبهم ، وحشرنا في زمرتهم .. هل يصلحُ أنْ يُدَّعى في حقهم أنَّهم كانوا غير عارفينَ بعقائدِ التوحيدِ ، وأنَّ ما حصل لهم مِنْ ذلكَ إنَّما حصل لهم بمُجرَّدِ التقليدِ ؟! ولا خفاءَ أَنَّ مَنْ توهَّمَ ذلكَ في حقهم فهو مفترِ كذَّابٌ مُنتقِص لهم ، يدخل في مقتضى الوعيدِ السابقِ لَمَنْ سبَّهم ، ومُدَّعي تلكَ النقيصة في حقهم يفضحُهُ العقل والنقل ، وهو مُبتدِعٌ يجبُ هِجرانه ومعاداته إلى أن يتوبَ ؛ إذ المتضحُ في حقهم لكل عاقل والمقطوع بهِ أنَّهم حازوا قَصَبَ السبق في كلٌّ كمال ، لا سيما المعرفة بالله تعالى فتلك قد امتزجت بلحمهم ودمهم ، فصارَتْ مِنَ الأمور الضروريَّةِ في حق جميعهم
Malik said: 'The Prophet used to go out to al-Baqi' in the middle of the night to supplicate for them and ask forgiveness for them, like one bidding farewell, and Allah Almighty commanded him to do that, and he (peace be upon him) commanded love for them and loyalty to them, and hostility to those who are hostile to them (1). And from Ka'b: 'There is no one among the Companions of Muhammad (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) except that he will have intercession on the Day of Resurrection.' And he asked al-Mughira ibn Nawfal to intercede for him on the Day of Resurrection (2). Sahl al-Tustari said: 'He has not believed in the Prophet (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) who does not honor his Companions (3).' So look at what has been reported concerning these noble, distinguished masters, whom Allah chose above all Muslims except the prophets and messengers, may Allah be pleased with them, and benefit us by loving them, and gather us in their company... Is it fitting to claim regarding them that they were not knowers of the doctrines of tawhid, and that what they attained of that was only attained by mere blind taqlid?! There is no doubt that whoever imagines that regarding them is a slanderous liar and one who detracts from them, falling under the import of the previous threat against those who insult them, and the claimant of that deficiency regarding them is refuted by reason and transmitted knowledge, and he is an innovator whose shunning and enmity is obligatory until he repents; for it is evident to every rational person and certain that they took the foremost place in every perfection, especially knowledge of Allah Almighty, for that became mixed with their flesh and blood, thus becoming one of the necessary matters for all of them.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that the Companions were not true knowers of tawhid and only followed blind taqlid. The author begins by citing three authorities: Imam Malik, Ka'b al-Ahbar, and Sahl al-Tustari, all of whom praise the Companions. Malik reports that the Prophet used to visit the Baqi' cemetery at night to pray for the dead, and that Allah commanded him to love the Companions. Ka'b states that every Companion will intercede on the Day of Judgment, and he asked al-Mughira to intercede for him, showing their high rank. Sahl says that one who does not honor the Companions does not truly believe. The author then asks rhetorically: after all these virtues, can it be claimed that the Companions were not knowers of tawhid and only followed taqlid? He then declares that anyone who imagines such a thing is a slanderous liar and one who detracts from the Companions, falling under the threat against those who insult them. Such a person is an innovator (mubtadi') who must be shunned until he repents. The author concludes that it is evident to every rational person that the Companions were foremost in all perfections, especially knowledge of Allah, which became ingrained in their very flesh and blood, thus becoming a necessary matter for all of them.

Key Terms
الصحابة
التوحيد
التقليد
السب
المبتدع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Companions were not true knowers of tawhid; they merely followed blind taqlid.
Correction: The Companions had perfect knowledge of tawhid, which became ingrained in their flesh and blood, and they were chosen by Allah above all Muslims except prophets.

Checkpoint
What does the author say about someone who claims that the Companions were only blind followers (muqallidun) in matters of tawhid?
A) They are mistaken but not sinful.
B) They are slanderous liars and innovators.
C) They are excused because they follow the majority.
D) They are unbelievers.

Key Takeaway
The Companions possessed perfect knowledge of tawhid, and anyone who claims otherwise is a slanderous innovator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever find yourself underestimating the Companions, thinking that because they didn't write long theological books they were simple-minded? How does this passage expose that arrogance, and what will you do to correct it?
?
The author says knowledge of Allah was 'mixed with their flesh and blood.' Is your knowledge of Allah that intimate and instinctive? What concrete steps will you take this week to make tawhid more than just information in your mind?
?
If someone today insulted a Companion in your presence, would you remain silent? This passage commands hostility to those who are hostile to them. Where does your heart truly stand on loving the Companions, and what change is needed?

Refuting Defamation of the Sahaba
Sanusi refutes those who ascribe deficiency to the Sahaba.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sanusi considers anyone who defames the Sahaba to be a lying innovator and the evidence for the Sahaba's perfection.

Core Idea
Defaming the Sahaba is a serious innovation, not a minor mistake.

In this passage, Sanusi addresses a critical issue: the status of the Sahaba (the companions of the Prophet ﷺ). He delivers a strong refutation against those who attribute any deficiency to them. As you read, notice how he supports his claim with both rational and transmitted evidence, and how he declares the Sahaba's perfection to be a necessary matter.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once to get a feel for its rhythm and strength. Then read the translation.
Notice the forceful language: 'مفترٍ كذَّابٌ مُنتقِص'.
2
Identify the accusation and response
Find the point where Sanusi states the accusation (imagining a deficiency) and then his response (the person is a liar and innovator).
3
Understand the evidence
Sanusi says the claim is refuted by 'al-aql wa al-naql' (reason and transmitted evidence). Then he gives the reason: the Sahaba attained the highest rank in every perfection, especially knowledge of Allah.
This knowledge became a 'daruri' (necessary) matter for them.
4
Grasp the ruling
Note the ruling: such a person is a 'mubtadi'' (innovator) and must be shunned until he repents.
This shows the gravity of defaming the Sahaba.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا خفاءَ أَنَّ مَنْ توهَّمَ ذلكَ في حقهم فهو مفترٍ كذَّابٌ مُنتقِص لهم ، يدخل في مقتضى الوعيدِ السابقِ لِمَنْ سبَّهم ، ومُدَّعي تلكَ النقيصة في حقهم يفضحُهُ العقل والنقل ، وهو مُبتدِعٌ يجبُ هِجرانه ومعاداته إلى أن يتوبَ ؛ إذ المتضحُ في حقهم لكل عاقل والمقطوع بهِ أنَّهم حازوا قَصَبَ السبق في كلِّ كمال ، لا سيما المعرفة بالله تعالى فتلك قد امتزجت بلحمهم ودمهم ، فصارَتْ مِنَ الأمور الضروريَّةِ في حق جميعهم
And it is not hidden that anyone who imagines that about them is a lying impostor, a detractor of them, falling under the implication of the previous threat for those who insult them. And the claimant of that deficiency against them is refuted by reason and transmitted evidence, and he is an innovator whose abandonment and enmity is obligatory until he repents. For it is clear to every rational person and certain that they acquired the foremost rank in every perfection, especially knowledge of Allah Most High, which became mixed with their flesh and blood, so it became of the necessary matters concerning all of them.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of anyone who attributes any deficiency to the Sahaba. It begins by stating that such a person is a liar and a detractor, and falls under the divine threat against those who insult the Sahaba. Then it asserts that the claim is refuted by both reason (al-aql) and transmitted sources (al-naql). Such a person is an innovator (mubtadi') who must be shunned until he repents. The reason is that it is clear to every rational person that the Sahaba attained the highest rank in every perfection, especially ma'rifat Allah (knowledge of Allah), which was so deeply embedded in them that it became a necessary matter (daruriyya). This shows the impossibility of any deficiency in them.

Key Terms
مفتر
كذاب
منتقص
مبتدع
قصب السبق
المعرفة بالله
ضرورية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling on someone who claims deficiency in the Sahaba?
A) He is a disbeliever.
B) He is an innovator who must be shunned until repentance.
C) He is a sinner but not an innovator.
D) He is excused because he is ignorant.

Key Takeaway
Defaming the Sahaba is a serious innovation; they are perfect in all virtues, especially knowledge of Allah, which became a necessary part of their being.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever entertained or tolerated a negative thought about any of the Sahaba, even in jest? What does this passage demand you do about that thought right now?
?
The Sahaba's knowledge of Allah was so deep it became part of their flesh and blood. How does your own knowledge of Allah compare? What concrete change in your daily routine will you make to pursue that same level of certainty?
?
This passage says a detractor must be shunned until repentance. Is there anyone in your life who speaks ill of the Sahaba? Have you faced the discomfort of distancing from them? If not, what is holding you back?

The Saved Sect and the Necessity of Learning Sunni Creed
Sanusi cites the hadith of 73 sects and asserts the necessity of learning Ahl al-Sunnah books.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sanusi identifies Ahl al-Sunnah as the saved sect and why learning their creedal works is necessary for true faith.

Core Idea
The saved sect requires not just affiliation but active learning of the scholars' books.

After establishing the importance of rational judgments, Sanusi turns to the Prophetic prophecy about sectarian division. He cites the famous hadith of 73 sects and declares that the saved sect is Ahl al-Sunnah. But he does not stop there — he adds a crucial condition: being among them today requires learning what their scholars have recorded in their books. This lesson explores that condition and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the hadith
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the hadith about the 73 sects and the identification of the saved sect.
The hadith is a well-known prophecy about sectarian division.
2
Examine the condition for being among the saved
Sanusi states that today one is from Ahl al-Sunnah only if they learn what the scholars agreed upon in their books. Reflect on what this means.
This condition emphasizes active study, not mere birth or label.
3
Understand the result of learning
The passage says that by understanding their clarification, one becomes a true believer in agreement with Quran, Sunnah, and salaf. Consider why learning is necessary for true faith.
True faith is directly tied to correct belief learned from the scholars.

Source Text

وضم إلى ذلك بعضُهم ذكرَ حُجَج الرد على شبه المبتدعة التي دبَّتْ في الناس بعد موتهم دبيب النمل ، وقد أخبر بها النبيُّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ في قولِهِ : ( إِنَّ بَنِي إِسْرَائِيلَ افْتَرَقُوا عَلَى اثْنَتَيْنِ وَسَبْعِينَ فِرْقَةً . وَسَتَفْتَرِقُ هَذِهِ الْأُمَّةُ عَلَى ثَلَاثٍ وَسَبْعِينَ فِرْقَةً ، كُلُّهَا فِي النَّارِ إِلا وَاحِدَةً )  ، ولا شكّ أنَّ هذهِ الواحدة الناجية هي جماعة أهل السنة رضيَ الله عنهم ، ولا يكون منهم اليوم إلا مَنْ تعلَّمَ ما نضُوا عليهِ في كتبهم ، واستضاءَ قلبه بمعرفتِهِ ، وبفهم ما أوضحوهُ مِنْ ذلك يكونُ الإنسانُ في عقائدِهِ موافقاً لما جاءَ بهِ الكتاب والسنَّةُ ، وما كانَ عليهِ السلف الصالح ، وكان مؤمناً حقاً .
And some of them added the mention of the proofs of refutation of the doubts of the innovators which crept among the people after their death like the creeping of ants. And the Prophet (peace be upon him) informed of them in his saying: 'Indeed the Children of Israel split into seventy-two sects, and this community will split into seventy-three sects, all in the Fire except one.' There is no doubt that this one saved sect is the group of Ahl al-Sunnah, may Allah be pleased with them. And today no one is among them except one who learns what they agreed upon in their books, and whose heart is illuminated by knowledge of it. And by understanding what they clarified from that, a person becomes in his beliefs in agreement with what the Book and the Sunnah brought, and what the righteous predecessors were upon, and he becomes a true believer.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion by noting that later scholars added to their works the proofs to refute the doubts of innovators that spread after the Sahaba. It then cites the famous hadith about the division of the Ummah into 73 sects, with only one saved. The author identifies that saved sect as Ahl al-Sunnah. Crucially, he states that today, one is counted among them only if he learns what they (the scholars) have agreed upon in their books and his heart is illuminated by that knowledge. By understanding their clarifications, one's beliefs become aligned with the Quran, Sunnah, and the way of the salaf, and he becomes a true believer (mu'minan haqqan). This emphasizes the necessity of studying the theological works of Ahl al-Sunnah to be part of the saved sect.

Key Terms

الفرقة الناجية
أهل السنة
كتبهم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Simply being born into a Sunni family or claiming the label is enough to be saved.
Correction: The passage explicitly requires learning what the scholars agreed upon in their books (تعلم ما نضوا عليه في كتبهم) for one to be among them.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is necessary to be among the saved sect today?
A) Claiming to be Sunni.
B) Learning what the scholars agreed upon in their books.
C) Performing many good deeds.
D) Avoiding all theological discussions.

Key Takeaway
True faith in line with the saved sect requires actively learning and understanding the creed as transmitted by Ahl al-Sunnah scholars.

?
If you were to die tonight, could you honestly say that your heart has been illuminated by knowledge of the creed as taught by Ahl al-Sunnah, or have you relied on passive affiliation? What change will you make starting today to ensure you are a 'true believer' as described?

The Saved Sect: Ahl al-Sunnah and the Duty to Learn Their Creed
The author identifies the saved sect and its contemporary requirement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that being part of the saved sect today requires actively learning the creedal writings of Ahl al-Sunnah.

Core Idea
Salvation is tied to learning—not just claiming affiliation.

This lesson begins with the famous hadith about the 73 sects. The author identifies the saved sect and then explains what it takes to be counted among them today: not mere lip service, but a genuine study of their books that illuminates the heart and brings one's beliefs in line with the Quran, Sunnah, and the way of the salaf.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the hadith
Read the Arabic passage once to see the reference to the 73 sects and the identification of the saved sect.
The hadith is well-known; the author uses it as a starting point.
2
Identify the condition for being among the saved
Notice the phrase 'لا يكون منهم اليوم إلا من تعلم ما نضوا عليه في كتبهم' – this directly states the requirement.
3
Reflect on the result of learning
Consider how learning leads to illumination of the heart and agreement with Quran, Sunnah, and the salaf, resulting in true faith.
The passage emphasises that this knowledge transforms the believer.
4
Summarise the lesson
Write a one-sentence summary of the main teaching: salvation today requires active study of Sunni creedal works.
This connects to the learning objective.

وَسَتَفْتَرِقُ هَذِهِ الْأُمَّةُ عَلَى ثَلَاثٍ وَسَبْعِينَ فِرْقَةً كُلُّهَا فِي النَّارِ إِلا وَاحِدَةً، وَلَا شَكَّ أَنَّ هَذِهِ الْوَاحِدَةَ النَّاجِيَةَ هِيَ جَمَاعَةُ أَهْلِ السُّنَّةِ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهُمْ، وَلَا يَكُونُ مِنْهُمُ الْيَوْمَ إِلَّا مَنْ تَعَلَّمَ مَا نَضُوا عَلَيْهِ فِي كُتُبِهِمْ، وَاسْتَضَاءَ قَلْبُهُ بِمَعْرِفَتِهِ، وَبِفَهْمِ مَا أَوْضَحُوهُ مِنْ ذَلِكَ يَكُونُ الْإِنْسَانُ فِي عَقَائِدِهِ مُوَافِقًا لِمَا جَاءَ بِهِ الْكِتَابُ وَالسُّنَّةُ، وَمَا كَانَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَفُ الصَّالِحُ، وَكَانَ مُؤْمِنًا حَقًّا. وَبِالْجُمْلَةِ: فَلَا يَشُكُّ عَاقِلٌ أَنَّ مَنْ يَذُمُّ النَّظَرَ فِي عِلْمِ التَّوْحِيدِ فَهُوَ شَيْطَانُ إِنْسٍ، قَاطِعٌ لِطَرِيقِ اللهِ تَعَالَى، مُرِيدٌ أَنْ يَبْقَى الْجَاهِلُ عَلَى تَخْلِيطَاتٍ فِي عَقَائِدِهِ، وَبِدَعٍ وَإِلْحَادٍ فِي فَهْمِ أَشْيَاءَ مِنَ الْكِتَابِ وَالسُّنَّةِ عَلَى ظَوَاهِرِهَا مَعَ الْإِجْمَاعِ عَلَى تَأْوِيلِهَا، وَهَذِهِ شَهْوَةُ إِبْلِيسَ بِلَا شَكٍّ، وَمَنْ سَعَى فِي تَحْصِيلِ شَهْوَتِهِ فَهُوَ صَاحِبُهُ وَخَلِيفَتُهُ فِي الْفَسَادِ، وَالْعِيَاذُ بِاللهِ تَعَالَى.
And this nation will split into seventy-three sects, all of them in the Fire except one. And there is no doubt that this one saved sect is the group of Ahl al-Sunnah, may Allah be pleased with them. And among them today is only he who learns what they adhered to in their books, and his heart is illuminated with its knowledge, and by understanding what they clarified of that, a person becomes in his beliefs in agreement with what the Book and the Sunnah brought, and with what the righteous predecessors were upon, and he is a true believer. In summary: no intelligent person doubts that whoever disparages reflection on the science of tawhid is a human devil, a cutter of the path of Allah Most High, desiring that the ignorant remain upon confused mixtures in his beliefs, and innovations and heresy in understanding things from the Book and the Sunnah according to their apparent meanings despite the consensus on their interpretation. And this is the desire of Iblis without doubt, and whoever strives to fulfill his desire is his companion and his successor in corruption, and Allah forbid.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage opens with a doctrinal identification and a strong defense of kalam. It begins by citing the well-known prophetic hadith about the 73 sects, declaring the saved sect to be Ahl al-Sunnah (the Sunni community). The author then makes a crucial contemporary application: to be counted among this saved group today, one must actively learn the creedal positions that the early Sunni scholars recorded in their books, not merely claim affiliation. This learning is described as illuminating the heart and bringing one's beliefs into conformity with the Quran, Sunnah, and the way of the salaf, resulting in true faith. The second part delivers a blunt warning: anyone who disparages the study of tawhid (the science of God's oneness, i.e., kalam) is likened to a human devil who blocks the path of Allah, keeping the ignorant in confusion, innovation, and heresy by insisting on literal interpretations where scholarly consensus (ijma') has established figurative interpretation (ta'wil). The author identifies this as the fulfillment of Iblis's desire and condemns those who aid it.

Correction: The passage explicitly states that only those who learn the books of Ahl al-Sunnah are considered among them today.

The Grave Sin of Disparaging the Study of Tawhid
The author condemns those who disparage kalam and links them to Iblis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author condemns those who discourage the study of kalam as enemies of true faith.

Core Idea
Disparaging kalam is a devilish act that blocks Allah's path.

In the second part of this passage, the author delivers a stern warning against those who speak ill of the science of tawhid (kalam). He characterizes such individuals as human devils who actively work to keep people in ignorance, innovation, and heresy. This lesson explains the gravity of their offense and its connection to Iblis's own desire.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the strong language
Read the Arabic passage and pay attention to phrases like 'شيطان إنس' and 'قاطع لطريق الله' to feel the severity.
The author uses very strong terms to condemn the disparager.
2
Identify the two harms caused
Notice that the disparager wants the ignorant to remain in confusion and to insist on literal interpretations despite consensus on figurative interpretation.
These harms block people from correct understanding.
3
Understand the connection to Iblis
Reflect on why the author says this is the desire of Iblis and that aiding it makes one his companion in corruption.
This shows the serious spiritual danger.

Al-Shafi'i and the People of Kalam
Response to those who cite al-Shafi'i to forbid kalam; explains historical context.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a report of al-Shafi'i's statement against kalam is correctly understood as targeting only deviant innovators, not Sunni kalam.

Core Idea
Al-Shafi'i's ruling applies only to deviant sects, not all kalam.

Some argue that al-Shafi'i prohibited the study of kalam, citing a report that he said to beat them with palm branches. This lesson shows that the prohibition was specific to certain innovators of his time, such as 'Amr ibn 'Ubayd and Hafs al-Qard, and does not extend to Sunni theological inquiry.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its full translation to grasp the argument directly from the source.
Pay attention to the names mentioned.
2
Identify the false claim and the response
Notice that the passage begins by stating the false claim (that al-Shafi'i forbade kalam) and then gives the response: the ruling applies only to specific individuals.
3
Note the specific individuals and their sects
Two individuals are named: 'Amr ibn 'Ubayd from the Mu'tazila and Hafs al-Qard from the Qadariyya. These deviant sects are the target, not Sunni kalam.
This prevents the misconception that al-Shafi'i opposed all kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما يَستنِدُ إِليهِ بعضُ مَنْ أعمى الله بصيرتهُ في ادعائِهِ تحريم النظرِ في علم التوحيدِ ؛ مِنْ أنَّ الشافعي رضيَ اللهُ تعالى عنه رأى في أهل علم الكلام أنْ يُضربوا بالجريدِ . . نقولُ بمُوجَبِهِ في أولئك الذينَ كانوا يُسمَّونَ أهلَ علمِ الكلام في زمانِهِ ؛ وهم عمرُو بنُ عُبَيدٍ مِنَ المعتزلة في زمانه وحفصُ القردِ مِنَ القدرية وأضرابهم
And what some of those whom Allah has blinded in their insight rely upon in their claim of the prohibition of reflection on the science of tawhid, from that al-Shafi'i, may Allah the Exalted be pleased with him, held that the people of the science of kalam should be beaten with palm branches... We respond by applying it to those who were called the people of the science of kalam in his time, and they are 'Amr ibn 'Ubayd from the Mu'tazila in his time, Hafs al-Qard from the Qadariyya, and their likes.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage refutes the argument that al-Shafi'i banned kalam outright. The author states that those who argue for prohibition rely on a report that al-Shafi'i said the 'people of kalam' should be beaten with palm branches. The response is that this ruling applies only to the specific individuals who were known as 'people of kalam' in al-Shafi'i's era, who were innovators from deviant sects, such as 'Amr ibn 'Ubayd (Mu'tazili) and Hafs al-Qard (Qadari). It does not apply to all practitioners of kalam who adhere to Sunni methodology.

حفص القرد
القدرية
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That al-Shafi'i opposed all kalam
Correction: He opposed only the deviant sects of his time, like the Mu'tazila and Qadariyya.

Checkpoint

A) All Sunni kalam scholars
B) Only 'Amr ibn 'Ubayd and Hafs al-Qard and their like
C) All people who study logic
D) Only the Mu'tazila of all times

Key Takeaway
Al-Shafi'i's statement was directed at specific deviant groups, not at Sunni kalam scholars.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Objection: Does the Proof of Creation Cover Separate Substances?
Sanusi presents an objection that the proof of creation may not cover incorporeal substances.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection raised against the proof of the world's creation: that it may not apply to immaterial substances like separate intellects.

Core Idea
The proof of creation only directly covers bodies and accidents, leaving room for doubt about separate substances.

Sanusi now presents a potential challenge to the proof of creation that was discussed in the previous lesson. An objector points out that the demonstration only addresses bodies and their accidents. But if the world contains entities that are neither — such as the separate substances of the philosophers or the intellects accepted by al-Ghazali — then the proof does not establish their creation. Understanding this objection is crucial for appreciating the completeness of the theological argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice the conditional structure: 'If you say... then...'
The objector is speaking, not the author.
2
Identify the components of the proof
The proof covers bodies (ajrām) and their accidents (ṣifāt). Find these terms and note what is omitted.
3
Consider the implications
Why does the objector think this omission is problematic? What are the separate substances? Think about what entities might exist that are neither bodies nor accidents.
This sets up the need for a broader proof or a reply.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني : في بيان أقوال العلماء في الجوهر المفارق ( المجرَّد ) . إن قلت : إنَّ الذي حصل لنا مِنْ برهان هذه العقيدة حدوث جميع العالم على تقديرِ صحةِ أنَّهُ منحصر في الأجرام وصفاتِها ، وحصرُهُ هذين غير ضروري ، فعلى تقدير أن يكون في العالم ما ليس بجرم ولا قائم به - كما يقوله الفلاسفة في الجواهر المفارقة ، وتبعهم الغزالي في العقول - لم يحصل لنا برهان على حصولِ هذا الزائد على الأجرام وصفاتها
The second: Concerning the clarification of the opinions of the scholars on the separate substance (al-jawhar al-mufāriq) (the abstract). If you say: Indeed what we have obtained from the proof of this creed (ʿaqīda) is the contingency (ḥudūth) of the entire world on the assumption that it is confined to bodies (ajrām) and their accidents (ṣifāt), and its confinement to these two is not necessary. So on the assumption that in the world there is something that is not a body nor subsisting in it — as the philosophers (falāsifa) say concerning the separate substances (jawāhir mufāriqa), and al-Ghazālī followed them concerning the intellects (ʿuqūl) — then we have not obtained a proof for the occurrence of this extra [entity] beyond bodies and their accidents.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage presents an objection to the proof of the world's creation. The objector points out that the demonstration given only covers bodies (ajrām) and their accidents (aʿrāḍ). But if the world contains entities that are neither bodies nor accidents — i.e., separate substances like the intellects (ʿuqūl) claimed by philosophers — then the proof does not establish the creation of such entities. The objector also notes that al-Ghazālī followed the philosophers in positing such separate intellects, so even within the Islamic tradition this objection carries weight. The answer to this objection is presumably provided later in the text.

Key Terms
الجوهر المفارق
المجرد
الأجرام
الصفات
الفلاسفة
الغزالي
العقول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof of creation covers all existents.
Correction: The objector argues that the proof only directly covers bodies and accidents, so if there are non-bodily substances, they are not proven created by this argument.

Checkpoint
What does the objector claim is not covered by the proof of the world's creation?
A) Bodies (ajrām)
B) Accidents (aʿrāḍ)
C) Separate substances (jawāhir mufāriqa)
D) The human soul

Key Takeaway
The objection demonstrates that a proof limited to bodies and accidents does not necessarily establish the creation of all existing things, such as separate substances.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face an objection to your faith, do you honestly examine your own assumptions, or do you default to comfortable answers? This passage forces you to consider whether your certainty rests on unproven premises. What basis do you have for your core beliefs?
?
Sanūsī presents an objection that could unsettle a person's reliance on a proof. Have you ever had a question that made you doubt something you thought was solid? How did you handle it, and what does that reveal about your approach to intellectual challenges?
?
The objector points out that the proof may not cover all categories of existence. In your own spiritual life, are there areas where you have assumed your understanding is comprehensive, yet you have never questioned whether it accounts for every aspect? What steps can you take to seek a more grounded certainty?

Sects and Disagreements
beginner
5 min
Only Innovators Affirm Direction for God
Sanusi states that no Ahl al-Sunna affirmed direction, only Hashwiyya and Karramiyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Ahl al-Sunna unanimously deny direction for God, and that only the innovated sects of Hashwiyya and Karramiyya affirm it, with internal contradictions.

Core Idea
No true Sunni ever said God is in a direction.

This passage from Sanusi's al-Muqaddimat clarifies a crucial boundary: the position of Ahl al-Sunna on God's direction. Sanusi names the only sects that broke consensus, and shows their internal disagreements. This teaches us how to identify sound doctrine from deviant claims.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once carefully, then read the English translation. Let the author's claim sink in before analyzing.
Notice the concise style: Sanusi states a categorical denial first.
2
Identify the two innovated sects
Sanusi names the Hashwiyya and the Karramiyya as the only groups who affirmed a direction for God. Mark them.
These are the sects that broke the consensus of Ahl al-Sunna.
3
Examine their internal disagreements
Even though they agreed that God's direction is 'above', they split into sub-sects: some said He is in contact with the Throne, others said He is separate. Those who said separate further disagreed on whether the distance is finite or infinite.
This internal inconsistency is a sign of deviance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يقل بالجهةِ أحدٌ مِنْ أهل السنَّةِ ، وإِنَّما قالَ بها طائفةٌ مِنَ المبتدعة(۱) ؛ وهم الحشوية والكرامية ، وأجمعوا على أَنَّهُ يتعيَّنُ لهُ - تعالى عن قولهم - مِنَ الجهاتِ جهةً فوق ، ثم اختلفوا بعد ذلك ؛ فمنهم مَنْ قالَ : إِنَّهُ مماس للعرش تعالى الله عن ذلك علوّاً كبيراً ، ومنهم مَنْ زعمَ أَنَّهُ مباين لهُ ، ثم اختلف هؤلاء : فمنهم مَنْ زعمَ أَنَّهُ مباين بمسافة متناهية ، ومنهم مَنْ زعم أنَّهُ مباين بمسافةٍ غيرِ متناهية .
And not one of Ahl al-Sunna affirmed direction, rather only a group of innovators (1) affirmed it; they are the Hashwiyya and the Karramiyya. And they agreed that for Him—exalted above their saying—a direction 'above' is determined. Then they differed after that: among them are those who said that He is in contact with the Throne—exalted is Allah above that with great exaltation—and among them are those who claimed that He is separate from it. Then these differed: among them are those who claimed that He is separate by a finite distance, and among them are those who claimed that He is separate by an infinite distance.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage classifies the doctrinal positions regarding God's direction. Sanusi first asserts that no member of Ahl al-Sunna held that God is in a direction. Only two sects of innovators (mubtadi'a) did: the Hashwiyya and the Karramiyya. They all agreed that God's direction is 'above'. They then split: some claimed God is in contact (mummas) with the Throne, others that He is separate (mubayin). Those who said separate further split: finite vs. infinite distance. This shows the internal contradictions among those who affirm direction.

Key Terms
أهل السنة (Ahl al-Sunna)
مبتدعة (mubtadi'a)
حشوية (Hashwiyya)
كرامية (Karramiyya)
مماس (mummas)
مباين (mubayin)
مسافة (masafa)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Ash'ari or Maturidi scholars affirm a direction for God.
Correction: Sanusi explicitly states that no Ahl al-Sunna (which includes Ash'aris and Maturidis) affirmed direction. Only the innovated sects Hashwiyya and Karramiyya did.

Checkpoint
Which groups does Sanusi identify as the only ones who affirmed direction for God?
A) Ash'aris and Maturidis
B) Hashwiyya and Karramiyya
C) Salafis and Sufis
D) Mu'tazila and Jahmiyya

Key Takeaway
Ahl al-Sunna are unanimous that God is not in any direction; only innovators affirm direction, and they disagree among themselves.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself imagining Allah as being 'up there' or in a specific place? What does this passage teach you about correcting that assumption, and how will you train your mind to think of Allah without direction?
?
Sanusi declares that not a single Ahl al-Sunna affirmed direction—only innovators. Does your heart submit to this consensus, or do you feel a resistance? What does that resistance reveal about your attachment to innovated beliefs?
?
If you were to tell a friend that Allah is not in any direction, and they replied, 'But where is He then?'—how would you answer using the words of this passage? Are you prepared to defend the Sunni position with clarity and conviction?

Sects and Disagreements
beginner
4 min
The Innovators Who Affirm a Direction for Allah
Sanusi enumerates the innovators and their disagreements on direction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the beliefs of al-Hashwiyya and al-Karamiyya regarding Allah's direction and their internal disagreements.

Core Idea
All sects affirming a direction agree Allah is above, but then fall into confusion about contact and distance.

Sanusi begins by identifying the innovators who corruptly affirm a direction for Allah. He shows that despite their initial agreement, they immediately break into multiple conflicting positions. This internal inconsistency itself points to the error of their approach.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage describing the sects
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the names of the sects and the sequence of agreements and disagreements.
The sects are al-Hashwiyya and al-Karamiyya.
2
Identify the common agreement
All these sects agree that Allah necessarily has a direction: the direction of above (jiha fawq). Understand that this is the core error they share.
3
Trace the three internal disagreements
They disagree on three points: (1) whether Allah contacts the Throne or is separate from it, (2) if separate, whether the distance is finite or infinite. Note how each disagreement moves further into speculation.
These disagreements show that their foundation is unsound.
4
Reflect on the logical consequence
Ask yourself: if these sects cannot agree among themselves, how can their view be correct? This passage uses their own discord as implicit proof that the direction claim is false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المبتدعة(۱) ؛ وهم الحشوية والكرامية ، وأجمعوا على أَنَّهُ يتعيَّنُ لهُ - تعالى عن قولهم - مِنَ الجهاتِ جهةً فوق ، ثم اختلفوا بعد ذلك ؛ فمنهم مَنْ قالَ : إِنَّهُ مماس للعرش تعالى الله عن ذلك علوّاً كبيراً ، ومنهم مَنْ زعمَ أَنَّهُ مباين لهُ ، ثم اختلف هؤلاء : فمنهم مَنْ زعمَ أَنَّهُ مباين بمسافة متناهية ، ومنهم مَنْ زعم أنَّهُ مباين بمسافةٍ غيرِ متناهية .
[ إساءة الحشوية القائلين بإثباتِ الجهةِ لهُ تعالى
لأهل السنة والجماعة وللإمام أحمدَ ]
وقد لطَّخَتِ الحشويَّةُ بهذا المذهب الفاسد بعض أئمة أهل السنَّةِ ، فربَّما نسبوه لأحمد بن حنبل رضيَ اللهُ تعالى عنه (۲) ؛ إذْ همُ مُقلّدونَ لهُ الفروع ، فأوهموا أنَّهم كما تبعوه في الفروع تبعوه في العقائدِ ، وحاشاه أن تكونَ عقائده رضيَ الله تعالى عنه مثل عقائدِهم ؛ إذْ إمامته في علم التوحيد على طريقِ أهلِ السنَّةِ مُجمع عليها ، ومناظرتُه لأهل البدع وامتحانهُ معَهم في ذاتِ اللهِ تعالى مشهور مستفيض رضيَ تعالى عنه ، وجزاه عن نفسِهِ وعن المسلمين أفضل الجزاء
ولو قُدِّرَ أنَّ ذلكَ وقعَ منه - رضيَ اللهُ تعالى عنه ـ على سبيلِ الفَرْضِ والتسليمِ الجدليّ كما يُقدَّرُ وقوع المحالِ ، ولا حول ولا قوَّةَ إلا بالله العلي العظيم .. لم يكن لهم عذر ولا حُجَّةٌ باتباعِهِ(۱) ؛ إذ التقليد في عقائد الدين المجمع على صحتها لا يفيد عندَ كثيرٍ مِنَ المحققينَ فكيف بالتقليد فيما قام البرهان القطعي وحصل الإجماع على فسادِهِ ؟!
The innovators (al-mubtadi'a) (1) – they are al-Hashwiyya and al-Karamiyya – and they agreed that He – exalted above their saying – is necessarily characterized by a direction (jiha) from among the directions: the direction of above. Then they differed after that: among them are those who said that He is in contact with the Throne – Allah is exalted above that by a great exaltation – and among them are those who claimed that He is separate from it. Then these differed: among them are those who claimed that He is separate by a finite distance, and among them are those who claimed that He is separate by an infinite distance.
[The injury of al-Hashwiyya who assert a direction (jiha) for Him – exalted is He – to Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a and to Imam Ahmad]
And al-Hashwiyya have sullied with this corrupt doctrine some of the imams of Ahl al-Sunna, so they sometimes attribute it to Ahmad ibn Hanbal – may Allah be pleased with him (2) – because they are his followers (muqallidun) in the branches (furu'), so they falsely suggested that just as they follow him in the branches, they follow him in the creed ('aqa'id). Far be it from him that his creed – may Allah be pleased with him – should be like their creed; for his imamate in the science of tawhid according to the way of Ahl al-Sunna is a matter of consensus, and his debates with the people of innovation (ahl al-bid'a) and his examination with them concerning the Essence of Allah – exalted is He – are well-known and widely transmitted. May Allah be pleased with him and reward him on behalf of himself and the Muslims the best reward.
And if it were supposed that that occurred from him – may Allah be pleased with him – by way of hypothetical assumption and dialectical submission (taslim jadali), just as the occurrence of the impossible is supposed, and there is no power or strength except with Allah, the Most High, the Supreme – they would have no excuse and no proof in following him (1); for taqlid in the creeds of the religion that are agreed upon as sound is not beneficial according to many of the investigators (muhaqqiqin), so how about taqlid in that for which decisive proof (burhan qat'i) has been established and consensus (ijma') has occurred on its corruption?!
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the sects that affirm a direction (jiha) for Allah, particularly al-Hashwiyya and al-Karamiyya. The author first defines these innovators and describes their internal disagreements: they all agree that Allah is above, but then differ on whether He is in contact with the Throne or separate, and if separate, whether by a finite or infinite distance. Then the author addresses the defamation by al-Hashwiyya, who have tainted some Sunni imams by attributing their corrupt doctrine to Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal. The author strongly refutes this, stating that Ahmad's creed is pure and based on the way of Ahl al-Sunna, and that his debates with innovators are well-known. Finally, the author argues that even if Ahmad had hypothetically conceded such a point in dialectical argument (taslim jadali), it would not be permissible to follow him in that, because taqlid in matters of creed that are agreed upon as sound is not valid, and even more so when decisive proof and consensus indicate the corruption of that belief.

Key Terms
المبتدعة
الحشوية
الكرامية
الجهة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the one point on which all the innovators agree regarding Allah?
A) That He is in contact with the Throne
B) That He is separate from the Throne by a finite distance
C) That He necessarily has the direction of above
D) That He is separate by an infinite distance

Key Takeaway
Even among sects that affirm a direction for Allah, there is no agreement on how He relates to the Throne, revealing the corruption of their foundational claim.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson shows that innovators who affirm a direction for Allah cannot agree on the details. Have you ever assumed that a common belief among Muslims (like 'Allah is above') is automatically correct without verifying it against the understanding of Ahl al-Sunna? What will you do to ensure your beliefs about Allah are based on sound evidence?
?
Sanusi highlights internal contradictions among sects. Reflect on your own understanding of Allah's attributes: Are there any descriptions you hold that might be influenced by human imagination rather than revelation? Commit to studying the creed of the Salaf on one attribute this week.
?
The innovators' disagreements stemmed from using human analogies for Allah. In your daily life, how often do you fall into thinking about Allah in human terms? What practical step can you take today to purify your concept of Allah from such comparisons?

Defending Imam Ahmad from the False Attribution of Direction
Sanusi defends Imam Ahmad and argues against taqlid in corrupt creed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Ahmad is not to be associated with the belief in direction, and why following him in such a matter is not valid.

Core Idea
Imam Ahmad's creed is pure, and following him in a corrupt belief is never excusable—especially when decisive proof and consensus condemn it.

Having described the sects, Sanusi now turns to a major injustice: the Hashwiyya have tried to drag Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal into their corrupt doctrine. Sanusi passionately defends Ahmad, showing his impeccable orthodoxy, and then argues that even if Ahmad had hypothetically said such a thing in a dialectical context, following him would be invalid because taqlid in creed is unacceptable, especially when decisive proof and consensus refute the claim.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about al-Hashwiyya's defamation
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice how Sanusi describes the Hashwiyya 'sullying' some imams and falsely attributing their view to Imam Ahmad.
Key phrase: 'لطخت الحشوية بهذا المذهب الفاسد بعض أئمة أهل السنة'
2
Understand Sanusi's defense of Imam Ahmad
Sanusi lists three proofs of Ahmad's orthodoxy: his imama in tawhid by consensus, his famous debates with innovators, and his examination regarding Allah's Essence.
3
Analyze the hypothetical argument
Sanusi makes a hypothetical concession to argue that even if Ahmad said such a thing, it would be dialectical (taslim jadali), not real belief.
This is a powerful rhetorical move.
4
Learn the principle about taqlid in creed
Sanusi concludes that taqlid in sound creed is not beneficial, so how much more unacceptable is taqlid in something proven corrupt by decisive proof and consensus?

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal believed in a direction for Allah because his followers in fiqh claim so.
Correction: Imam Ahmad's creed is pure and based on the way of Ahl al-Sunna, and his debates show his opposition to such beliefs. Moreover, even if he had hypothetically entertained it dialectically, it would not be valid to follow him due to decisive proof against it.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, why would it be invalid to follow Imam Ahmad in the belief in direction even if he had stated it?
A) Because Ahmad later retracted it.
B) Because taqlid in creed is not beneficial even in sound matters, so how can it be in a matter proven corrupt by decisive proof and consensus?
C) Because the Hashwiyya misinterpret his words.
D) Because Ahmad never made such a statement.

Key Takeaway
Even if an imam were hypothetically to state a corrupt belief, following him in it is invalid because decisive proof and consensus have already established its falsehood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever clung to a belief about Allah simply because a respected scholar or teacher held it, without verifying it against decisive evidence from the Quran, Sunnah, and sound reason? What would it take for you to let go of that if proof showed it false?
?
When you learn a matter of creed, do you accept it purely based on the authority of an imam or do you seek to understand the proof? This lesson says even a great imam's words cannot be followed if they contradict decisive proof. How ready are you to examine your own beliefs even if they come from someone you deeply admire?
?
If you discovered that a belief you inherited from your family or community was actually a corrupt innovation rejected by consensus and proof, would you have the courage to abandon it despite the social pressure? What is stopping you from doing that examination right now?

Dismissal of Defamatory Writings Against Ibn Abi Zayd
Sanusi declares defamatory writings corrupt and dismisses them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Sanusi dismisses as corrupt any writings that attribute the belief in direction to Ibn Abi Zayd, Ibn 'Abd al-Barr, and other Salaf.

Core Idea
Defamations against early scholars are corrupt and unworthy.

In this brief but decisive passage, Sanusi addresses a specific slander found in some writings that accused respected early scholars of holding an anthropomorphic belief in direction for Allah. He declares such accusations to be corrupt and completely disregarded. This lesson clarifies the author's stance and its importance in protecting the legacy of the Salaf.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic sentence and its English translation to grasp the directness of Sanusi's statement.
Notice the strong language: 'fāsid' (corrupt) and 'lā yultaftu ilayhi' (not to be paid attention to).
2
Identify the main claim being dismissed
Recognize that Sanusi is refuting writings that defame Ibn Abi Zayd, Ibn 'Abd al-Barr, and other Salaf by associating them with the belief in direction (jiha).
The phrase 'bi-hi' refers to the doctrine of direction.
3
Understand the significance
Reflect on why such a dismissal is important: it protects the orthodoxy of these early scholars and upholds divine transcendence.
This aligns with Ash'ari commitment to tanzih (transcendence).

Source Text

And what is found in some writings, of defamation of Shaykh Ibn Abi Zayd and Abu 'Amr ibn 'Abd al-Barr and some of the Salaf with it (i.e., with the doctrine of direction), is corrupt and not to be paid attention to.

This short passage dismisses any claims found in books that associate Ibn Abi Zayd and Ibn 'Abd al-Barr with the belief in direction (jiha). The author declares such claims to be corrupt (fāsid) and unworthy of consideration, thereby protecting the reputation of these early scholars from false attribution.

Refutation of the Christian Doctrine of Three Hypostases
Sanusi refutes the Christian claim of three hypostases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Christian claim of three hypostases is rationally impossible according to Sanusi, and how it violates divine simplicity and unity.

Core Idea
The Christian trinity contradicts both reason and divine transcendence.

Sanusi now turns to a specific theological error: the Christian doctrine of three hypostases (aqānīm). Having established the unity and transcendence of God, he exposes the logical contradictions in the claim that God is composed of three distinct principles. This passage demonstrates how kalam reasoning applies to refute false doctrines.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Pay attention to the strong opening word 'بطلان' (refutation).
2
Identify the Christian claim
The passage states that Christians assert three hypostases as principles for the existence of the world and for God. Find how Sanusi describes this.
3
List the contradictions Sanusi highlights
Sanusi points out several contradictions: 1) God would be composed from these hypostases, 2) Hypostases are attributes yet called gods, 3) They claim the three are one God, combining unity and multiplicity, 4) The essence is composed of mere states or mental considerations.
Notice that each contradiction builds on the previous one.
4
Understand the final argument
Sanusi concludes that the hypostases, being mere states or mental aspects, cannot constitute a real entity. Ask yourself why this is a strong refutation.
This connects back to the lesson on attributes and states (ahwal).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بطلان قول النصارى في إثباتِ الأقانيم الثلاثةِ وبهذا تعرفُ استحالة ما قالته النصارى - أهلَكَهمُ اللهُ تعالى - مِنَ الأقانيم الثلاثةِ؛ أي : الأصول الثلاثة لوجود العالم لحدوثه عنها. وهي أصول لوجودِ الإله؛ لتركَّبه منها عندَهم، تعالى الله علواً كبيراً، وهي أقنوم الوجودِ، وأقنوم العلم، وأقنوم الحياة، وحكمهم عليها بأنَّها آلهةٌ ثلاثةٌ معَ أنَّها صفات، ثم قالوا مع ذلك : إنَّ مجموع الثلاثة إله واحدٌ، فجمعوا بين نقيضين؛ وحدةٍ وكثرة، وجعلوا الذات تتركَّبُ مِنْ مُجرَّدِ أحوال لا وجود لها، أو وجوه واعتبارات لا تُوجَدُ إلا في الأذهان ! وذلكَ غيرُ معقول لعاقل .
Refutation of the Christians' claim of establishing the three hypostases. And by this you know the impossibility of what the Christians—may God destroy them—said about the three hypostases, i.e., the three principles of the existence of the world due to its origination from them. And they are principles for the existence of God, because according to them He is composed from them—exalted is God greatly above that—and they are the hypostasis of existence, the hypostasis of knowledge, and the hypostasis of life. And their judgment that they are three gods despite being attributes, then they say along with that: the sum of the three is one God, so they combined two opposites: unity and multiplicity. And they made the essence composed of mere states that have no existence, or aspects and considerations that exist only in minds! And that is not rationally conceivable for any rational person.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage is a refutation (būṭlān) of the Christian doctrine of three hypostases (aqānīm). The author begins by stating that from the preceding arguments one can recognize the impossibility of the Christians' claim. They assert three hypostases, which they interpret as the three principles from which the world originated, as they believe the world is originated from them. They also claim these are principles for the existence of God because, in their view, God is composed from them. The author exclaims that God is far exalted above this. The three hypostases are defined as the hypostasis of existence, the hypostasis of knowledge, and the hypostasis of life. The Christians then judge these three to be gods, despite the fact that they are attributes (which cannot be independent). Moreover, they claim that the sum of the three is one God, thereby combining two opposites: unity and multiplicity. Furthermore, they make the divine essence composed of mere states (aḥwāl) that have no external existence, or aspects and considerations that exist only in the mind. The author concludes that this is rationally inconceivable for any rational person.

Key Terms
أقنوم (hypostasis)
أصول (principles)
آلهة (gods)
صفات (attributes)
وحدة وكثرة (unity and multiplicity)
أحوال (states)
وجوه واعتبارات (aspects and considerations)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the Christian trinity is a coherent concept that can be rationally defended.
Correction: Sanusi demonstrates that the doctrine of three hypostases leads to multiple logical contradictions: composition in God, calling attributes gods, and the impossibility of combining unity and multiplicity in a single essence.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what logical contradiction do the Christians commit in their doctrine of three hypostases?
A) They claim three gods are one god.
B) They say attributes are not divine.
C) They deny the existence of God.
D) They believe God is simple without composition.

Key Takeaway
Sanusi refutes the Christian hypostases by showing they involve composition of God, attributes as gods, and the impossible combination of unity and multiplicity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever accepted a belief about God that, upon honest reflection, contains a logical contradiction? What would it take for you to reject it, even if it is widely accepted?
?
Sanusi calls the Christians to task for making God composed of attributes as if they are separate. Do you ever treat God's attributes as if they are distinct 'parts' in your mind? How can you ensure your understanding of God remains transcendent?
?
The passage says the Christian view is 'not rationally conceivable for any rational person.' Are there any beliefs you hold that, if examined closely, are also rationally inconceivable? What will you do about it?

The Logical Contradiction of the Trinity
Sanusi refutes the Christian Trinity as self-contradictory.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical contradictions in the Christian doctrine of the Trinity as identified by Sanusi.

Core Idea
The Trinity combines unity and multiplicity, which is impossible for the divine.

Sanusi now turns to refute a major false doctrine: the Christian Trinity. He shows that the so-called 'three hypostases' are contradictory both in claiming three gods and one God, and in reducing the divine essence to mental constructs. This passage is a clear application of the rational principles he has established.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Christian claims
Read the passage and list the three hypostases (existence, knowledge, life) and what the Christians claim about them.
Sanusi uses the term 'أقنوم' for hypostasis.
2
Spot the contradictions
Notice how Sanusi highlights that they call these hypostases 'gods' and 'attributes' simultaneously, and then claim they are one God.
This combines unity and multiplicity.
3
Understand the final criticism
Sanusi points out that the hypostases are mere mental constructs. Ask yourself why this is impossible according to earlier lessons.
Mental constructs have no real existence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبهذا تعرفُ استحالة ما قالته النصارى - أهلَكَهمُ اللهُ تعالى - مِنَ الأقانيم الثلاثةِ ؛ أي : الأصول الثلاثة لوجود العالم لحدوثه عنها . وهي عن ذلك أصول لوجودِ الإله ؛ لتركَّبه منها عندَهم ، تعالى الله علواً كبيراً ، وهي أقنوم الوجودِ ، وأقنوم العلم ، وأقنوم الحياة ، وحكمهم عليها بأنَّها آلهةٌ ثلاثةٌ معَ أنَّها صفات ، ثم قالوا مع ذلك : إنَّ مجموع الثلاثة إله واحدٌ ، فجمعوا بين نقيضين ؛ وحدةٍ وكثرة ، وجعلوا الذات تتركَّبُ مِنْ مُجرَّدِ أحوال لا وجود لها ، أو وجوه واعتبارات لا تُوجَدُ إلا في الأذهان ! وذلكَ غيرُ معقول لعاقل .
And by this you know the impossibility of what the Christians—may God Almighty destroy them—said of the three hypostases; that is, the three principles of the existence of the world due to its origination from them. And they are, concerning that, principles of the existence of the deity because He is composed of them according to them—exalted is God greatly. They are the hypostasis of existence, the hypostasis of knowledge, and the hypostasis of life. And they judged them as three gods while they are attributes. Then they said additionally that the sum of the three is one God, so they combined two opposites: unity and multiplicity. And they made the Essence composed of mere states that have no existence, or aspects and considerations that exist only in minds! That is not comprehensible to any rational person.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage refutes the Christian Trinity. It first establishes that the three hypostases (existence, knowledge, life) are, according to the Christians, principles for the existence of the world and also for the existence of God (since God is composed of them). Then it points out the contradiction: they call these hypostases three gods while they are actually attributes. Then they claim the sum is one God, combining unity and multiplicity. Moreover, they make the divine essence composed of mere states (aḥwāl) or mental considerations, which is impossible. Thus their doctrine is irrational.

Key Terms
أقنوم
ألوهية
صفات
نقيضين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Trinity involves three distinct real persons that are somehow one God without contradiction.
Correction: Sanusi shows that this is impossible because it combines unity and multiplicity, and reduces attributes to mental constructs.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is the contradiction in the Christian Trinity?
A) They claim three gods but also one God.
B) They deny attributes.
C) They say Jesus is God.
D) They reject the Word.

Key Takeaway
The Christian doctrine of the Trinity is logically impossible because it combines unity and multiplicity and treats divine attributes as separate entities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The passage says the Trinity is 'not comprehensible to any rational person.' Is there any belief you hold about Allah that, if examined rationally, would also be contradictory? Are you willing to test your beliefs against logic and revelation, even if it is uncomfortable?
?
Sanusi's refutation is sharp ('may God destroy them'). This firmness in defending tawheed challenges a culture of 'all paths lead to God.' Are you willing to call false beliefs about Allah what they are, even when it is socially costly? What is one area where you have softened the truth about tawheed?

Sanusi's Refutation of the Union of the Word with Jesus
Sanusi refutes three interpretations of the union of the Word with Jesus' body.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three interpretations of the union of the Word with Jesus and why each is rationally impossible according to Sanusi.

Core Idea
Every interpretation of the union of the Word with Jesus leads to logical absurdity.

Sanusi continues his critique of Christian theology by examining the claim that the Word (hypostasis of knowledge) united with Jesus' body. Christians differed on how this union occurred, and Sanusi presents three common interpretations—accident/subsistence, mixture, and impression—and refutes each in turn. This passage shows how careful reasoning exposes the irrationality of such doctrines.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the three interpretations
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice that after stating the claim, Sanusi lists three different ways Christians explained the union. Mark each one.
The interpretations are: subsistence as accident, mixture, and impression.
2
Examine the refutation of each interpretation
For each interpretation, Sanusi provides a reason why it is impossible. For the first, he notes that one meaning cannot subsist in two essences. For the second, mixture is an attribute of bodies. For the third, only a likeness is impressed, not the thing itself.
Think about why each refutation is effective against the Christian claim.
3
Reflect on the final verdict
Read the concluding lines where Sanusi dismisses the entire doctrine as irrational and the Christians as the worst of sects. Consider how this fits into his broader theological project.
Sanusi's tone is severe, reflecting the stakes of the debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم زعموا أيضاً: أنَّ أقنوم العلم منها ـ ويُسمَّى : الكلمة - اتحد بناسوت عيسى ؛ أي : جسدِهِ ، ومِنْ ثَمَّ كَانَ إلها عندهم . واختلفوا في معنى اتحادِ الكلمة بهِ : فمنهم مَنْ فسَّرَ قيامَ الكلمةِ بهِ كما يقومُ العَرَضُ بالجوهر : وهذا يُوجِبُ مفارقته لذات الجوهر الذي هو عندهم مجموع الأقانيم الثلاثة ، وهم يقولون : اتَّحد بناسوت عيسى مِنْ غيرِ أنْ يفارق ذاتَ الجوهر ، ومن المعلوم ضرورةً : أنَّ المعنى الواحد لا يقوم بذاتين . ومنهم مَنْ فسَّرَ هذا الاتحاد بالاختلاطِ والمزج : كاختلاط الخمرِ والماء ونحوهما مِنَ المائعاتِ ، وكيفَ يُعقَلُ الاختلاط الذي هو مِنْ صفاتِ الأجسام في الكلمة التي هي معنى مِنَ المعاني ، بل هي عندهم حال وخاصية للذات الأزلية ؟! ومنهم مَنْ فَسَّرَهُ بالانطباع : كانطباع صورة النقشِ في الشمع ومعلوم أن النقش لم يحصل فيما طُبعَ فيه ، وإنَّما حصل فيه مثاله . ولنقتصر على هذا القدْرِ مِنْ بيانِ فضائحهم ؛ فإِنَّ التطويل غيرُ لائق بالغرضِ مِنَ هذا المختصرِ ، والقومُ قد انكشف عوارُهم ، ومباديه تدلُّ على مناهيه ، ومذهبهم غير معقول ، وهم أخسُّ الفِرَقِ كلها وأرذلها أفهاماً ، وإدراك الحقائق على مثلهم عسير .
Then they also claimed that the hypostasis of knowledge among them—called the Word—united with the humanity of Jesus, i.e., his body, and therefore he was a god according to them. And they differed concerning the meaning of the union of the Word with him: some of them interpreted the subsistence of the Word in him as an accident subsists in a substance: this necessitates its separation from the essence of the substance which is, according to them, the sum of the three hypostases. And they say: it united with the humanity of Jesus without separating from the essence of the substance. And it is known necessarily that one meaning does not subsist in two essences. Some of them interpreted this union as mixture and blending: like the mixing of wine and water and similar liquids. How can mixture, which is an attribute of bodies, be conceived in the Word, which is a meaning among meanings—rather it is, according to them, a state and property of the eternal Essence?! And some of them interpreted it as impression: like the impression of the image of an engraving in wax. And it is known that the engraving did not occur in that which it was impressed upon, but rather its likeness occurred in it. And we will limit ourselves to this amount of exposing their scandals; for prolongation is not fitting the purpose of this compendium, and the people have been exposed in their defects, and their principles indicate their outcomes, and their doctrine is not rational, and they are the vilest of all sects and the most degraded in understanding, and perceiving realities upon their like is difficult.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage refutes the Christian claim that the Word (hypostasis of knowledge) united with Jesus' body. It presents three interpretations of this union and refutes each. The first interpretation: the Word subsists in Jesus as an accident in a substance. This would require the Word to separate from the divine essence (the sum of hypostases), but they claim union without separation. Also, one meaning cannot subsist in two essences. The second: mixture, like wine and water. But mixture is an attribute of bodies, whereas the Word is a mental meaning or state, not a body. The third: impression, like an engraving in wax. But the engraving itself is not in the wax, only its likeness. Thus all interpretations fail. The author concludes that their doctrine is irrational and they are the worst of sects.

Key Terms
اتحاد
ناسوت
الكلمة
عرض
جوهر
اختلاط
انطباع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The union of the Word with Jesus could be a literal physical union like mixing or impression.
Correction: Sanusi shows that each interpretation leads to logical contradictions: accident-subsistence requires separation from the essence, mixture is for bodies only, and impression only transfers a likeness, not the thing itself.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the interpretations of the union of the Word with Jesus according to Sanusi?
A) Subsistence like an accident.
B) Mixture like wine and water.
C) Incarnation like a spirit in a body.
D) Impression like an engraving in wax.

Key Takeaway
The Christian doctrine of the union of the Word with Jesus is rationally indefensible because each attempted interpretation leads to contradiction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a claim that contradicts reason, do you automatically reject it or do you sometimes hold onto it out of habit? What in your own faith might you be believing without rational scrutiny?
?
Sanusi shows that even well-intentioned interpretations of divine unity can lead to absurdity. Have you ever rationalized a belief to make it more 'acceptable' while ignoring its logical inconsistencies?
?
The passage ends by calling the Christians 'the vilest of sects' for their irrationality. How does this challenge you to be both a defender of truth and a person of compassion? Are you willing to call out falsehood clearly, even if it offends?
