Refutation of the Qadariyya: No Created Power Invents Actions
Sanusi refutes the Qadariyya who assert that the slave's created power invents his actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Qadariyya claim that created power invents actions is a contradiction of reason, revelation, and consensus.

Core Idea
No created power can invent actions; only Allah creates all things.

The Qadariyya made a subtle error. They agreed with Ahl al-Sunna that a created power exists in the slave for voluntary actions, but then claimed that this power actually invents the action. Sanusi refutes them with two decisive arguments: rational necessity and textual consensus. Let's see how.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Qadariyya doctrine
Read the passage to identify what the Qadariyya affirm and how they differ from Ahl al-Sunna.
Both groups agree on the existence of created power, but differ on its effect.
2
Identify their error
Note that the Qadariyya claim the created power invents the action at the slave's will.
3
Examine the rational refutation
Reason demands that Allah alone originates all things directly; no creature can invent independently.
This is a matter of tawheed al-khaliq.
4
Examine the scriptural refutation
The Quran, Sunna, and consensus affirm that no creator but Allah exists and nothing happens outside His will.
Qadariyya contradict the very sources they claim to follow.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وثانيهما مذهب القدرية القائلين بثبوت قدرة حادثة للعبد مع الأفعال الاختيارية كما يقول أهل السنة لكن خالفوهم بأن قالوا تلك القدرة الحادثة التي خلق الله تعالى في العبد هي التي بها يخترع العبد أفعاله على وفق ما يشاء ولا شك أن هؤلاء مبتدعة مناقضون لما دل عليه العقل من وجوب انفراده تعالى باختراع جميع الكائنات ابتداء بلا واسطة على وفق ما شاء جل وعز ومناقضون أيضا لما دل عليه الكتاب والسنة ووقع عليه إجماع سلف الأمة من أن لا خالق إلا الله تعالى وأن ما شاء الله سبحانه كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن
And the second (school) is the school of the Qadariyya, who affirm the existence of an originated power for the slave with voluntary actions, just as the Ahl al-Sunna say. But they contradicted them by saying that this originated power which God Most High created in the slave is that by which the slave invents his actions according to what he wills. And there is no doubt that these are innovators, contradicting what reason has indicated: the necessity of His exclusivity, Most High, in inventing all originated things initially without mediation according to what He wills, Majestic and Exalted. And they also contradict what the Book and the Sunna have indicated, upon which the consensus of the predecessors of the community rests: that there is no creator but God Most High, and that what God wills occurs, and what He does not will does not occur.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage refutes the Qadariyya (those who affirm free will). It begins by noting that both the Qadariyya and the Ahl al-Sunna agree that an originated power (قدرة حادثة) exists in the slave for voluntary actions. However, the Qadariyya err by claiming that this power actually creates and invents the action according to the slave's desire. The author declares them innovators for two reasons: First, they contradict reason, which necessitates that God alone originates all things directly without any intermediary. Second, they contradict revelation (the Quran and Sunna) and the consensus of the Salaf, which affirm that there is no creator but God and that God's will is sovereign—whatever He wills happens, and what He does not will does not happen. Thus, the Qadariyya attribute creative power to the slave, which is shirk and undermines tawheed.

Key Terms

قدرة حادثة
اختراع
مبتدعة
إجماع سلف الأمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Qadariyya are similar to Ahl al-Sunna because both affirm a created power to act.
Correction: The Qadariyya attribute creative effect to that power, whereas Ahl al-Sunna deny any creative effect and hold that Allah alone creates all actions, including the slave's acts.

Checkpoint
What do the Qadariyya claim about the originated power (al-qudra al-ḥāditha) in the slave?
A) It is ineffective.
B) It is the means by which the slave invents his own actions.
C) It is identical to God's power.
D) It only applies to involuntary actions.

Key Takeaway
The Qadariyya deviate by attributing creative power to the slave's created ability, contradicting the core Islamic belief that only Allah creates.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
This lesson declares that attributing creative power to anyone besides Allah is innovation and contradiction of reason. Is there any area of your life where you act as if your will is independent of Allah's? What concrete step will you take today to submit your will to His?
?

The Sunni Middle Path: Compelled in a Mold of Choice
Sanusi presents the Sunni position on human actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position on human actions as a middle path between Jabriyya and Qadariyya, affirming both divine omnipotence and human responsibility.

Core Idea
The slave is compelled in the mold of choice.

Sanusi now presents the Sunni middle path that reconciles the demands of rational truth and religious law. He shows how the Sunni school avoids both extreme determinism and the claim that humans create their own actions. This passage introduces the famous formulation that the slave is 'compelled in a mold of choice', which is the key to understanding Islamic theology of human agency.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then the literal translation. Notice how Sanusi contrasts the Sunni position with the two deviant sects.
The passage ends abruptly at 'وإنما هو' but forms a complete thought.
2
Identify the two errors avoided
The passage mentions two groups: the Jabriyya (extreme determinists) and the Qadariyya (who claim humans create their own acts). Understand how the Sunni school avoids each.
The key is that the Sunni school combines reality (ḥaqīqa) and law (sharīʿa).
3
Understand 'accompaniment without effect'
The passage states that the originated power (qudra ḥāditha) accompanies voluntary acts but has no effect. Grasp this nuanced concept: the power is present but does not cause the act.
This distinguishes from both Jabriyya (who deny any human power) and Qadariyya (who claim human power creates the act).
4
Grasp the summary formulation
The passage concludes with the famous phrase: 'the capable slave is compelled in a mold of choice'. Reflect on how this balances divine omnipotence and human accountability.
The slave is compelled in creation (no effective power) but ascribed choice because his voluntary actions are accompanied by capacity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما مذهب أهل الحق رضي الله تعالى عنهم فقد جمع بين الحقيقة والشريعة وسلم بفضل الله تعالى من بدعة الفريقين لأنهم جانبوا الجبرية بتقسيم الأفعال إلى قسمين اختيارية واضطرارية وأن الأولى مقدورة للعبد بمعنى أن له قدرة حادثة تقارن تلك الأفعال الاختيارية وتتعلق بها من غير تأثير وهذه الأفعال هي التي في وسع المكلف عادة وبها وقع التكليف على حسب ما دل عليه الشرع وجانبوا القدرية لكونهم لم يجعلوا لتلك القدرة الحادثة تأثيرا ألبتة في أثر ما عموما بل العبد عندهم وقدرته الحادثة ومقدورها الكل مخلوق الله تعالى بلا واسطة ولا شريك أصلا على حسب ما دلت عليه الحقيقة العقلية وحاصل العبد القادر عند أهل الحق أنه مجبور في قالب مختار مجبور من حيث إنه لا أثر له البتة في أثر ما عموما وإنما هو
As for the school of the people of truth—may God be pleased with them—it combines reality and law, and by God's grace is saved from the innovation of the two groups. For they avoided the Jabriyya by dividing actions into two categories: voluntary and involuntary, and that the first is within the capacity of the slave in the sense that he has an originated power that accompanies those voluntary actions and is related to them without effect. And these actions are those within the usual capacity of the obligated person, and by them obligation occurs according to what the Law indicates. And they avoided the Qadariyya because they did not assign any effect at all to that originated power in any effect whatsoever generally; rather, the slave, his originated power, and its object are all created by God Most High without mediation and without any partner at all, according to what rational reality indicates. And the upshot of the capable slave according to the people of truth is that he is compelled in a mold of choice: compelled in that he has no effect at all in any effect whatsoever generally, and he is merely...
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage presents the Sunni position (مذهب أهل الحق) as a middle path that combines intellectual reality (الحقيقة) and religious law (الشريعة). The Sunni school avoids the two extremes. First, they avoid the Jabriyya by dividing actions into voluntary and involuntary. They affirm that voluntary actions are within the slave's power (مقدورة للعبد) in the sense that the slave has an originated power (قدرة حادثة) that accompanies these actions, but this power has no effect (لا تأثير). These voluntary actions are the basis of obligation because they are within the slave's usual capacity (وسع عادي). Second, they avoid the Qadariyya by denying any effect (تأثير) to the originated power; the slave, his power, and the act are all directly created by God alone, without any partner. The final summary statement is famous: 'the capable slave is compelled in a mold of choice' (العبد مجبور في قالب مختار). This means that from the perspective of God's sole creative agency, the slave is compelled—he has no effect on any event. But from the perspective of the law, he is attributed with choice because his actions are accompanied by his created power and capacity, making him accountable. The passage ends with 'and he is merely...' (وإنما هو), implying his being is only a locus for God's action.

Key Terms
مذهب أهل الحق
حقيقة
شريعة
اختيارية
اضطرارية
قدرة حادثة
لا تأثير
مجبر في قالب مختار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the Sunni position is contradictory (saying both compelled and free), but it is a nuanced reconciliation.
Correction: Compelled in creation (no effective power) yet free by accompaniment of power and legal capacity.

Checkpoint
According to the Sunni position, how does the originated power (al-qudra al-ḥāditha) relate to the voluntary act?
A) It creates the act.
B) It accompanies the act without any effect.
C) It is the act itself.
D) It compels the act.

Key Takeaway
The Sunni position holds that humans have no effective power over their actions but are accountable because their actions are accompanied by a divinely created capacity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you truly feel that your action was created by God yet you are responsible? Or do you tend to blame your nature or circumstances (like the Jabriyya) or feel that you alone caused it (like the Qadariyya)? This lesson demands you examine which tendency actually governs your heart.
?
The passage says the slave is 'compelled in a mold of choice'. How does this shape your daily struggle with obedience and sin? Do you find yourself ignoring your own responsibility because 'everything is from God'? Or do you despair because you think you alone must change? Which extreme do you fall into, and what would it mean to truly hold both truths together?
?
If you really believed that your power has no effect—that God is the sole creator of your acts—would you still strive in worship? This teaching is meant to deepen reliance on God, not paralyze action. Reflect: does your understanding of predestination increase your hope in God's mercy or does it make you lethargic? Commit to one concrete change in your attitude toward effort and reliance after this lesson.

Refutation of Innovators Denying Divine Omnipotence
Sanusi refutes two innovating groups using reason and revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi refutes innovating groups by showing that they contradict both rational necessity and revealed texts regarding God's exclusive creation and will.

Core Idea
Reason and revelation agree: nothing exists without Allah's will.

Sanusi here issues a decisive refutation against those who deny that all creation is directly from God. He shows that such views contradict not only rational necessity but also the explicit teachings of the Quran, Sunnah, and the consensus of the early Muslim community. This lesson will help you see how he uses both sources of knowledge to establish the correct position.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the full passage once without pausing. Then read the translation. Notice the two main parts: one about reason and one about revelation.
The passage is a single sentence with two parallel clauses.
2
Identify the two sources of evidence
Sanusi uses reason (العقل) and revelation (الكتاب والسنة والإجماع). Find where each is mentioned.
3
Understand the rational proof
Reason necessitates that God alone is the creator of all things initially, without any intermediary, according to His will.
Key terms: وجوب انفراد, اختراع, ابتداء, بلا واسطة.
4
Understand the revelatory proof
The Quran, Sunnah, and consensus affirm that there is no creator but Allah, and what He wills happens, and what He does not will does not happen.
Key terms: إجماع سلف الأمّة.
5
Reflect on the innovation charge
Sanusi declares these groups to be innovators because they contradict both sources. Consider why innovation is serious in Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا شكّ أنَّ هؤلاء مبتدعةٌ ، مناقضونَ لما دلَّ عليهِ العقلُ ؛ مِنْ وجوب انفرادِهِ تعالى باختراع جميع الكائناتِ ابتداءً بلا واسطة على وَفْقِ ما شاءَ جلَّ وعزَّ ، ومناقضونَ أيضاً لما دلّ عليه الكتاب والسنَّةُ ووقع عليه إجماع سلفِ الأمَّةِ ؛ مِنْ أنْ لا خالق إلا الله تعالى ، وأَنَّ ما شاء الله سبحانهُ كانَ ، وما لم يشأ لم يكن
And there is no doubt that these are innovators, contradicting what reason indicates: the necessity of His exclusivity, may He be exalted, in inventing all created things initially without intermediary according to what He willed, Glorious and Exalted, and contradicting also what the Book and Sunnah indicate and what the consensus of the predecessors of the community fell upon: that there is no creator except God Almighty, and that what God willed, may He be glorified, comes to be, and what He did not will does not come to be.
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of two innovating groups (Jabriyya and Qadariyya, though not named here) by showing they contradict both reason and revelation. Sanusi begins by asserting without doubt that these groups are innovators. He provides two proofs: first, reason demands that God alone is the exclusive creator of all things initially without any intermediary, according to His will. Second, revelation (the Book and Sunnah) and the consensus of the Salaf affirm that there is no creator but Allah, and that what He wills happens and what He does not will does not happen. Thus the innovators oppose both sources.

Key Terms
مبتدعة
وجوب انفراد
اختراع
ابتداء
بلا واسطة
إجماع سلف الأمّة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that human actions are outside God's will or that creation occurs through intermediaries independent of God.
Correction: This passage affirms that all creation is directly from God without intermediary, and nothing occurs without His will.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what do the innovators contradict?
A) Only reason
B) Only revelation
C) Both reason and revelation
D) Neither reason nor revelation

Key Takeaway
Sanusi refutes innovators by showing they contradict both rational necessity and revealed texts regarding God's exclusive creation and will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that nothing happens in your life—whether a success, a failure, a chance meeting, or a sudden tragedy—without Allah's will? When something you dislike occurs, do you accept it as from Him, or do you inwardly attribute it to chance or people's choices alone?
?
Have you ever caught yourself thinking that your own efforts or decisions are independent of Allah's creative power? How does this passage confront that assumption, and what would it mean for you to live as if every moment is directly created by Him?
?
If you were to fully internalize that Allah alone invents all things 'without intermediary' (bila wasita), how would your reliance on created means—wealth, status, medicine, personal ability—change? Would you still worry, or would your trust shift entirely to the Creator?

The Qadariyyah as the Magians of this Ummah
Sanusi explains the comparison of the Qadariyyah to the Magians and its basis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Qadariyyah (Mu'tazila) are likened to the Magians and the theological basis for this comparison.

Core Idea
Denying Allah's role in evil aligns one with dualist theology.

Sanusi cites a famous hadith comparing the Qadariyyah to the Magians. This comparison is not arbitrary—it rests on a deep theological parallel: both groups separate the origin of good and evil. In this passage, Sanusi unpacks the meaning of the hadith and explains why the Mu'tazila are the intended referents.

Guided Path
1
Clarify the phrase 'we do not see an effect'
Sanusi first notes that 'see' here means opinion, not physical sight. He is distinguishing between the two meanings to avoid misunderstanding.
This is a minor lexical point that sets the stage for the main topic.
2
Examine the hadith and its implications
Read the hadith from Ibn 'Umar and note the strong language: visiting the sick and funerals are prohibited. Consider what this implies about the gravity of the Qadariyyah's error.
The hadith also mentions being cursed by seventy prophets.
3
Understand the basis of the comparison
Sanusi explains that both Magians and Qadariyyah avoid attributing evil to a single divine source. Magians posit two creators; Qadariyyah ascribe evil to Iblis or human actions.
This reveals that the Mu'tazila, who deny that Allah creates evil acts, are the group being criticized.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وإنْ لم نرَ لها تأثيراً ( هو مِنَ الرأي ، لا مِنَ الرؤيةِ ؛ أي : ولم يكنْ رأينا فيها أنَّ لها تأثيراً . وقوله : ( مجوس هذهِ الأُمَّةِ ( أشار بهذا إلى ما صح عنِ ابنِ عمرَ رضيَ الله عنهما أنَّهُ قالَ : ( القدريَّةُ مجوس هذهِ الأُمَّةِ ؛ إِنْ مرضوا فلا تعودوهم ، وإن ماتوا فلا تشهدُوهم ) ، وقد رواه أبو داود حديثاً وقد رُوِيَ : ( أَنَّهُمْ لُعِنُوا عَلَى لِسَانِ سَبْعِينَ نَبِيَّاً ( وقد روى مسلم في صحيحِهِ تبرؤ عبدِ اللهِ بنِ عمرَ رضيَ اللهُ تعالى عنهما منهم ، والحكم عليهم بما يقتضي كفرَهم عندَهُ ووجه تشبيههم بالمجوس : أنَّ المجوس جعلوا للخير فاعلاً وللشر فاعلاً ، والقدرية أيضاً منعوا نسبة الشرِّ إلى الله تعالى وأضافوه إلى إبليس تسباً وسَعْياً ، وإلى العبادِ مباشرةً وفِعلاً ، وهذه المناسبة التي بين المعتزلة والمجوس تُعيَّنُ أنَّهمُ المرادون بالقدرية في الحديثِ
His saying 'And if we do not see an effect for it' — it is from opinion (ra'y), not from vision (ru'yah); meaning: we did not hold the opinion that it has an effect. And his saying 'the Magians of this ummah' — he pointed by this to what is authentically reported from Ibn 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with them both, that he said: 'The Qadariyyah are the Magians of this ummah; if they become sick, do not visit them, and if they die, do not attend their funerals.' Abu Dawud reported it as a hadith, and it has been reported: 'They were cursed on the tongue of seventy prophets.' Muslim reported in his Sahih the disavowal of 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with them both, from them (the Qadariyyah), and the judgment against them as implying their disbelief according to him. And the aspect of likening them to the Magians is that the Magians made for good a doer and for evil a doer, and the Qadariyyah also prevented attributing evil to Allah Almighty and ascribed it to Iblis as attribution and seeking, and to the servants as direct action and doing. And this connection between the Mu'tazila and the Magians specifies that they are the ones intended by 'Qadariyyah' in the hadith.
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory commentary on two phrases in the original text. The author first clarifies the meaning of 'we do not see an effect for it' — explaining that it refers to opinion (ra'y) rather than physical sight (ru'yah). Then he explains the phrase 'the Magians of this ummah' by citing the well-known hadith of Ibn 'Umar that the Qadariyyah (those who deny predestination) are the Magians of this community, and the hadith includes instructions to avoid them when sick or dead. He also mentions that they were cursed on the tongues of seventy prophets. He notes that Muslim reported Ibn 'Umar's disavowal of them and a judgment implying their disbelief. Then he explains the reason for the comparison: just as the Magians posit two separate creators for good and evil, the Qadariyyah also deny the attribution of evil to Allah and instead ascribe it to Iblis or to human actions directly. This commonality shows that the Mu'tazila (the rationalist sect) are the intended referents of 'Qadariyyah' in the hadith.

Key Terms
القدرية (Qadariyyah)
مجوس (Magians)
القدرة الحادثة (created power)
المعتزلة (Mu'tazila)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith about the Qadariyyah being the Magians of this ummah automatically excommunicates all Qadariyyah from Islam.
Correction: The hadith indicates a severe judgment, but Sanusi notes that Ibn 'Umar's judgment implies disbelief according to him (at his own view), not necessarily a universal ruling. The comparison is primarily about theological similarity, not automatic excommunication.

Checkpoint
What is the basis for likening the Qadariyyah (Mu'tazila) to the Magians?
A) Both believe in two gods
B) Both deny the attribution of evil to Allah or ascribe it to a separate source
C) Both reject all prophets
D) Both practice fire worship

Key Takeaway
The Qadariyyah (Mu'tazila) are likened to the Magians because both assign good and evil to separate sources rather than attributing everything to Allah alone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experience pain or injustice, does your heart instinctively blame shaytan, another person, or circumstances rather than humbly accepting it from Allah? How can you train yourself to see all events—including evil—as part of Allah's decree without compromising His justice?
?
The Qadariyyah thought they were honoring Allah by not attributing evil to Him. But in reality, they denied His complete sovereignty. Is there any area of your life where you subtly 'protect' Allah's perfection by avoiding the full implications of His will—such as in suffering or moral evil? What would it mean for your faith to fully embrace that everything comes from Him?
?
This lesson warns that attributing evil to sources other than Allah can lead to a subtle dualism in your heart. Do you ever find yourself thinking of good as from Allah and evil as from elsewhere? How can you cultivate a heart that sees all things—good and apparent evil—as from Him alone, trusting in His wisdom and justice?

Defending Imam al-Haramayn's Orthodoxy
Defending al-Juwayni by citing Taftazani's denial and quoting al-Irshad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how scholars defended Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni) against the attribution of the philosophical view that human power causes actions, and how al-Taftazani's testimony confirms his orthodox Ash'ari position.

Core Idea
Al-Juwayni's own words disprove the false attribution of philosophical causality to him.

In this passage, the commentator vigorously defends Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni) from a serious accusation: that he held the same view as the philosophers regarding human power causing actions. He asserts that al-Juwayni's piety and knowledge make such a statement impossible, and if it were said, it was only for debate. To solidify the defense, he cites al-Taftazani's explicit denial and quotes al-Juwayni's own words from al-Irshad, which affirm that the originated power has no effect at all.

Guided Path
1
Read the defense and alleged statement
Begin by reading the passage from the beginning to the quote from al-Taftazani. Notice how the commentator expresses astonishment and then gives reasons for certainty that al-Juwayni never held the attributed view.
The attributed view is that human action occurs by the servant's own power and will obligatorily.
2
Identify Taftazani's testimony
Al-Taftazani first reports what is commonly written in books about al-Juwayni's school, then refutes it by quoting al-Juwayni's own words. Focus on the contrast between the attributed doctrine and the actual quote.
3
Analyze the key quote from al-Irshad
Al-Juwayni's quote states that the Salaf agreed that only Allah creates, and that the relation of an attribute to its object does not entail causal effect. Understand the example: knowledge of the known does not cause the known.
This is the core of the Ash'ari position on power.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage concludes that the originated power (qudra haditha) has no effect at all. Ask yourself: why is this significant for the debate on human free will and divine omnipotence?
This echoes the earlier discussion of causality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قلتُ : وإذا قالَ هذا في مقالة القاضي والأستاذ معَ خفتهما بالنسبة إلى ما نُقِلَ عن إمام الحرمين .. فكيف بتلك المقالة الشنيعة التي نُقِلَتْ عن الإمام ؟! ولا يرضى أن يقولَها مُوفَّقٌ ، ولا يُعرَفُ مثلُها أو قريب منها إلا عن الفلاسفة أهلكهم الله تعالى وأخلى منهم الأرض . والذي يُقطَعُ به لدينِ إمام الحرمين ، ووَرَعِهِ وغزارة علمه ، وفِرارِهِ مِنَ البدع وما يقرُبُ منها .. أنَّه لم يقل هذه المقالة ، وعلى تقدير أنْ يكونَ قالَها فيتعيَّنُ أنْ يكونَ قالَها على سبيل البحث والمناظرة كما سبق ، مع قطعِهِ ببطلانها . وقد أشار التفتازاني في « شرح المقاصدِ الدينيَّةِ » إلى عدمِ تحققِ صدور هذه المقالة عن الإمامِ ، ونصه المشهور فيما بين القومِ ( والمذكور في كتبهم : أنَّ مذهب إمام الحرمين أنَّ فعلَ العبدِ واقع بقدرته وإرادته إيجاباً كما هو رأي الحكماء ) ، قال : ( وهذا خلافُ ما صرَّحَ بهِ الإمامُ فيما وقعَ إلينا مِنْ كُتُبِهِ ؛ قالَ في « الإرشادِ » : « اتَّفَقَ أئمَّةُ السلفِ قبل ظهورِ البدع والأهواء على أنَّ الخالق هو الله تعالى ، ولا خالق سواه ، وأنَّ الحوادث كلَّها إِنَّما حدثَتْ بقدرةِ اللهِ تعالى مِنْ غيرِ فرق بينَ ما تتعلَّقُ قدرةُ العبدِ بهِ وبينَ ما لا تتعلَّقُ ؛ فإِنَّ تعلُّق الصفةِ بالشيء لا يستلزم تأثيرها فيه ؛ كالعلم بالمعلوم والإرادة بفعل الغيرِ ، فالقدرة الحادثة لا تُؤثر في مقدور ما أصلاً .
I say: If this is said regarding the statement of al-Qadi and al-Ustadh, despite their lightness relative to what was transmitted from Imam al-Haramayn, then how about that repugnant statement attributed to the Imam?! No rightly guided person would be pleased to say it, and its like or near it is not known except from the philosophers – may Allah destroy them and empty the earth of them. And what is conclusively affirmed regarding the religion of Imam al-Haramayn, his piety, his vast knowledge, and his flight from innovations and what approaches them – is that he did not say this statement. And if it is assumed that he said it, then it is necessary that he said it by way of research and debate as before, while being certain of its falsehood. And al-Taftazani in his 'Sharh al-Maqasid al-Diniyya' indicated the non-verification of this statement issuing from the Imam. His famous text among the people is: 'What is mentioned in their books – that the school of Imam al-Haramayn is that the action of the servant occurs by his own power and will obligatorily, as is the opinion of the philosophers.' He said: 'This contradicts what the Imam explicitly stated in what has reached us from his books. He said in al-Irshad: “The imams of the Salaf agreed – before the emergence of innovations and desires – that the Creator is Allah Almighty, and there is no creator other than Him, and that all events only occur by the power of Allah Almighty, with no difference between what the servant’s power is related to and what it is not related to. For the relation of an attribute to a thing does not entail its having effect in it, like knowledge of the known and will regarding the action of another. So the originated power has no effect at all in what is within its power.”'
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This passage continues the defense by focusing on the more serious statement attributed to Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni), namely that human action is by the servant's own power. The author (the commentator) begins by expressing astonishment: if such a defense is needed for the relatively milder statements of al-Qadi and al-Ustadh, then how much more for the repugnant statement attributed to al-Juwayni? He then asserts that it is certain, given al-Juwayni's religion, piety, vast knowledge, and avoidance of innovations, that he never said that. But even if he did, it must have been in a debate context, while he was certain of its falsehood. To bolster this, the author cites al-Taftazani from his 'Sharh al-Maqasid'. Al-Taftazani first reports what is commonly written in books: that al-Juwayni's doctrine is that the servant's action occurs by his own power and will obligatorily, like the philosophers. Then he refutes that by quoting al-Juwayni's own words from al-Irshad. In that quote, al-Juwayni affirms that the Salaf agreed that only Allah is the Creator, all events happen by Allah's power, and the relation of an attribute (like power) to its object does not imply causal effect. He gives examples: knowledge of the known does not cause the known, and will regarding another's action does not cause that action. Therefore, the originated power (al-qudra al-haditha) has no effect at all. This shows that al-Juwayni's actual position is orthodox Ash'arism, contrary to the attributed statement.

Key Terms
إمام الحرمين
القدرة الحادثة
التفتازاني
الإرشاد
الفلاسفة
البدعة
المقاصد الدينية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni) held that human actions are caused by the servant's own power and will, similar to the philosophers.
Correction: Al-Juwayni's own words from al-Irshad, as quoted by Taftazani, affirm that all events occur by Allah's power alone, and the originated power (al-qudra al-haditha) has no effect at all. The attributed statement is either false or was said in a debate context while being certain of its falsehood.

Checkpoint
According to al-Taftazani's quote from al-Juwayni's al-Irshad, why does the originated power have no effect?
A) Because it is not a real attribute.
B) Because the relation of an attribute to a thing does not entail its having effect in it.
C) Because the servant's will negates its effect.
D) Because Allah created it for testing only.

Key Takeaway
Al-Juwayni's own words in al-Irshad affirm that the originated power has no effect, confirming his orthodox Ash'ari stance against philosophical causality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever accepted an accusation against someone based on hearsay without first checking their own words? Will you commit to verifying before judging, especially regarding the scholars of Islam?
?
Al-Juwayni fled from innovations and what approaches them. What beliefs or practices in your life are near innovations that you need to distance yourself from? How will you start today?
?
The commentator says that no rightly guided person would be pleased to utter the repugnant statement. Are you pleased with any statement you make that contradicts the Salaf's understanding? What is one belief you hold that needs to be brought in line with their consensus?

Warning against False Attribution to Sunni Imams
Sanusi condemns false attribution to Sunni imams and exposes motives of innovators.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the danger of attributing false statements to Sunni imams and the motives behind such fabrications.

Core Idea
Fabricated statements attributed to Sunni imams are slander intended to cause fitna.

Sanusi begins by strongly condemning the practice of attributing causal efficacy to created power, calling it slander. He then reveals that innovators have deliberately inserted corrupt statements into the works of eminent imams like al-Ghazali, and even fabricated hadith, with malicious purposes. This lesson exposes those motives and sets the stage for understanding the proper methodology in creed.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note how Sanusi opens with a strong condemnation.
Notice the phrase 'la shakka fihi' (no doubt about it).
2
Identify the accusation
Sanusi accuses the 'human devils among the innovators' of inserting corrupt statements into the books of Sunni imams. Locate this accusation in the text.
3
Find the three motives
The passage mentions three motives for these fabrications: causing fitna, envy, and belittling the Sharia. Can you find them?
The third motive is connected to inserting fabricated hadith.
4
Reflect on the Quranic verse
Sanusi quotes Surah as-Saff:8. How does this verse reinforce his warning?
The verse assures that God's light will prevail despite their efforts.

وبالجملة : فتلطيخُ هؤلاء الأئمة الأعلامِ - رضيَ اللهُ تعالى عنهم ، ونفعنا بهم ، وجزاهم عن المسلمينَ أفضل الجزاء - بإسنادِ تأثير ما حقيقي للقدرة الحادثة .. افتراء وكذبٌ لا شكَ فيهِ وقد دَسَّتْ شياطينُ الإِنسِ مِنَ المبتدعة أقوالاً فاسدةً لا تصح عقلاً ولا نقلاً في كتب بعض أئمة السنَّةِ الأعلام ؛ كـ « إحياء الإمامِ الغزالي ) ونحوه ؛ بقصدِ الفتنة ، أو حسداً لتزهد الناسُ في الاقتداء بهم والعكوف على النظر فيما أودعوهُ مِنَ الجواهر النفيسة في تأليفهم ، التي يُعَدُّ التسديد لها مِنَ الكرامات الخارقة للعادة • بل دشوا كثيراً مِنْ ذلكَ في الأحاديثِ النبوية ، وتجاسروا على إدخال الأحاديث الموضوعةِ الكاذبة فيها ؛ لأغراض منها قصد الحطّ مِنْ شرفِ الشرعِ النفيس ، يُرِيدُونَ لِيُطْفِئُوا نُورَ اللَّهِ بِأَفْوَاهِهِمْ وَاللَّهُ مُتِمُّ نُورِهِ، وَلَوْ كَرِهَ الْكَفِرُونَ ﴾ [الصف : ۸] . وإِنَّما أطلتُ بذكْرِ هذا التنبيه ؛ لما رأيتُ ابتلاء المسلمين بكثير ممن ينقلُ هذه الأقوال الفاسدة ، ويُلبس عليهم بنسبتها إلى هؤلاء الأئمَّةِ الأعلامِ رضيَ اللهُ تعالى عنهم ، وهم برآء منها رأساً ومِن اعتقادِها على الوجه الذي يفهمُهُ ناقلا عنهم ، مِنْ غيرِ أَنْ يُبيَّنَ ما فيها مِنَ الفسادِ العظيم الذي لا يرضاه أدنى العقلاء المسدَّدينَ ، أو يُخْرِجَ لها مِنَ التأويل ما يليقُ بأولئكَ الأئمَّةِ رضيَ الله تعالى عنهم و ونفعنا بهم وربُّما ينقلُها بعضُ مَنْ لا خلاقَ لهُ في مجلس يجمعُ عامة الناسِ وغيرهم على وجهِ لا يُبيِّنُ لهم ما يحتسبونَ عليه وما هو الحقُّ الذي يعتمدون عليه ، ويبعثه على ذلكَ إظهار أنَّهُ حافظ لما لم يحفظه الناسُ مِنْ غرائب الأقوالِ ! وما عرف الأحمقُ أنَّ الحق في العقائدِ العقلية واحد لا يقبلُ الخلاف ، فلا يحتاج المكلَّفُ فيها إلا إلى معرفة ذلكَ القولِ الواحدِ الذي هو الحق ، وما سواه فساد وضلال لا حاجة لأحدٍ بحفظه ، ولا لتمضمض الفم بذكرِهِ ، اللهم إلا أن يذكرَهُ العارفُ لإظهار فسادِهِ والتحذيرِ مِنْ شَرِّهِ ؛ فحسن . وأمَّا حفظه على وجهِ يُلبِّسُ على حافظِهِ ، ويشك فيه هل هو حق أم لا .. فحفظ هذا مذموم ، وفتنةٌ مهلكةٌ له ولمَنْ يتعلَّمُ منه والعياذ بالله تعالى ؛ إذ هو جاهل بمعرفة الحقِّ الذي هو واحد في عقيدة لا تقبلُ الخلاف شرعاً ولا عقلاً ، ويجب عليه ما يجب على سائر الجهلة ممَّنْ لم يحفظ شيئاً مِنْ تلكَ الأقوالِ أنْ يبحث عن معرفة الحقِّ ، وما يعتقده في أصل دينه وإنَّما يُمدَحُ حفظ الأقوالِ والبحث عن غرائبها في المسائل الفرعية
In summary: staining these eminent imams — may God Almighty be pleased with them, benefit us through them, and reward them with the best reward from the Muslims — by attributing a real effect to the originated power [qudra] is slander and lying, no doubt about it. The human devils among the innovators have inserted corrupt statements that are not sound by reason or transmission into the books of some eminent Sunni imams, such as the 'Ihya' of Imam al-Ghazali and the like, with the intent of causing sedition, or out of envy so that people become averse to following them and dedicating themselves to examining the precious jewels they deposited in their writings, which are considered among the extraordinary miracles. Rather, they inserted much of that into prophetic hadiths, and dared to introduce fabricated, false hadiths into them for purposes including the intent of belittling the honor of the noble Law, desiring to extinguish the light of God with their mouths, but God will complete His light, though the disbelievers detest [Surah as-Saff: 8]. I only lengthened this warning because I saw Muslims afflicted by many who transmit these corrupt statements and confuse them by attributing them to these eminent imams — may God Almighty be pleased with them — while they are completely innocent of them and of believing in them in the way the transmitter understands them, without clarifying the immense corruption in them that not even the most minimal of right-minded rational people would approve, or producing for them an interpretation befitting those imams — may God be pleased with them and benefit us through them. Perhaps someone with no good share transmits them in a gathering that includes common people and others in a way that he does not clarify to them what they are to be held accountable for and what is the truth upon which they should rely. What incites him to that is showing that he is a memorizer of things that people have not memorized from rare sayings! The foolish one did not know that the truth in rational beliefs is one and does not admit disagreement, so the legally responsible person needs only to know that single statement which is the truth; everything else is corruption and misguidance, no one needs to memorize it nor even to rinse his mouth with its mention, except if the knowledgeable one mentions it to show its corruption and warn against its evil — that is good. As for memorizing it in a way that confuses its memorizer, making him doubt whether it is truth or not, such memorization is blameworthy, a destructive temptation for him and for whoever learns from him — God forbid! For he is ignorant of knowing the truth, which is one in a creed that does not admit disagreement by law or reason. It is incumbent upon him what is incumbent upon other ignorant people who have not memorized any of those sayings: to seek knowledge of the truth and what he believes in the foundation of his religion. Indeed, memorization of sayings and searching for their rarities is only praised in subsidiary issues.
Source pages p. 398

Commentary
This passage is a warning and a critique. The author begins by asserting that attributing real causal influence to the originated power (qudra) of created beings is slander and clear falsehood. He then explains how the human devils among the innovators have inserted corrupt statements, which are neither rationally nor textually sound, into the books of eminent Sunni imams like al-Ghazali's Ihya, with malicious motives: to cause fitna, or envy leading people to abandon following those imams. They even dared to insert fabricated hadiths into the prophetic tradition to belittle the Sharia, citing the Quranic verse that God will complete His light despite the disbelievers. The author explains his extended warning: he sees many Muslims deceived by those who transmit these false statements, attributing them to the imams without clarifying the corruption or offering a sound interpretation. Some transmit them in gatherings without explaining the truth, motivated by a desire to show off rare knowledge. The author then makes a key doctrinal point: in rational beliefs ('aqa'id 'aqliyya), the truth is one and does not admit of disagreement. A responsible person (mukallaf) needs only to know that single truth; everything else is corruption. Memorizing false statements is only praiseworthy if done by a knowledgeable person to expose their falsehood and warn against them. If memorized in a way that causes confusion about truth, it is blameworthy and a destructive temptation. The ignorant person who memorizes such statements is like any other ignorant person who must seek the truth. Memorization and research into rare opinions is only praiseworthy in subsidiary (furū') issues, not in foundational creed.

Key Terms
القدرة الحادثة (al-qudra al-hāditha)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a motive Sanusi attributes to the innovators for inserting false statements?
A) Causing sedition (fitna)
B) Envy so that people abandon following the imams
C) To increase knowledge among the people
D) Belittling the honor of the Sharia

Key Takeaway
The insertion of fabricated statements into the works of Sunni imams is a malicious act aimed at undermining the Sunnah and causing confusion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever repeated a famous saying attributed to an imam without checking its source? How does Sanusi's warning make you feel about the responsibility you bear for every word you transmit about the scholars?
?
Sanusi says the innovators were motivated by envy so that people would turn away from following the imams. Search your heart: is there any envy you harbor toward someone who is more knowledgeable or more followed that might subtly influence how you speak about them?
?
The innovators inserted fabricated hadiths with the aim of 'extinguishing the light of God.' When you share a hadith or a quote without verifying its authenticity, could you be inadvertently contributing to obscuring that light? What will you commit to change today?

Sects and Disagreements
intermediate
6 min
The Singularity of Truth in Rational Creed
Sanusi establishes that truth in rational beliefs is one and distinguishes between praiseworthy and blameworthy memorization.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that in rational beliefs ('aqa'id 'aqliyya) the truth is singular and does not admit disagreement, and that memorizing false statements is only praiseworthy for refutation.

Core Idea
In creedal matters, truth is one; everything else is corruption.

Sanusi continues by explaining why he gave such an extended warning: he sees many Muslims deceived by those who transmit false statements without clarification. He then lays down a fundamental principle: in rational beliefs, the truth is one and does not admit disagreement. This lesson explores that principle and its implications for how we approach creedal statements.

Guided Path
1
Read the second part of the passage
Read from 'Wa innamā aṭaltu' to the end. This part explains the principle of truth being one.
Notice the contrast between the foolish transmitter and the knowledgeable refuter.
2
Understand the principle of unity of truth
Sanusi asserts that truth in rational beliefs is one and does not admit disagreement. Reflect on why this is important for a mukallaf.
3
Differentiate praiseworthy and blameworthy memorization
The passage distinguishes when mentioning false statements is good (for refutation) and when it is blameworthy (causing doubt). Identify both cases.
The key is the intention and the outcome.
4
Apply to the duty of the ignorant
Sanusi says anyone ignorant of the truth, including those who memorize false statements without understanding, must seek the truth. How does this apply to students of knowledge?
This leads to the conclusion that in subsidiary issues, memorization is praised.

Commentary

He then explains how the human devils among the innovators have inserted corrupt statements, which are neither rationally nor textually sound, into the books of eminent Sunni imams like al-Ghazali's Ihya, with malicious motives: to cause fitna, or envy leading people to abandon following those imams. The author then makes a key doctrinal point: in rational beliefs ('aqa'id 'aqliyya), the truth is one and does not admit of disagreement. Key Terms
العقائد العقلية (al-ʿaqāʾid al-ʿaqliyya)
الخلاف (al-khilāf)
المكلَّف (al-mukallaf)
المسائل الفرعية (al-masāʾil al-farʿiyya)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Memorizing many different creedal statements is a sign of knowledge and praiseworthy.
Correction: Sanusi clarifies that in rational beliefs, truth is one; memorizing false statements is only praiseworthy for refutation, and if it causes doubt it is blameworthy.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is it praiseworthy to mention a false or corrupt statement in matters of creed?
A) When one wants to show off rare knowledge in a gathering.
B) When one memorizes it without understanding its truth or falsehood.
C) When a knowledgeable person mentions it to expose its corruption and warn against its evil.
D) When it is in a subsidiary (furūʿ) issue and one is researching.

Key Takeaway
In foundational creed, the truth is one; seeking it is obligatory, and memorizing deviant opinions is only beneficial for refutation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever been more concerned with appearing knowledgeable about rare, deviant opinions than with grasping the simple, saving truth of your creed? What will you do this week to prioritize the truth over impressiveness?
?
When you hear a theological claim from a speaker or a book, do you critically evaluate whether it is the singular truth or a corrupt statement, or do you accept it because it sounds novel? Will you commit to verifying everything against the Qur'an and Sunnah from today?
?
Sanusi says that memorizing statements that cause doubt is a destructive temptation. Is there any belief you hold that you have not personally verified, leaving you in uncertainty? Will you resolve to seek clarity on that matter before the day ends?

Classification of Shirk into Types
Sanusi enumerates three types of shirk and their subtypes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the major categories of shirk according to Sanusi, including the subtle forms of attributing causal power to creation.

Core Idea
Shirk goes beyond idol worship; it includes attributing independent causation to nature.

Sanusi presents a detailed classification of shirk, showing that it takes various forms beyond the obvious worship of idols and angels. He highlights three main types, with special attention to the subtle error of attributing causal efficacy to natural objects and celestial bodies. This passage helps us recognize the breadth of shirk as understood in Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice how Sanusi structures his classification.
The passage mentions 'four kinds' but lists three; this is consistent across manuscripts.
2
Identify the three main types
Look for the first two types: (1) shirk of Christians affirming hypostases, (2) worship of idols/angels as intermediaries. Then the third type is attributing action to other than Allah, which has its own subtypes.
3
Examine the subtypes of causal shirk
The third main type is subdivided into three: (a) celestial spheres influencing the lower world, (b) natural objects like fire or food acting by themselves, (c) the view that things act by their nature, which Sanusi declares as disbelief without dispute.
This shows the danger of philosophical views on causality.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider why Sanusi includes these subtle forms: shirk is not only about worship but also about attributing autonomous power to anything other than Allah.

والطريق الثالثُ : الشَّرْكُ والعدد والحكم بأنَّ الآلهة كثيرة : وهذا الشِّرْكُ على أربعة أصناف : شرك تتعدَّدُ فيهِ ذاتُ اللهِ تعالى : وذلك شرك النصارى في ثبوتِ أقانيمها ، وأنَّها ثلاثةٌ تخلُقُ بثلاثتِها ، وهي ثلاثةٌ واحدٌ! نعوذُ باللهِ من الضلالة . والصنف الآخرُ مِنَ الشركِ : إثباتُ آلهة تُقرَّبُ إِليهِ مَنْ عبدَها وعظَمَها ، وهذا هو عبادة الأوثان والملائكة . وصنف آخرُ مِنَ الشِّرْكِ : وهو إضافة الفعل لغير الله سبحانه وهذا الصنف على ثلاثة أنواع : أحدها : إضافة الفعل إلى الأفلاكِ ؛ بأنَّها تُؤثر في العالم السفلي تأثيرات في الأجسام والنبات والمركَّبات ، وأن البعض يتولَّدُ مِنَ البعض ، وهذا النوع يختص بهِ الفيلسوفيُّ ومَنْ تابعَهُ مِنْ عامَّتِهم . عُمْيُ الْقُلُوبِ عَمُوا عَنْ كُلِّ فَائِدَةٍ لِأَنَّهُمْ كَفَرُوا بِاللَّهِ تَقْلِيدَا. الثاني : ما أُضيفَ مِنْ بعض الأفعالِ إلى البعض ؛ مِنْ أَنَّ النارَ تُحرِقُ ، والطعامَ يُشبِعُ ، والثوبَ يستر ، إلى غير ذلكَ مِنْ ربطِ العاداتِ حتى ظنُّوها واجبةً ، وتلك ضلالةٌ تبع الفيلسوفيَّ فيها كثيرٌ مِنْ عامَّةِ المسلمينَ ، وهم فيها على اعتقادات : فمَنْ قالَ : بطبعها تفعل .. فلا خلاف في كفره .
And the third way: polytheism (shirk), multiplicity, and the judgment that the gods are many. And this shirk is of four kinds: shirk in which the essence of Allah Almighty is multiplied: and that is the shirk of the Christians in affirming their hypostases (aqanim), and that they are three, creating by their three, and they are three one! We seek refuge with Allah from misguidance. And the other kind of shirk: affirming gods that bring near to Him whoever worships and magnifies them, and this is the worship of idols and angels. And another kind of shirk: and it is attributing action to other than Allah the Exalted, and this kind is of three types: one of them: attributing action to the celestial spheres; that they effect influences in the lower world, effects in bodies, plants, and compounds, and that some are generated from others; and this type is specific to the philosopher and those of their commoners who follow him. 'Blind of hearts, they are blind to every benefit, because they disbelieved in Allah through blind imitation.' The second: what is attributed of some actions to some [causes]; such as that fire burns, food satiates, clothing covers, and so on from linking habits until they deemed them necessary; and that is a misguidance in which many of the common Muslims followed the philosopher; and they are in it upon [various] beliefs. So whoever says: 'it acts by its nature' — there is no dispute about his disbelief.
Source pages p. 404

Commentary
This passage is a classification of shirk (polytheism) into categories. Sanusi begins by stating that the third path of misguidance is shirk, the belief in multiple deities. He then claims there are four kinds, though only three are listed (as the footnote clarifies). The first kind is the shirk of the Christians, who affirm multiple hypostases (أقانيم) within the divine essence, believing in three that are one. Sanusi calls this misguidance. The second kind is the worship of idols and angels as intermediaries that are supposed to bring one closer to Allah. The third kind is attributing actions to other than Allah, which itself has three subtypes: (a) attributing effects to the celestial spheres, claiming they influence the lower world, a view held by philosophers; (b) attributing causal efficacy to natural objects like fire, food, and clothing, based on habitual observation, leading people to consider these causal connections necessary; Sanusi notes that many common Muslims followed the philosophers in this. He then states that whoever says these things act by their own nature (بطبعها تفعل) is a disbeliever without dispute.

Key Terms
شرك
أقانيم
إضافة الفعل
ربط العادات
طبع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many think shirk only means worshiping other deities like idols.
Correction: Sanusi shows shirk also includes attributing causal power to natural objects or celestial bodies, as in philosophical views.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, how many types does the third category of shirk (attributing actions to other than Allah) have?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) One

Key Takeaway
Sanusi teaches that shirk encompasses not only direct worship of other beings but also attributing independent causal power to any created thing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see a fire burn or food satisfy your hunger, do you ever unconsciously think these things have power in themselves? How does Sanusi's teaching that such a belief is shirk challenge you to change your inner thoughts? What practical step will you take this week to remind yourself that only Allah creates effects?
?
The common Muslims followed philosophers into error. In what areas of your life have you accepted popular beliefs or scientific assumptions without checking them against the teachings of Ahl al-Sunnah? What will you do to start examining your beliefs more critically?
?
Sanusi declares without dispute that whoever says a created thing acts by its nature is a disbeliever. Does this description fit any belief you hold? If not, are you still certain that you never attribute causality to anything other than Allah? How would you respond if someone accused you of this type of shirk?

The Mu'tazila on Human Action and Their Disbelief
Sanusi presents and refutes the Mu'tazila view on human action.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila claim that humans create their own actions, the Sunni response declaring them disbelievers, and the evidence for that ruling.

Core Idea
Claiming that humans create their own actions leads to disbelief.

Sanusi now addresses a major theological deviation: the Mu'tazila assertion that the servant invents his own actions. This claim challenges Allah's sole creatorship and leads to a grave consequence. In this passage, Sanusi presents their argument and then refutes it, showing why the Sunni stance is to declare them disbelievers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Sanusi categorises this as the third type of misattribution.
2
Identify the Mu'tazila claim
Find what the Mu'tazila assert about human actions and their reasoning. They say the servant invents his own actions, otherwise Allah would be unjust.
3
Understand the Sunni disagreement
Sanusi notes that Ahl al-Sunna disagree on takfir. Determine which view is considered more apparent according to Sanusi.
The phrase 'al-aẓhar annahum kāfirūn' indicates the stronger position.
4
Examine the evidence
Two proofs are given: a hadith about the Qadariyya being cursed and a Qur'anic verse. Ask yourself how these support the ruling.
The verse challenges any creator besides Allah, refuting the idea that humans create.
5
Reflect on the implications
Think about why this issue is so serious in Sunni theology. How does it relate to tawhid and divine attributes?
This connects to the broader lesson on attributing acts to others.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع الثالثُ ممَّا أُضيف الفعلُ فيهِ إلى غيرِ اللهِ سبحانَهُ : ما ذهَبَ إليهِ المعتزلةُ مِنْ أنَّ العبد يخترعُ أفعال نفسِهِ ، وقالوا : لو كَلَّفَ اللهُ تعالى بما لا يخترعُهُ العبدُ . . لكانَ جَوْراً وظلماً ! وقد اختلف أهل السنَّةِ في تكفيرهم ، والأظهرُ أنَّهم كافرونَ وهذا مذهبُ القاضي أبي بكر بن الطيب في تكفيرِ مَنْ يَؤُولُ بِهِ قولُهُ إلى الكفر ولقولِهِ عليهِ الصلاةُ والسلامُ : « لُعِنَتِ الْقَدَرِيَّةُ عَلَى لِسَانِ سَبْعِينَ نَبِيّاً » ولتكذيبهم قوله تعالى : هَلْ مِنْ خَلِقٍ غَيْرُ اللَّهِ ﴾ [فاطر : ٣]
The third type of that in which an act is attributed to other than Allah: that which the Mu'tazila went to, that the servant invents his own actions, and they said: If Allah were to charge with what the servant does not invent, it would be injustice and tyranny. And the Ahl al-Sunna disagreed concerning declaring them disbelievers, and the more apparent is that they are disbelievers. And this is the madhhab of al-Qadi Abu Bakr ibn al-Tayyib in declaring disbelievers those whose statement leads them to disbelief, and because of his statement (peace be upon him): 'The Qadariyya were cursed on the tongue of seventy prophets' and because of their denial of His statement: 'Is there any creator other than Allah?' [Fatir: 3].
Source pages p. 406

Commentary
This passage discusses the third type of misattribution of actions: the Mu'tazila claim that the servant invents his own actions. They argue that if Allah charged the servant with what he does not create, that would be unjust. Sanusi notes that Ahl al-Sunna differ on takfir of the Mu'tazila, but the more apparent view is that they are disbelievers. He supports this with the hadith cursing the Qadariyya (which includes the Mu'tazila) and the Qur'anic verse challenging any creator besides Allah.

Key Terms
المعتزلة (al-Mu'tazila)
يخترع (yakhtari‘, invents)
جور (jawr, injustice)
قدريّة (Qadariyya)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Mu'tazila are merely innovators but not disbelievers.
Correction: Sanusi states the more apparent view is that they are disbelievers, supported by hadith and Quran.

Checkpoint
What is the more apparent ruling regarding the Mu'tazila according to Sanusi?
A) They are innovators but not disbelievers
B) They are disbelievers
C) They are excused
D) They are like the Qadariyya

Key Takeaway
Sanusi affirms that the Mu'tazila are disbelievers based on the hadith cursing the Qadariyya and the Qur'anic verse challenging any creator besides Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you accomplish something good, do you find yourself thinking 'I did it' more than 'Allah enabled me'? How does this lesson expose that as a dangerous echo of the Mu'tazila claim?
?
Have you ever justified a sin by saying 'I couldn't help it' or 'It's just how I am'? What does the absolute sovereignty of Allah over all actions, taught in this lesson, demand you change in how you view your own will?
?
If the Mu'tazila were cursed for attributing creation to themselves, what does that say about your own subtle pride in your talents or efforts? What concrete step can you take today to consciously attribute every success and failure solely to Allah?

Does Command Entail Will? The Mu'tazila Argument Refuted
Mu'tazila objection and Sanusi's first rebuttal against command implying will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazila argument that God must provide means to obey is based on a false principle, and how Sanusi refutes it using the example of the disbeliever.

Core Idea
Command does not necessarily mean the commander wills the commanded act.

The Mu'tazila raise an objection based on human analogies: a wise person would not command without enabling. Sanusi responds by exposing their underlying principle, which he rejects. This lesson covers the objection and Sanusi's first rebuttal.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Mu'tazila's analogies (wise person, caller to reconciliation, host) and note the conclusion they draw: failure to enable is blameworthy.
The analogies are based on human norms.
2
Identify the underlying principle
Sanusi states that the objection is built on the principle that commanding something entails the commander's will for it. Identify this principle.
This is the key point of disagreement.
3
Understand the counterexample
Sanusi provides the example of Allah commanding the disbeliever to believe while not willing belief from him. Reflect on how this disproves the principle.
If command entailed will, this would be impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا - أذلَّ اللهُ تعالى بدعتهم ، وكشف عوارَهم لكل مسلم - : نحن نقطع بأنَّ الحكيم إذا أمر بطاعة ، وقَدَرَ أنْ يعطي المأمور ما يصل به إلى الطاعةِ مِنْ غيرِ تضرُّر بذلكَ ، ثم لم يفعل .. كان مذموماً عند العقلاء ، معدوداً في زمرة البخلاء وكذلكَ مَنْ دعا عدوَّهُ إلى الموالاة والرجوع إلى الطاعة .. لا يجوزُ أنْ يعاملَهُ مِنَ الغلظ واللين إلا بما هو أنجح في حصول المراد ، وأدعى إلى ترك العنادِ وأيضاً من اتخذ ضيافة لرجل ، واستدعى حضوره ، وعلمَ أَنَّهُ لو تلقَّاهُ بشِّرِ وطلاقة وجْهِ لدخل وأكل ، وإلا فلا . . فالواجب عليهِ البِشْرُ والطلاقة والملاطفة ، لا أضدادها ! قلنا : بنيتُم هذا الكلامَ على أصلكم الفاسد ؛ أَنَّ الأمر بالشيء يستلزم إرادةَ الآمرِ له ، حتى يلزم أن يعين الأمرُ المأمور ليحصل لهُ مراده ! وذلك باطل عندنا ؛ فإنَّ اللهَ سبحانَهُ قد أمر الكافر بالإيمان ولم يرده منه ، وإِنَّما أَرادَ منه ضدَّهُ ولو سلَّمْنا استلزام الأمرِ الإرادةَ بناءً على أصلكم الفاسد كان قياسكم أيضاً فاسداً ؛ لأن ما ذكر تموه إنَّما يصح في حكيم يحتاجُ إلى طاعة الأولياء ورجوع الأعداء ، ويتعزّزُ بكثرة الأعوان والأنصار ، وتعظُمُ لديه الأقدارُ ، ويكون للشيء الحادث بالنسبة إليه شرفٌ مِنْ حيث ذاته و مقدار وأينَ هذا ممَّنْ ثبتَ لهُ الغَناءُ المطلقُ والكمال الأزلي ؛ بحيثُ استوى بالنسبة إليهِ إقبال جميع الخلْقِ على طاعتِهِ ، وإدبار جميع إلى معصيته ؟! فكيفَ وكلا الأمرين دال على سَعَةِ مُلْكِهِ وعظيم قدرتِهِ ونفوذ إرادتِهِ ؟! إِذْ هو جلَّ وعلا الذي أقبلَ بمَنْ أقبل على طاعتِهِ ، ومنعها الآخرَ وساقَهُ إلى معصيتِهِ ، لا أثر لمخلوق مِنْ مخلوقاتِهِ في أثر ما عموماً ، بل هو جلَّ وعلا يُقلب الجميع ويديرهم كيف شاء وَلَوْ شَاءَ رَبُّكَ لَجَعَلَ النَّاسَ أُمَّةً وَاحِدَةً ﴾ [هود : ١١٨]
They said — may Allah Almighty humiliate their innovation, and expose their shame to every Muslim —: We are certain that the wise person, if he commands an act of obedience, and is able to give the commanded one that by which he may reach obedience without harm from that, and then does not do it... he would be blameworthy in the view of the rational people, counted among the group of the miserly. Likewise, whoever calls his enemy to amity and return to obedience... it is not permissible for him to treat him with harshness or gentleness except with that which is most successful in attaining the desired end, and most conducive to abandoning stubbornness. Also, whoever prepares a feast for a man, and invites his presence, and knows that if he meets him with cheerfulness and an open face he would enter and eat, otherwise no... then it is obligatory upon him to show cheerfulness, openness, and kindness, not their opposites! We said: You have built this speech upon your corrupt principle: that commanding something entails the will of the commander for it, such that it necessitates that the commander aid the commanded so that his desire is obtained. And that is false in our view, for Allah — glorified be He — has commanded the disbeliever to believe and did not will it from him; rather He willed its opposite from him. And even if we grant the entailment of command for will based on your corrupt principle, your analogy is also corrupt, because what you have mentioned is only valid for a wise person who needs the obedience of the friends and the return of the enemies, and is strengthened by many supporters and helpers, and for whom things become great, and for whom a contingent thing has honor in terms of its essence and measure. And where is this compared to One to whom absolute self-sufficiency and eternal perfection are established, such that, relative to Him, the turning of all creation towards His obedience and their turning away towards His disobedience are equal?! How (can it be) when both matters indicate the vastness of His kingdom, the greatness of His power, and the penetration of His will?! For He — exalted and majestic — is the One who turns towards obedience whom He wills, and prevents the other and propels him to disobedience. There is no effect of any creature from His creatures upon any effect at all; rather He — exalted and majestic — turns all and directs them as He wills. "And if your Lord had willed, He would have made mankind one nation" [Surah Hud: 118].
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage presents an objection from the Mu'tazila and Sanusi's refutation of it. The passage is an objection-and-answer structure. First, the Mu'tazila argue by analogy with a wise person: if a wise person commands something and can provide the means without harm but does not, he is blameworthy. Similarly, one calling an enemy to reconciliation must use the most effective means (gentleness). And one inviting a guest must be welcoming. They imply that God, if He commands faith and yet does not provide the necessary means (or withholds grace), would be blameworthy like the miser. Sanusi responds with two points. First, he rejects their underlying principle that commanding something necessitates the commander's will for that thing. He gives the counterexample: Allah commanded the disbeliever to believe but did not will belief from him; rather He willed his disbelief (i.e., He willed the opposite). Thus the command does not imply the commander's will. Second, even if one grants that command entails will (their principle), their analogy fails because it applies only to a wise person who needs support from others and whose status depends on obedience. But God is utterly self-sufficient and eternal; the obedience or disobedience of all creatures is equal to Him. Both actually demonstrate His power and will. God is the one who turns some to obedience and others to disobedience; no creature has any independent effect. The passage ends with a Quranic verse affirming God's absolute will.

Key Terms
الأمر بالشيء يستلزم إرادة الآمر
الحكيم
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If God commands something, He must will it and provide the means for it to happen.
Correction: God can command what He does not will, as shown by His command to the disbeliever to believe while willing disbelief from him.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what example disproves the principle that command entails will?
A) Allah commanded the angels to prostrate to Adam.
B) Allah commanded the disbeliever to believe but did not will belief from him.
C) Allah commanded Moses to speak to Pharaoh.
D) Allah commanded all humans to obey.

Key Takeaway
God's command does not imply His will for the commanded act; He can command what He wills against, as with the disbeliever's faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that Allah commanded the disbeliever to believe but did not will it, does that disturb your sense of fairness? Does it challenge your understanding of divine justice? How does Sanusi's distinction between command and will change the way you view God's relationship with human action? Take a moment to ask yourself: if God can command what He does not will, what does that mean for your own salvation? Are you relying on His command or on His will?
?
Consider a time you commanded someone to do something you did not truly want them to do (e.g., out of duty or social pressure). Can you identify a moment in your life where your own command did not express your will? How does that experience help you understand that God's commands are not always an expression of His will? Now, commit to surrendering your understanding of fairness to God's absolute wisdom, even when His ways seem puzzling.
?
If God commands faith but does not will it for some, what does that mean for your own faith? Does it make you grateful that He willed faith for you? Does it create fear and awe that His will is not bound by His commands? How should this affect your daily worship and reliance on Him? Tonight, in your prayer, thank Allah for willing faith for you, and ask Him to keep you firm until the end.

God's Self-Sufficiency: Why the Wise Person Analogy Fails
Sanusi's second rebuttal: even if command entails will, the analogy fails due to God's self-sufficiency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazila analogy with a wise person does not apply to God, due to His absolute self-sufficiency and eternal perfection.

Core Idea
God does not need our obedience; He is utterly self-sufficient.

Even if one grants that command entails will, the Mu'tazila analogy is still flawed because it compares God to a needy human. This lesson examines Sanusi's second rebuttal, which highlights God's absolute self-sufficiency and the futility of measuring Him by human standards.

Guided Path
1
Read the conditional argument
Sanusi first posits 'even if we grant' the principle, then proceeds to dismantle the analogy. Notice the logical structure: conditional concession followed by a stronger refutation.
This shows Sanusi's thoroughness.
2
Contrast the wise person with God
The wise person needs supporters and benefits from obedience, but God is described as having absolute self-sufficiency (الغناء المطلق) and eternal perfection (الكمال الأزلي). List the contrasts.
God is not affected by anyone's obedience or disobedience.
3
Reflect on the Quranic verse
The lesson ends with the verse 'If your Lord had willed, He would have made mankind one nation.' Consider how this reinforces God's absolute control.
Allah's will is supreme and no creature has independent effect.

قالوا - أذلَّ اللهُ تعالى بدعتهم ، وكشف عوارَهم لكل مسلم - : نحن نقطع بأنَّ الحكيم إذا أمر بطاعة ، وقَدَرَ أنْ يعطي المأمور ما يصل به إلى الطاعةِ مِنْ غيرِ تضرُّر بذلكَ ، ثم لم يفعل .. كان مذموماً عند العقلاء ، معدوداً في زمرة البخلاء وكذلكَ مَنْ دعا عدوَّهُ إلى الموالاة والرجوع إلى الطاعة .. لا يجوزُ أنْ يعاملَهُ مِنَ الغلظ واللين إلا بما هو أنجح في حصول المراد ، وأدعى إلى ترك العنادِ وأيضاً من اتخذ ضيافة لرجل ، واستدعى حضوره ، وعلمَ أَنَّهُ لو تلقَّاهُ بشِّرِ وطلاقة وجْهِ لدخل وأكل ، وإلا فلا . . فالواجب عليهِ البِشْرُ والطلاقة والملاطفة ، لا أضدادها ! قلنا : بنيتُم هذا الكلامَ على أصلكم الفاسد ؛ أَنَّ الأمر بالشيء يستلزم إرادةَ الآمرِ له ، حتى يلزم أن يعين الأمرُ المأمور ليحصل لهُ مراده ! وذلك باطل عندنا ؛ فإنَّ اللهَ سبحانَهُ قد أمر الكافر بالإيمان ولم يرده منه ، وإِنَّما أَرادَ منه ضدَّهُ ولو سلَّمْنا استلزام الأمرِ الإرادةَ بناءً على أصلكم الفاسد كان قياسكم أيضاً فاسداً ؛ لأن ما ذكر تموه إنَّما يصح في حكيم يحتاجُ إلى طاعة الأولياء ورجوع الأعداء ، ويتعزّزُ بكثرة الأعوان والأنصار ، وتعظُمُ لديه الأقدارُ ، ويكون للشيء الحادث بالنسبة إليه شرفٌ مِنْ حيث ذاته و مقدار وأينَ هذا ممَّنْ ثبتَ لهُ الغَناءُ المطلقُ والكمال الأزلي ؛ بحيثُ استوى بالنسبة إليهِ إقبال جميع الخلْقِ على طاعتِهِ ، وإدبار جميع إلى معصيته ؟! فكيفَ وكلا الأمرين دال على سَعَةِ مُلْكِهِ وعظيم قدرتِهِ ونفوذ إرادتِهِ ؟! إِذْ هو جلَّ وعلا الذي أقبلَ بمَنْ أقبل على طاعتِهِ ، ومنعها الآخرَ وساقَهُ إلى معصيتِهِ ، لا أثر لمخلوق مِنْ مخلوقاتِهِ في أثر ما عموماً ، بل هو جلَّ وعلا يُقلب الجميع ويديرهم كيف شاء وَلَوْ شَاءَ رَبُّكَ لَجَعَلَ النَّاسَ أُمَّةً وَاحِدَةً ﴾ [هود : ١١٨]
They said — may Allah Almighty humiliate their innovation, and expose their shame to every Muslim —: We are certain that the wise person, if he commands an act of obedience, and is able to give the commanded one that by which he may reach obedience without harm from that, and then does not do it... he would be blameworthy in the view of the rational people, counted among the group of the miserly. Likewise, whoever calls his enemy to amity and return to obedience... it is not permissible for him to treat him with harshness or gentleness except with that which is most successful in attaining the desired end, and most conducive to abandoning stubbornness. Also, whoever prepares a feast for a man, and invites his presence, and knows that if he meets him with cheerfulness and an open face he would enter and eat, otherwise no... then it is obligatory upon him to show cheerfulness, openness, and kindness, not their opposites! We said: You have built this speech upon your corrupt principle: that commanding something entails the will of the commander for it, such that it necessitates that the commander aid the commanded so that his desire is obtained. And that is false in our view, for Allah — glorified be He — has commanded the disbeliever to believe and did not will it from him; rather He willed its opposite from him. And even if we grant the entailment of command for will based on your corrupt principle, your analogy is also corrupt, because what you have mentioned is only valid for a wise person who needs the obedience of the friends and the return of the enemies, and is strengthened by many supporters and helpers, and for whom things become great, and for whom a contingent thing has honor in terms of its essence and measure. And where is this compared to One to whom absolute self-sufficiency and eternal perfection are established, such that, relative to Him, the turning of all creation towards His obedience and their turning away towards His disobedience are equal?! How (can it be) when both matters indicate the vastness of His kingdom, the greatness of His power, and the penetration of His will?! For He — exalted and majestic — is the One who turns towards obedience whom He wills, and prevents the other and propels him to disobedience. There is no effect of any creature from His creatures upon any effect at all; rather He — exalted and majestic — turns all and directs them as He wills. "And if your Lord had willed, He would have made mankind one nation" [Surah Hud: 118].
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage presents an objection from the Mu'tazila and Sanusi's refutation of it. The passage is an objection-and-answer structure. First, the Mu'tazila argue by analogy with a wise person: if a wise person commands something and can provide the means without harm but does not, he is blameworthy. Similarly, one calling an enemy to reconciliation must use the most effective means (gentleness). And one inviting a guest must be welcoming. They imply that God, if He commands faith and yet does not provide the necessary means (or withholds grace), would be blameworthy like the miser. Sanusi responds with two points. First, he rejects their underlying principle that commanding something necessitates the commander's will for that thing. He gives the counterexample: Allah commanded the disbeliever to believe but did not will belief from him; rather He willed his disbelief (i.e., He willed the opposite). Thus the command does not imply the commander's will. Second, even if one grants that command entails will (their principle), their analogy fails because it applies only to a wise person who needs support from others and whose status depends on obedience. But God is utterly self-sufficient and eternal; the obedience or disobedience of all creatures is equal to Him. Both actually demonstrate His power and will. God is the one who turns some to obedience and others to disobedience; no creature has any independent effect. The passage ends with a Quranic verse affirming God's absolute will.

Key Terms
الغناء المطلق
الكمال الأزلي
الطرد والاعتزال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God needs our obedience or is affected by it in some way, like a human leader.
Correction: God is absolutely self-sufficient and eternal; obedience and disobedience are equal in their effect on Him, though both manifest His power.

Checkpoint
Why does Sanusi say the analogy with a wise person fails even if command entails will?
A) Because a wise person would never command without enabling.
B) Because God does not need obedience and is absolutely self-sufficient.
C) Because the disbeliever is not invited to obedience.
D) Because the wise person in the analogy is imaginary.

Key Takeaway
God's absolute self-sufficiency renders human analogies of wise behavior inapplicable; He is not in need of anything, and all actions depend solely on His will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you obey Allah because you believe He needs your obedience, or because you recognize His absolute sovereignty and your complete dependence on Him? How does this shift your intention in worship?
?
If God gains nothing from your obedience and loses nothing from your disobedience, what truly motivates you to obey Him? Is it love, fear, or something else? Examine your heart honestly.
?
The passage says obedience and disobedience are equal in benefit to God, yet He still commands. How does this reality affect your view of His mercy and justice? Will you live today with a deeper awareness that your actions are before the Self-Sufficient One who does not need them, but who directs all things?
