Critique of Mu'tazili Analogical Reasoning
Sanusi criticizes the Mu'tazili method of qiyas al-gha'ib 'ala al-shahid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sanusi rejects the Mu'tazili use of analogy from the witnessed to the unseen and how he upholds the Sunni foundation of divine freedom.

Core Idea
Mu'tazili analogies collapse under the weight of divine freedom.

This passage is a passionate critique of the Mu'tazili method of drawing analogies from human experience to God. Sanusi argues that their approach is fundamentally flawed because it fails to account for God's absolute sovereignty. He uses a vivid example to demonstrate that what is rational for humans is not necessarily binding on God.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verse
Begin by reciting the verse from Surat al-Sajda (32:13) to ground the discussion in divine revelation. Notice how God's will is not constrained by human notions of benefit.
The verse shows that God could have guided all but chose to fill Hell — His will is free.
2
Understand the human example
Consider the hypothetical scenario: a person with two equally harmless and beneficial options. No rational person would blame them for choosing either. This sets up the contrast with God.
In human affairs, such choice is morally neutral; but God's actions are not subject to human criteria.
3
Identify the rhetorical questions
Sanusi asks 'So what are these flawed views of yours?!' and 'What are these disjointed analogies of yours?' These are sharp condemnations of the Mu'tazili method.
The terms 'flawed views' (الأنظار المختلة) and 'disjointed analogies' (الأقيسة المنحلة) are key.
4
Grasp the Sunni foundation
Sanusi asserts that the truth is the foundation of Ahl al-Sunna, and he shows that Mu'tazili analogies cannot stand against it. They 'flew away' and 'vanished' when confronted with this truth.
This affirms Sunni creed that God is not obligated to do what is most beneficial for creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ شِئْنَا لَا نَيْنَا كُلَّ نَفْسٍ هُدَنهَا وَلَكِنْ حَقَّ الْقَوْلُ مِنْ لَأَمْلَأَنَّ جَهَنَّمَ مِنَ الْجِنَّةِ وَالنَّاسِ أَجْمَعِينَ ﴾ [السجدة : ١٣] . ونحنُ لو قدرنا في الشاهدِ شخصاً استوى بالنسبة إليه أمران ؛ بحيثُ لا يَتوقَّع في كلَّ منهما ضرراً لا حالاً ولا مالاً ، ولا يستفيد من فعل واحدٍ منهما كمالاً .. لَمَا ذمَّهُ عاقل في اختياره ما شاءَ منهما . فما هذه الأنظارُ منكم المختلَّةُ ؟! وما هذهِ الأقيسةُ منكم المنحلة ؟!(۱) التي وضعناها على محض الحقِّ الذي لا يصح غيرُه ، ولا يُقبَلُ في الشرع سواه ؛ وهو أصلُ أهل السنَّةِ رضيَ اللهُ تعالى عنهم .. فطارَتْ ، وانعدمَتْ بالكلية واضمحلت ثم ركَبْنا هذا على زخاريف أباطيلكم - قبَّحها الله تعالى - فلم تستطع حملها ، وزهقت عنها إلى الحضيض الأسفل ، وتلاشت وبطلت .
And if We willed, We could have given every soul its guidance, but the word from Me will be fulfilled: I will surely fill Hell with jinn and people all together. [Sajda: 13]. And we, in the witnessed realm, if we imagine a person for whom two matters are equal, such that he expects no harm from either of them, neither in condition nor wealth, and he does not derive perfection from doing either of them... no rational person would blame him for choosing whichever he wishes. So what are these flawed views of yours?! And what are these disjointed analogies of yours? which we placed upon pure truth, none other than which is valid, and which is accepted in the Law besides it—and it is the foundation of the Ahl al-Sunna, may Allah be pleased with them—they flew away, and became completely nonexistent and vanished. Then we mounted this upon the decorations of your falsehoods—may Allah disparage them—and they could not carry them, and they sank to the lowest depths, and they dissipated and were nullified.
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage is a general critique of the Mu'tazili method of reasoning by analogy from the witnessed (shahid) to the absent (gha'ib). The author begins by quoting a Quranic verse (32:13) to establish that God's will is not bound by what seems beneficial to humans; He could have guided all but chose to fill Hell. Then he gives a human example: if a person has two equally beneficial options, no one would blame him for choosing either. The Mu'tazila, however, use such analogies to argue that God must do what is most beneficial. The author derides their 'flawed views' and 'disjointed analogies,' stating that they were brought to the pure truth (the Sunni position) but could not withstand it—they 'flew away' and vanished. He then says he mounted these analogies on the 'decorations' of Mu'tazili falsehoods, and they collapsed under the weight.

Key Terms
الأنظار المختلة
الأقيسة المنحلة
قياس الغائب على الشاهد
أصل أهل السنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that all analogical reasoning in theology is invalid.
Correction: The author critiques only the Mu'tazili misuse of analogy, not analogy per se.

Checkpoint
What does the author accuse the Mu'tazila of using in their arguments?
A) Sound analogies based on the Qur'an
B) Flawed and disjointed analogies
C) Rational proofs from the Sunni tradition
D) Miracles and prophetic traditions

Key Takeaway
Sanusi condemns Mu'tazili analogical reasoning as flawed and dismantles it with the Sunni principle of divine sovereignty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reason about God's actions—like why He allows suffering or guides some but not others—do you find yourself slipping into the Mu'tazili mindset, assuming God must act 'fairly' by human standards? Which specific belief of yours might be an example of this? Will you submit to God's absolute sovereignty even when it feels uncomfortable?
?
Sanusi calls the Mu'tazili views 'flawed' and their analogies 'disjointed'—but have you ever arrogantly trusted your own intellect over clear revelation? Think of one time you rationalized away a clear command because your reasoning said otherwise. Will you repent from that and commit to letting revelation correct your intellect, not the other way around?
?
The verse 'If We willed, We could have given every soul its guidance' confronts the assumption that everyone 'deserves' guidance. Does this verse unsettle you? Do you secretly believe that you are better than others because you were guided? How will you cultivate humility and gratitude for the grace of guidance, knowing it is purely from Allah's will, not your merit?

Summary: The Corruption of Mu'tazilite Principles
Concluding summary on Mu'tazilite corruption.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author considers the Mu'tazilite principles to be evidently corrupt and self-refuting.

Core Idea
The very existence of Mu'tazilite misguidance is proof of its falsehood.

The author concludes his discussion of the Mu'tazilites with a powerful summary. He asserts that their errors are so obvious and numerous that they need no further refutation—their own existence as a misguided doctrine is itself evidence against them. This passage encapsulates the author's dismissive attitude toward the Mu'tazilite school.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice that the Arabic ends mid-sentence.
The passage is a concluding summary.
2
Identify the two main claims
The author makes two points: (a) the corruptions are too apparent and numerous to ignore, and (b) the very existence of their misguidance is evidence against them. Find these in the text.
3
Reflect on the rhetorical strategy
Consider why the author uses this argument. By saying that the misguidance itself is proof, he avoids needing a detailed refutation. This is a strong dismissive move.
This shows the author's confidence in his earlier arguments.

Source Text

وبالجملة : فمفاسد أصولِ المعتزلة أظهرُ مِنْ أَنْ تخفى ، وأكثرُ مِنْ أنْ تُحصى ، ووجود ضلالتهم هي بعينها دليلُ الردُّ عليهم ; إذْ لو وجبَ
In summary: the corruptions of the principles of the Mu'tazilites are too apparent to be hidden and too numerous to be counted. The existence of their misguidance is in itself evidence of refutation against them, for if it were obligatory...

This is a concluding summary. The author states that the flaws in Mu'tazilite doctrine are obvious and numerous, and their very misguidance serves as a proof against them. The sentence is cut off, but the intent is clear: the doctrine is self-refuting.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
If the Mu'tazilite error was so obvious, why do you think so many intelligent people fell into it? What does that say about your own susceptibility to subtle deviations? Are you actively guarding your heart and mind against them?

Sanusi's First Counterargument: Why Not Kill All Disbelievers as Children?
Sanusi presents the Mu'tazila claim and then refutes it with a reductio ad absurdum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first counterargument Sanusi uses against the Mu'tazila claim of al-aslah, showing that it leads to an absurd implication regarding disbelievers.

Core Idea
If killing children to prevent disbelief is beneficial, why didn't God kill all disbelievers as children?

Sanusi refutes the Mu'tazila doctrine that God must always do what is most beneficial for His servants. He begins by presenting their claim and then immediately turns it against them with a devastating reductio ad absurdum. In this lesson, we examine the first counterargument involving Pharaoh, Haman, and other notorious disbelievers.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Mu'tazila claim
Read the first part where the Mu'tazila state that causing children to die before puberty is most beneficial because God knows they would disbelieve if they lived.
They argue that death saves them from the harm of obligation.
2
Identify the counterargument
Sanusi then asks: if that logic holds, why didn't God cause all known disbelievers like Pharaoh to die as children? That would have been more beneficial.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
3
Reflect on the implication
Notice that the Mu'tazila would have to accept that such a death is better, yet they themselves do not experience it. Their principle leads to a contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بطلان قول أن الأصلح إمانة العبدِ قبل البلوغ فإن قالوا : الأصلحُ في حقهم ما فعلَ مولانا جل وعزَّ بهم مِنْ إما تتهم قبل البلوغ ؛ لأنَّه قد علم سبحانَهُ أنَّهم لو عاشوا إلى البلوغ لكفروا وضلُّوا وأضَلُّوا ، وأنَّهم لا يفوزون بمصلحة التكليف قيل لهم : فقد علم أيضاً جلَّ وعزَّ في سائر الكفرة ؛ كفرعونَ وهامان والنمروذ وأبي جهل أنهم إذا بلغوا وكُلّفوا فَجَروا وطَغَوا وكفروا ، فهلا أماتهمُ اللهُ عزَّ وجلَّ صغاراً ؟! فهو أصلح وأسلم ممَّا وقعوا فيهِ مِنَ العذابِ ، وغضبِ اللهِ تعالى الذي لا طاقة لمخلوق به ، وهم يقنعون بدون درجةِ الصبي ، ولا يَعْدِلُونَ بالسلامة شيئاً ثم نقول لهم أيضاً : يلزمكم أن يكونَ ما فعله سبحانه ؛ مِنْ إماتة الأنبياء والرُّسُلِ الهادين المهتدين والعلماء العاملين والأولياء المرشدينَ ، وتبقية إبليس وذريَّتِهِ الضالين المضلين إلى يوم الدين. أصلح لعباده ، وكفى بإلزام هذا شناعة وفضاحة وبالجملة : فمفاسد أصولِ المعتزلة أظهرُ مِنْ أَنْ تخفى ، وأكثرُ مِنْ أنْ تُحصى ، ووجود ضلالتهم هي بعينها دليلُ الردُّ عليهم ؛ إذْ لو وجبَ على الله تعالى الأصلحُ لعبادِهِ كما يزعمون .. لَمَا أَضلَّهمُ اللهُ تعالى وأعمى بصائرهم وتركهم في عَمَهِ وريبٍ يتردَّدونَ . فقد تبيَّنَ لكلِّ مؤمن بالعِيانِ : أنَّ أحكام العلي ذي الجلال .. لا تُوَزنُ بميزان أهل الاعتزال ، فعرفَ أَنَّ الواجبَ إِنَّما هو التفويضُ والإذعان ظاهراً وباطناً لـمَنْ لا مُعقِّبَ لِحُكْمِهِ ، ولا مُراجِعَ له في قضائِهِ ، ولا جَوَلانَ للعقولِ في سرِّ قَدَرِهِ ، ولا ضدَّ له ولا شبيهَ ولا مثالَ ، فتباركَ اللهُ ربُّ العالمينَ ، اللهم؛ عاملنا بمخض فضلِكَ وكرمِكَ في الدنيا والآخرة يا أرحم الراحمين.
Refutation of the statement that the most beneficial is to cause the servant to die before puberty. For if they say: The most beneficial for them is what our Lord, Mighty and Sublime, did with them, causing them to die before puberty, because He, glorified, knew that if they lived to puberty they would disbelieve, go astray, and lead others astray, and that they would not attain the benefit of obligation. It is said to them: He, Mighty and Sublime, also knew concerning all the disbelievers, such as Pharaoh, Haman, Nimrod, and Abu Jahl, that if they reached puberty and were obligated, they would transgress, rebel, and disbelieve. So why did not God, Mighty and Sublime, cause them to die as children? That would be more beneficial and safer than the punishment they fell into and the wrath of God Almighty that no creature can bear, and they are content with less than the rank of the child, and they do not exchange anything for safety. Then we also say to them: It would be necessary for you that what He, glorified, did, such as causing the death of the prophets and messengers who guide and are guided, the scholars who act, and the saints who guide, and leaving Iblis and his progeny, those who are astray and lead others astray, until the Day of Judgment, is more beneficial for His servants. And sufficient is this imposition as disgrace and shame. And in summary: The corruptions of the principles of the Mu'tazila are too apparent to be hidden and too numerous to be counted. And the existence of their misguidance is itself the proof of refutation against them; because if it were obligatory upon God Almighty to do the most beneficial for His servants as they claim, He would not have led them astray, blinded their insight, and left them wandering in confusion and doubt. So it has become clear to every believer by clear sight that the judgments of the Most High, Possessor of Majesty, are not weighed by the scale of the people of i'tizal. So he knows that the duty is only delegation and submission, outwardly and inwardly, to Him whose judgment no one can overturn, and no one can review His decree, and there is no room for intellects in the secret of His decree, and there is no opposite, no likeness, and no similitude to Him. So blessed be Allah, Lord of the worlds. O Allah, treat us with the essence of Your bounty and generosity in this world and the Hereafter, O Most Merciful of the merciful.
Source pages p. 417

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila doctrine of al-aslah (the most beneficial). The author begins by stating the Mu'tazila claim: that God causes children to die before puberty because He knows they would disbelieve and be lost if they lived, so death is more beneficial for them and saves them from the harm of obligation. Then he presents the first counterargument: if that were true, then God should have caused all disbelievers like Pharaoh, Haman, Nimrod, and Abu Jahl to die as children, because He knew they would disbelieve and rebel. That would have been more beneficial and safer for them than the punishment they incurred. The Mu'tazila would accept that such a death would be better than the punishment, and they value safety above all. Next, the author presents a second counterargument: by the same logic, it would be more beneficial for God to cause the death of prophets, scholars, and saints (who guide others) and to leave Iblis and his progeny alive until the Day of Judgment (since they lead astray). This is clearly absurd and shameful for the Mu'tazila to accept. The author then concludes that the corruption of Mu'tazila principles is obvious, and their very misguidance is a proof against them: if God were obliged to do what is most beneficial, He would not have allowed them to go astray. Finally, the author emphasizes that God's judgments are not subject to human scales; the proper response is submission and delegation to His decree, acknowledging that there is no opposite or likeness to Him, and ends with a supplication.

Key Terms
الأصلح
المعتزلة
التكليف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: It is merciful for God to cause children to die before they can sin.
Correction: Sanusi shows this logic would require God to kill all disbelievers as children, which contradicts divine wisdom and justice as seen in the existence of disbelievers.

Checkpoint
What is the first counterargument Sanusi uses against the Mu'tazila claim?
A) It would also require God to cause all disbelievers to die as children.
B) It would require God to cause the prophets to die as children.
C) It denies free will.
D) It contradicts the Quran.

Key Takeaway
Sanusi's first counterargument shows that the Mu'tazila principle of al-aslah leads to an absurd implication that God should have killed all disbelievers as children.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever questioned why God allows certain hardships or deaths that seem 'merciful' to you in the moment? How does Sanusi's argument challenge your tendency to measure God's actions by your own standard of benefit?
?
When you see non-Muslims or sinners living long lives, do you ever secretly feel that God should have prevented their disbelief? Can you trust His wisdom even when His actions seem to contradict your sense of what is 'best'?
?
The Mu'tazila tried to make God's actions fit their logic, but it led to absurdity. Are there any commands or decrees of Allah that you struggle to accept because they don't seem 'beneficial' or 'merciful' by your reckoning? Will you submit to His wisdom and say, 'I believe, even if I do not understand'?

Sanusi's Second Counterargument and the Conclusion: The Duty of Submission
Sanusi delivers a second reductio ad absurdum and concludes that the Mu'tazila doctrine is self-refuting, leading to the imperative of submission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's second counterargument against the Mu'tazila and his conclusion that divine judgments are beyond human measure.

Core Idea
If God must always do what is most beneficial, then killing prophets and leaving Iblis alive would be better — an absurdity.

Sanusi continues his refutation with a second reductio ad absurdum: if the Mu'tazila principle were true, then it would be more beneficial for God to cause the death of prophets, scholars, and saints, and to keep Iblis and his progeny alive until the Day of Judgment. This leads to a clear condemnation of the Mu'tazila position. He then concludes that God's judgments are not subject to human scales and that submission is the only proper response.

Guided Path
1
Read the second counterargument
Sanusi argues that by the Mu'tazila logic, killing prophets and leaving Iblis alive would be more beneficial. Reflect on why this is disgraceful.
The Mu'tazila cannot accept this consequence.
2
Understand the conclusion
Sanusi states that the corruption of Mu'tazila principles is obvious—their very misguidance refutes them because if God were obliged to do what is best, He would not have allowed them to go astray.
This is a self-refuting argument.
3
Embrace the proper response
The lesson ends with the duty of delegation (tafwid) and submission (idhan) to God's decree, recognizing that intellects cannot penetrate His secrets.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بطلان قول أن الأصلح إمانة العبدِ قبل البلوغ فإن قالوا : الأصلحُ في حقهم ما فعلَ مولانا جل وعزَّ بهم مِنْ إما تتهم قبل البلوغ ؛ لأنَّه قد علم سبحانَهُ أنَّهم لو عاشوا إلى البلوغ لكفروا وضلُّوا وأضَلُّوا ، وأنَّهم لا يفوزون بمصلحة التكليف قيل لهم : فقد علم أيضاً جلَّ وعزَّ في سائر الكفرة ؛ كفرعونَ وهامان والنمروذ وأبي جهل أنهم إذا بلغوا وكُلّفوا فَجَروا وطَغَوا وكفروا ، فهلا أماتهمُ اللهُ عزَّ وجلَّ صغاراً ؟! فهو أصلح وأسلم ممَّا وقعوا فيهِ مِنَ العذابِ ، وغضبِ اللهِ تعالى الذي لا طاقة لمخلوق به ، وهم يقنعون بدون درجةِ الصبي ، ولا يَعْدِلُونَ بالسلامة شيئاً ثم نقول لهم أيضاً : يلزمكم أن يكونَ ما فعله سبحانه ؛ مِنْ إماتة الأنبياء والرُّسُلِ الهادين المهتدين والعلماء العاملين والأولياء المرشدينَ ، وتبقية إبليس وذريَّتِهِ الضالين المضلين إلى يوم الدين. أصلح لعباده ، وكفى بإلزام هذا شناعة وفضاحة وبالجملة : فمفاسد أصولِ المعتزلة أظهرُ مِنْ أَنْ تخفى ، وأكثرُ مِنْ أنْ تُحصى ، ووجود ضلالتهم هي بعينها دليلُ الردُّ عليهم ؛ إذْ لو وجبَ على الله تعالى الأصلحُ لعبادِهِ كما يزعمون .. لَمَا أَضلَّهمُ اللهُ تعالى وأعمى بصائرهم وتركهم في عَمَهِ وريبٍ يتردَّدونَ . فقد تبيَّنَ لكلِّ مؤمن بالعِيانِ : أنَّ أحكام العلي ذي الجلال .. لا تُوَزنُ بميزان أهل الاعتزال ، فعرفَ أَنَّ الواجبَ إِنَّما هو التفويضُ والإذعان ظاهراً وباطناً لـمَنْ لا مُعقِّبَ لِحُكْمِهِ ، ولا مُراجِعَ له في قضائِهِ ، ولا جَوَلانَ للعقولِ في سرِّ قَدَرِهِ ، ولا ضدَّ له ولا شبيهَ ولا مثالَ ، فتباركَ اللهُ ربُّ العالمينَ ، اللهم؛ عاملنا بمخض فضلِكَ وكرمِكَ في الدنيا والآخرة يا أرحم الراحمين.
Refutation of the statement that the most beneficial is to cause the servant to die before puberty. For if they say: The most beneficial for them is what our Lord, Mighty and Sublime, did with them, causing them to die before puberty, because He, glorified, knew that if they lived to puberty they would disbelieve, go astray, and lead others astray, and that they would not attain the benefit of obligation. It is said to them: He, Mighty and Sublime, also knew concerning all the disbelievers, such as Pharaoh, Haman, Nimrod, and Abu Jahl, that if they reached puberty and were obligated, they would transgress, rebel, and disbelieve. So why did not God, Mighty and Sublime, cause them to die as children? That would be more beneficial and safer than the punishment they fell into and the wrath of God Almighty that no creature can bear, and they are content with less than the rank of the child, and they do not exchange anything for safety. Then we also say to them: It would be necessary for you that what He, glorified, did, such as causing the death of the prophets and messengers who guide and are guided, the scholars who act, and the saints who guide, and leaving Iblis and his progeny, those who are astray and lead others astray, until the Day of Judgment, is more beneficial for His servants. And sufficient is this imposition as disgrace and shame. And in summary: The corruptions of the principles of the Mu'tazila are too apparent to be hidden and too numerous to be counted. And the existence of their misguidance is itself the proof of refutation against them; because if it were obligatory upon God Almighty to do the most beneficial for His servants as they claim, He would not have led them astray, blinded their insight, and left them wandering in confusion and doubt. So it has become clear to every believer by clear sight that the judgments of the Most High, Possessor of Majesty, are not weighed by the scale of the people of i'tizal. So he knows that the duty is only delegation and submission, outwardly and inwardly, to Him whose judgment no one can overturn, and no one can review His decree, and there is no room for intellects in the secret of His decree, and there is no opposite, no likeness, and no similitude to Him. So blessed be Allah, Lord of the worlds. O Allah, treat us with the essence of Your bounty and generosity in this world and the Hereafter, O Most Merciful of the merciful.
Source pages p. 417

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila doctrine of al-aslah (the most beneficial). The author begins by stating the Mu'tazila claim: that God causes children to die before puberty because He knows they would disbelieve and be lost if they lived, so death is more beneficial for them and saves them from the harm of obligation. Then he presents the first counterargument: if that were true, then God should have caused all disbelievers like Pharaoh, Haman, Nimrod, and Abu Jahl to die as children, because He knew they would disbelieve and rebel. That would have been more beneficial and safer for them than the punishment they incurred. The Mu'tazila would accept that such a death would be better than the punishment, and they value safety above all. Next, the author presents a second counterargument: by the same logic, it would be more beneficial for God to cause the death of prophets, scholars, and saints (who guide others) and to leave Iblis and his progeny alive until the Day of Judgment (since they lead astray). This is clearly absurd and shameful for the Mu'tazila to accept. The author then concludes that the corruption of Mu'tazila principles is obvious, and their very misguidance is a proof against them: if God were obliged to do what is most beneficial, He would not have allowed them to go astray. Finally, the author emphasizes that God's judgments are not subject to human scales; the proper response is submission and delegation to His decree, acknowledging that there is no opposite or likeness to Him, and ends with a supplication.

المعتزلة
التفويض
الإذعان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila principle of al-aslah is a sound way to understand God's actions.
Correction: Sanusi shows that applying the principle consistently leads to absurdities like killing prophets and leaving Iblis, and it is self-refuting because God allows misguidance.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?

The Duty of Tafwid and Rejection of Mu'tazili Rationalism
The author concludes that the correct stance is tafwid and submission, rejecting Mu'tazili rationalism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the correct stance is unconditional submission to Allah's decrees, rejecting the Mu'tazili doctrine of al-aslah.

Core Idea
Allah's actions are not subject to human reason; submission is our duty.

This passage is the concluding argument of a discussion on divine attributes. The author dismantles the Mu'tazili claim that Allah must do what is best for His creatures, showing it leads to absurdity. The only proper response is tafwid (delegation) and idh'an (submission) both outwardly and inwardly.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument against al-aslah
Read the Arabic passage once. Notice how the author uses a conditional: 'if it were obligatory upon Allah to do what is best, then He would not have led people astray.' This is a reductio ad absurdum of the Mu'tazili position.
The phrase 'as they claim' signals that the Mu'tazili view is being rejected.
2
Understand the call to submission
After refuting the Mu'tazili view, the author states that the correct stance is tafwid and idh'an. Reflect on what it means to 'delegate' matters to Allah and submit without questioning.
Tafwid is a key concept in Ash'ari theology: acknowledging that Allah's wisdom is beyond human comprehension.
3
Reflect on the doxology and du'a
The passage ends with praise of Allah and a supplication. Consider how this reinforces the attitude of submission and reliance on Allah's mercy.
The du'a asks for treatment based on grace, not justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على الله تعالى الأصلحُ لعبادِهِ كما يزعمون .. لَمَا أَضلَّهمُ اللهُ تعالى وأعمى بصائرهم وتركهم في عَمَهِ وريبٍ يتردَّدونَ . فقد تبيَّنَ لكلِّ مؤمن بالعِيانِ : أنَّ أحكام العلي ذي الجلال .. لا تُوَزنُ بميزان أهل الاعتزال ، فعرفَ أَنَّ الواجبَ إِنَّما هو التفويضُ والإذعان ظاهراً وباطناً لـمَنْ لا مُعقِّبَ لِحُكْمِهِ ، ولا مُراجِعَ له في قضائِهِ ، ولا جَوَلانَ للعقولِ في سرِّ قَدَرِهِ ، ولا ضدَّ له ولا شبيهَ ولا مثالَ ، فتباركَ اللهُ ربُّ العالمينَ ، اللهم ؛ عاملنا بمخض فضلِكَ وكرمِكَ في الدنيا والآخرة يا أرحم الراحمين.
Upon Allah Almighty is the best for His servants as they claim? Then He would not have led them astray and blinded their insights and left them wandering in darkness and doubt. So it has become clear to every believer by evident sight that the judgments of the Most High, Possessor of Majesty, are not weighed by the scale of the Mu'tazila. So he knew that the duty is only delegation and submission, outwardly and inwardly, to the One whose judgment there is no overturner, and no reviewer of His decree, and no circulation of intellects in the secret of His destiny, and no opposite, no likeness, and no example. So blessed be Allah, Lord of the worlds. O Allah, treat us with the essence of Your grace and generosity in this world and the Hereafter, O Most Merciful of the merciful.
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This passage is a concluding argument against the Mu'tazili doctrine that it is obligatory upon Allah to do what is best (al-aslah) for His creatures. The author states that if that were true, then Allah would not have led people astray and left them in confusion – but He does, so the premise is false. The correct position is that Allah's actions are not subject to human reason; the believer must practice tafwid (delegation of the matter to Allah) and idh'an (submission) both outwardly and inwardly. The author then praises Allah and makes a du'a, emphasizing that Allah's decrees have no overturner, and intellects have no scope to penetrate the secret of His predestination. This lesson thus underscores the Ash'ari rejection of rationalist theology in favor of unconditional submission.

Misconception: One can judge Allah's actions by human reason and find them unjust.
Correction: The passage shows that Allah's judgments are not weighed by human scales; the proper response is submission, not rational evaluation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

What is one specific area where you must stop weighing Allah's action on your own scale?

The author ends with a du'a: 'Treat us with the essence of Your grace and generosity.' This acknowledges that we deserve nothing but Allah's grace, not His justice. Examine your expectations: do you feel entitled to ease and understanding from Allah, as if He owes you what you consider 'best'? Where in your life are you demanding al-aslah from Allah rather than humbly begging for His grace? Will you repent from that entitlement and replace it with submission?

The Mujassima Also Effectively Deny Ru'ya
The commentator notes that the Mujassima share the Mu'tazila's condition for vision, effectively denying ru'ya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mujassima, despite verbally affirming ru'ya, effectively deny it by imposing conditions that contradict Sunni theology.

Core Idea
Affirming ru'ya with conditions is a denial in disguise.

The commentator builds on the previous proof for ru'ya by noting that even those who claim to affirm it may fall into denial if they impose unwarranted conditions. This passage clarifies that the anthropomorphist sects (Mushabbiha) share the Mu'tazila's misguided conditions for vision, effectively contradicting the Sunni position. We will explore this subtle but crucial distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage begins by downplaying the previous argument as additional.
2
Identify the condition imposed by the Mujassima
The passage states that the Mujassima shared with the Mu'tazila the condition that Allah is not seen except under certain conditions (e.g., direction, corporeality). Find this statement.
3
Understand why this condition negates ru'ya
Reflect on why imposing such conditions effectively denies the Sunni belief that Allah can be seen without modality. The commentator says they 'in reality deny vision.'
This is the core argument.
4
Analyze the quote from Ibn al-Tilimsani
Read the quote carefully. It distinguishes between the Sunni position (valid vision without modality) and the Karamiyya and Hashwiyya who disagree in meaning even if they agree in wording.
The quote reinforces the commentator's point.
5
Summarize the lesson
In your own words, explain why affirming ru'ya with conditions amounts to denial according to the commentator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما ذكره المصنف هنا هو من باب زيادة دليل إلى دليل ، فعدم التسليم به لا يضرُّ في ثبوت أصل الرؤية ، ولا سيما أنَّ العقل يجوزها ، والشرع يرجحها . واعلم : أنَّ المشبهة شاركوا المعتزلة في كونه سبحانه وتعالى لا يُرى إلا بتلك الشروط ، ولذا أثبتوا الجسمية له جل شأنه وعز ، فكانوا على التحقيق ممن ينكر الرؤية ، ولذا قال العلامة ابن التلمساني في ( شرح معالم أصول ) (ص ۳۸۱ ) : ( وأهل السنة قالوا : يصح أن يُرى مع تنزهه عن الكيفية ، فهم - يعني : الكرامية والحشوية من الحنابلة ـ مخالفون لهم معنى وإن ساعدوهم لفظاً )
What the author mentioned here is by way of adding a proof to a proof, for not accepting it does not harm the establishment of the reality of vision, especially as reason allows it and scripture gives preponderance to it. And know that the anthropomorphists (mushabbiha) shared with the Mu'tazila in that He, glorified and exalted, is not seen except under those conditions, and therefore they affirmed corporeality (al-jismiyya) for Him, may His majesty be exalted and magnified. So they are in reality among those who deny vision. Hence, the scholar Ibn al-Tilimsani said in (Sharh Ma'alim al-Usul, p. 381): 'And the Ahl al-Sunna said: it is valid that He be seen while being transcendent from modality. They - meaning the Karamiyya and Hashwiyya among the Hanabila - disagree with them in meaning even if they agree with them in wording.'
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage is an editorial note explaining that the previous argument about rays is additional; the main proof for ru'ya is rational possibility and scriptural preponderance. It then points out that the Mujassima (anthropomorphists) such as the Karamiyya and Hashwiyya among the Hanabila, by affirming conditions for vision (like being in a direction), actually join the Mu'tazila in denying ru'ya, because they effectively say God cannot be seen without these conditions, which is not the Sunni position. Thus, despite verbally affirming ru'ya, they deny it in meaning.

Key Terms
مشبهة
جسمية
كرامية
حشوية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That affirming ru'ya is enough without affirming the correct Sunni doctrine that God is seen without modality.
Correction: The commentator shows that even if one verbally affirms ru'ya, imposing conditions like direction or corporeality effectively denies the vision, because the Sunni position is that Allah is seen without any modality.

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator say the Mujassima effectively deny ru'ya?
A) They deny it outright
B) They affirm ru'ya with conditions that contradict Sunni theology
C) They say God cannot be seen at all
D) They say ru'ya is metaphorical

Key Takeaway
The Mujassima, by imposing conditions on ru'ya, effectively deny the Sunni belief that Allah can be seen without modality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever verbally affirmed a belief in Allah's attributes while, in your heart, attaching conditions that limit Him? What condition are you imposing that contradicts the Sunnah, and how will you purify your conviction today?

The Consensus on Wali's Rank Relative to Prophet
Sanusi states the Islamic consensus that a wali never reaches the rank of a prophet and lists prophetic distinctions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic consensus that no wali can reach the rank of a prophet, and you will learn the distinctive characteristics that are unique to prophets.

Core Idea
The highest wali never equals the lowest prophet — consensus of the Muslims.

Sanusi begins by invoking the unanimous agreement of the Muslims (ijma') on a crucial point of doctrine: no saint, no matter how exalted, can attain the station of a prophet. He then enumerates several prophetic privileges — sinlessness, revelation, and universal mission — that set prophets apart forever. This passage firmly guards against the extreme view that some awliya might surpass prophets.

Guided Path
1
Understand the consensus statement
Read the opening line where Sanusi declares the unanimous agreement of Muslims. Notice the word 'أجمعوا' (they unanimously agreed).
2
Identify the prophetic specificities
The passage lists several unique qualities of prophets. List them: sinlessness, security from bad end, revelation, seeing angels, being sent for reform of both worlds.
3
Recognize the refuted claim
The final incomplete sentence indicates that the opinion of some (who might claim a wali can be superior) is disregarded. Reflect on why this consensus is important in Sunni theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم : أنَّ المسلمين أجمعوا على أنَّ الوليَّ لا يصل إلى درجةِ النبي ؛ إذْ مِنْ خاصَّةِ النبيَّ معَ ما حازَهُ مِنْ شرفِ الولايةِ أَنَّهُ معصوم عنِ المعاصي ، مأمونٌ مِنْ سوء العاقبة بحكم النصوص القاطعة ، مُشرَّفٌ بالوحي ومشاهدة المَلَكِ ، مبعوث لإصلاح حال العالم ونظام أمر المعاش والمعادِ ، إلى غير ذلكَ مِنَ الكمالاتِ ، ولا يُعتَدُّ بقول بعض
And know that the Muslims have unanimously agreed that the wali does not reach the rank of the Prophet; because among the specificities of the Prophet, besides the honor of guardianship (wilaya) that he possesses, is that he is sinless (ma'sum), secure from bad end by virtue of definitive texts (nusus qati'a), honored with revelation (wahy) and seeing the angel (mushahadat al-malak), sent to reform the state of the world and the order of livelihood and the afterlife (al-ma'ash wa al-ma'ad), and other such perfections. And the saying of some is not taken into account...
Source pages p. 521

Commentary
This passage establishes a fundamental doctrinal point: the Muslim consensus (ijma') that a wali (saint) can never reach the rank of a prophet. The author then lists some distinctive characteristics of the prophet (al-nabi) beyond the honor of wilayah (guardianship) itself: (1) 'isma (infallibility from sins), (2) being secure from a bad end based on definitive scriptural evidence, (3) being honored with revelation and witnessing the angel, and (4) being sent to reform the world, including both worldly affairs (al-ma'ash) and afterlife affairs (al-ma'ad). These perfections (kamilat) are unique to prophets. The passage ends with an incomplete statement that the saying of some (perhaps those who claim a wali can be superior to a prophet) is not considered valid.

Key Terms
الولي
النبي
الإجماع
العصمة
الوحي
المشاهدة
المعاش والمعاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that a wali can reach or surpass the rank of a prophet.
Correction: The Muslim consensus (ijma') definitively states that no wali can reach the rank of a prophet, as prophets have unique attributes like sinlessness, revelation, and universal mission.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is one specific characteristic that distinguishes a prophet from a wali?
A) The wali can also receive revelation
B) The prophet is sinless (ma'sum)
C) The wali has a higher rank
D) The prophet cannot have wilayah

Key Takeaway
The Muslim consensus affirms that prophets hold a unique rank above all awliya due to exclusive divine distinctions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever secretly desired a direct, extraordinary spiritual experience (like a vision or dream) more than you desire to follow the prophetic sunnah in your daily life? How will you recalibrate your heart to honor the Prophet ﷺ above all else?
?
The Prophet ﷺ was sent to reform both your worldly livelihood and your afterlife. Which of these two aspects have you been neglecting? What is one concrete change you will make today to bring your daily work and your spiritual goals into alignment?
?
If the highest wali cannot reach the lowest prophet, what does that say about your own need to constantly learn and apply the prophetic example rather than seeking shortcuts or spiritual 'rank'? What is one area of your life where you have been following your own desires rather than the prophetic guidance, and what step will you take to correct it?

The State of Saints: Absorption and Rational Madness
Describes saints' spiritual absorption and blameless neglect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how saints may become so absorbed in divine contemplation that they neglect obligations without sin, and the concept of 'rational madmen'.

Core Idea
Saints in deep absorption are like sleepers, blameless but imperfect.

This passage from Sanusi's work describes an extraordinary spiritual state: saints who become completely absorbed in God can neglect religious duties without sin, akin to being asleep. It also introduces the unusual term 'rational madmen'. Let's explore this concept.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on saints' absorption
Read the Arabic passage once, then follow the translation. Notice how the author describes the saint's state.
2
Understand the condition: neglect without sin
The saint neglects obligations but does not sin. Identify the reason given: he is like a sleeping person.
The analogy of sleep is key.
3
Note the analogy of sleep
Why is the saint compared to one asleep? Because he is unable to observe both worlds simultaneously.
4
Learn the term 'rational madmen'
This heedlessness is called 'madness' but a specific type: rational madmen. Reflect on why they are considered rational.
The term 'majanin al-‘uqala' is unique.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
معارج الملكِ إلى منازل الحيوانِ ، بل ربَّما يحصلُ لهُ كمالُ الانجذابِ إلى عالم القدس ، والاستغراق في ملاحظة جانب الحقِّ ، فيَذهَلُ عن هذا العالم ، ويُخِلُّ بالتكاليفِ مِنْ غيرِ تأثُم بذلكَ ؛ لكونه في حُكْمِ كالنائم ؛ وذلك لعجزه عن مراعاة الأمرين ، وملاحظة الجانبين ، فربَّما يسألُ دوام تلكَ الحالة ، وعدم العود إلى عالم ، وهذا الدُّهولُ هو الجنونُ الذي ربَّما يُر. الجنونُ الذي ربَّما يُرجحُ على بعضِ غيرِ المكلَّف الظاهرِ العقولِ ، والمتسمَّونَ بهِ هُمُ المسمَّونَ بمجانين العقلاء (1) وبهذا يظهرُ فضلُ الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام على الأولياء ؛ فإنَّهم مع أنَّ استغراقهم أكمل ، وانجذابهم أشمل .. لا يُخِلُّونَ بأدنى طاعةٍ ، ولا يَذْهَلُونَ عن هذا الجانبِ ساعةٌ ؛ لأنَّ قوَّتَهمُ القدسيَّةَ مِنَ الكمال ، بحيثُ لا يشغلها شاغل عن ذلكَ الجناب ، ولهذا يُعاتبونَ على أدنى ذهول عن الأولى مِنْ مراتبِ الصواب
The ascents of the kingdom to the stations of the animal, but rather perhaps he obtains complete attraction to the world of holiness, and immersion in observing the side of the Truth, so he becomes heedless of this world, and neglects obligations without thereby sinning; because he is in the ruling of one asleep; and that is due to his inability to observe both matters and consider both sides. So perhaps he asks for the continuance of that state and not returning to the world, and this heedlessness is the madness which may [؟] be preferred over some of those not obligated, apparent intellects, and those characterized by it are called the rational madmen (1). And by this the superiority of the prophets, peace and blessings be upon them, over the saints becomes apparent; for they, while their immersion is more complete and their attraction more comprehensive, do not neglect the slightest act of obedience, nor are they heedless of this side for an hour; because their holy power is of such perfection that no distraction distracts them from that presence, and thus they are reproached for the slightest heedlessness regarding the better rank of correctness.
Source pages p. 524

Commentary
This passage discusses the spiritual state of saints (awliya) who become so absorbed in divine contemplation that they may neglect religious obligations, but without sin, akin to one asleep. It then contrasts this with the prophets, who maintain perfect attention to duties despite their greater absorption, showing their superiority. The passage begins by describing how a saint may achieve complete attraction to the spiritual world and become heedless of this world, neglecting duties without sin because he is in a state like sleep, unable to attend to both worlds. Such a saint may even wish to remain in that state permanently. This heedlessness is a form of madness—called 'the madness of the rational'—and these individuals are known as 'rational madmen' (majanin al-‘uqala). Then the author states that this clarifies the superiority of prophets over saints: prophets, despite their even more complete immersion and attraction, never neglect any act of obedience nor become heedless for a moment, because their holy power is so perfect that nothing distracts them from God. For this reason, they are reproached for even the slightest lapse from the better rank of correctness.

Key Terms
الأولياء
الاستغراق
الجنون
مجانين العقلاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that neglecting religious duties is always sinful, regardless of state.
Correction: The passage shows that in extreme spiritual absorption, saints may neglect duties without sin, like a sleeper.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the saint not sin when neglecting obligations?
A) Because he is not obligated
B) Because he is in a state like sleep
C) Because his absorption is forced
D) Because he is a prophet

Key Takeaway
Saints in complete absorption are considered like sleepers, and their neglect of duties is not sinful.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever used the excuse of being 'spiritually absorbed' to avoid fulfilling your religious duties? How does this lesson challenge that excuse?
?
Are you more like the saints who are so absorbed in God that they forget everything, or like those who are heedless of the divine? What does your neglect reveal about your true priorities?
?
What would it take for you to reach such a state of absorption that you become like a sleeper to this world? Is that a goal you genuinely desire, or a warning against abandoning your responsibilities?

The Superiority of Prophets over Saints
Argues for prophets' superiority over saints based on their perfect attention to duties.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why prophets are superior to saints: they maintain perfect obedience despite greater spiritual absorption.

Core Idea
Prophets combine complete absorption with perfect observance of duties.

After describing the state of saints, Sanusi now explains why prophets are superior. Despite having even deeper spiritual immersion, prophets never neglect any act of obedience, demonstrating the perfection of their holy power. Let's see why.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on prophets' superiority
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Focus on the contrast with saints.
2
Contrast with saints: greater absorption yet no neglect
Prophets have more complete immersion but do not neglect any duty. Notice the conjunction 'ma‘ anna' (despite that).
3
Understand the reason: perfect holy power
Their holy power is so perfect that nothing distracts them from God. Identify this explanation.
The term 'quwwatuhum al-qudsiyyah' is key.
4
Note the implication: prophets are reproached for slight lapses
Even the slightest heedlessness from the best course is reproached, highlighting their high station.

The Reality of Sihr: Rationally Possible and Scripturally Confirmed
Sanusi proves that sihr is rationally possible and actually occurs, refuting Mu'tazila denial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sanusi affirms that sihr (sorcery) is rationally possible and actually exists, and how he refutes the Mu'tazilite denial using reason and revelation.

Core Idea
Sihr is real but its effects come from God, not the sorcerer.

In this lesson, Sanusi tackles a theological controversy: do sorcery and the evil eye have real effects, or are they mere illusions? He presents the Sunni position that they are rationally permissible and confirmed by scripture, and he answers the Mu'tazilite objection. You will see how he grounds his argument in the universality of God's power and the concept of customary causation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the concise style and the use of Qur'anic citations.
2
Identify the two opposing positions
The passage presents the Sunni view (Ahl al-Haqq) and the Mu'tazilite view. Note how each is described and what evidence they rely on.
The Mu'tazila compare sihr to sleight-of-hand.
3
Understand the Sunni proof
Sanusi gives a rational proof for the permissibility of sihr. Identify the two premises: possibility in itself and God's universal power. Also, note the concept of 'customary cause' (sabab 'adi).
This proof refutes the idea that sihr implies independent creative power in the sorcerer.
4
Analyze the Qur'anic evidence
Sanusi cites al-Baqarah 2:102 and then addresses the objection from Taha 20:66. Follow how he interprets the latter to defend the reality of sihr.
The key is that even if the effect is illusion, it is still a real phenomenon created by God.
5
Review the objection and answer
Examine the objection from the story of Musa and how Sanusi answers it. Note the two possible responses: either the sorcerers produced real illusion, or even if conceded, the effect being illusion does not negate all reality.
This shows careful dialectical reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهو بالعين عند أهل الحق جائز عقلاً ، ثابت سمعاً ، وكذا الإصابة
وقالت المعتزلة : بل هو مجرد إراءة وتخييل لا حقيقة له ؛ بمنزلة الشعبذة التي سببها خفة حركات اليد ، أو إخفاء وجه الحيلة فيه ودليل الجواز عند أهل الحق : إمكان ذلك الأمر في نفسه ، وعموم قدرة الله تعالى ؛ فإنه جل وعلا هو الخالق ، لا مخترع سواه ، وإنما الساحر يضاف إليه الفعل لا على سبيل أنه اخترعه أو له تأثير ما ، بل على أنه سبب عادي لذلك ؛ كالطعام للشبع ونحوه من العاديات . ولهذا قال تعالى: ﴿ يُعَلِّمُونَ النَّاسَ السّحْرَ ... إلى قوله تعالى : ﴿فَيَتَعَلَّمُونَ مِنْهُمَا مَا يُفَرِّقُونَ بِهِ بَيْنَ الْمَرْءِ وَزَوْجِهِ ۚ وَمَا هُم بِضَارِّينَ بِهِ مِنْ أَحَدٍ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِ اللهِ ﴾ [البقرة : ١٠٢] ، ففي الآية إشعار بأن السحر ثابت واقع حقيقةً ، ليس بمجرد إراءة وتمويه ، ودلت على أن المؤثر والخالق إنما هو الله تعالى وحده
فإن قيل : قوله تعالى في قصة موسى عليه السلام : ﴿ يُخَيَّلُ إِلَيْهِ مِن سِحْرِهِمْ أَنَّهَا تَسْعَى ﴾ [طه : ٦٦] يدل على أنه لا حقيقة للسحر ، وإنما تخييل وتموية .
أجيب : بجواز أن يكون سحرهم إيقاع ذلك التخييل ، وقد خلقه الله تعالى عند ذلك الفعل الذي وقع على أيديهم ، ولو سلم فكون أثره في تلك الصورة هو التخييل لا يدل على أنه لا حقيقة له أصلاً
And it [sihr] and the [evil] eye are, according to Ahl al-Haqq, rationally permissible, confirmed by revelation, and likewise the affliction. The Mu'tazila said: 'Rather it is mere illusion and imagination, having no reality; like sleight-of-hand which is caused by quickness of hand movements, or hiding the trick.' The proof of permissibility according to Ahl al-Haqq is the possibility of that thing in itself, and the universality of God's power; for He, Glorious and Exalted, is the Creator, no inventor other than Him. The sorcerer's action is attributed to him not as innovation or independent effect, but as a customary cause for that [effect], like food for satiety and similar customary matters. Therefore He, Exalted, said: 'They teach people sorcery... to His saying: '...and they learned from them that by which they cause separation between a man and his wife. But they do not harm anyone through it except by permission of God'' [al-Baqarah 2:102]. In the verse there is indication that sorcery is established, occurring in reality, not mere illusion and deception, and it indicates that the effective agent and Creator is only God, Exalted, alone. If it is said: His saying in the story of Moses, peace be upon him: 'It seemed to him from their sorcery that they were moving' [Taha 20:66] indicates that sorcery has no reality, but rather it is imagination and deception. It is answered: by the possibility that their sorcery was causing that imagination, and God created it at that act which occurred at their hands. And even if it is conceded, then the fact that its effect in that form was imagination does not prove that it has no reality at all.
Source pages p. 525

Commentary
This passage defends the reality of sorcery. Sanusi first states that both sihr and the evil eye are rationally permissible (jā’iz ‘aqlan) and confirmed by revelation (thābit sam‘an). He then reports the Mu'tazilite view that sihr is mere illusion and sleight of hand. The proof of its possibility for Ahl al-Ḥaqq is that such events are inherently possible and within God's universal power. The sorcerer's action is only a customary cause (sabab ‘ādī), not an independent creation. The Qur'anic verse (al-Baqarah 102) confirms that sorcery is real and causes harm only by God's permission. The objection from the story of Musa (the illusion of snakes) is answered: the sorcerers' act produced real illusion not mere trickery, and God created the effect. The final sentence emphasizes that even if the effect is illusion, that does not negate its reality in its own realm.

Key Terms
سحر
إراءة
تخييل
شعبذة
سبب عادي
إذن الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse from Surah Taha (20:66) proves that sorcery has no reality at all; it is pure illusion.
Correction: Sanusi explains that the verse only describes the specific effect of the sorcerers' act (imagination), but does not negate the reality of sorcery in general. The effect itself is real (a real illusion created by God).

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is the relationship between the sorcerer's act and the effect?
A) The sorcerer creates the effect independently.
B) The effect is purely imaginary with no causation.
C) The sorcerer's act is a customary cause; God creates the effect.
D) The sorcerer's act is irrelevant.

Key Takeaway
Sihr is real but its ultimate cause is God; the sorcerer is only a customary means, and scriptural evidence confirms its reality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face fears of the unseen, do you truly believe that even black magic cannot touch you without God's permission, or does a part of your heart still attribute power to creatures?
?
The Mu'tazila denied sihr because they overestimated reason and underestimated revelation. Where in your life do you trust your intellect more than what God has revealed, even when it contradicts your reasoning?
?
If sihr's reality means that every effect—good or bad—comes only from God, how does that change the way you respond to harm or misfortune that comes to you or your loved ones? Will you turn to God alone or still fear human agents?

Mu'tazila Views on the Fate of the Disobedient
Taftazani explains the dominant Mu'tazila view and its exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the internal diversity among Mu'tazila scholars regarding the fate of the disobedient believer, particularly the weight-based approach of al-Jubba'i and his followers.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila were not unanimous on eternal punishment; many said the fate depends on weighing sins against rewards.

This passage from Taftazani clarifies a common misconception about Mu'tazila theology. While they are known for teaching that unrepentant sinners will be eternally punished, this was not the only view. Taftazani explains that many leading Mu'tazila scholars held a more nuanced position based on the relative weight of sin and reward.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let Taftazani's reporting style come through.
Note the names: al-Jubba'i, Abu Hashim, al-Ka'bi.
2
Identify the main positions
Look for the correction of the common view, the condition of weight (punishment exceeding reward), and the exception of al-Ka'bi.
The passage distinguishes between the famous view and the preferred view of many Mu'tazila.
3
Understand the role of revelation vs. reason
Notice that the judgment when weights are equal is based on revelation, but rationally forgiveness is possible.
This highlights the Mu'tazila reliance on reason within the bounds of scripture.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال التفتازاني : ( ونحنُ نقولُ : ينبغي أنْ يكونَ مَا اسْتَهرَ عَنِ المعتزلة مِنْ خلودِ العاصي غيرِ التائبِ في النارِ مذهبَ بعضهم ، والمختار لهم : خلافُهُ ؛ لأنَّ مذهب الجبائي وأبي هاشم وكثيرٍ مِنْ محققيهم - وهو اختيار المتأخرين منهم - : أنَّ الكبائرَ إِنَّما تُسقِط الطاعةَ ، وتُوجِبُ دخول النارِ إذا زادَ عقابها على ثوابها ، والعلم بذلك مُفوَّضٌ إلى الله تعالى ؛ فمَنْ خلط الحسناتِ بالسيئاتِ ، ولم تُعلَمْ غلبه الأوزارِ .. لم يُحكَمْ عليهِ بدخولِ النارِ ، بل إذا زادَ الثوابُ يُحكَمُ بأَنَّهُ لا يدخلُ النارَ أصلاً (١) واضطربوا فيما إذا تساوى الثواب والعقاب ، وصرَّحوا بأنَّ هذا بحسَبِ السمعِ ، وأمَّا بحسَبِ العقلِ فيجوزُ العفو عن الكبائر كلها(۲) (۳) إلا عند الكعبي ((٣) وقال في موضع آخر : ( اختلف أبو علي وأبو هاشم فزعم أبو علي : أنَّ الأقل يسقط ولا يسقط مِنَ الأكثر شيء ، وسقوطُ الأقلّ يكونُ عقاباً إن كانَ الساقط ثواباً ، وثواباً إنْ كانَ الساقط عقاباً ، وهذا هو الإحباط المخضُ وقال أبو هاشم : الأقلُّ يسقط ويسقط مِنَ الأكثرِ ما يقابله ؛ مثلُ مَنْ لَهُ مئةً جزءٍ مِنَ العقابِ واكتسب ألفَ جزءٍ مِنَ الثوابِ مثلاً ؛ فإِنَّهُ
Al-Taftazani said: (And we say: It should be that what is famous from the Mu'tazila about the eternity of the disobedient one who does not repent in the fire is the doctrine of some of them, and the preferred view for them is contrary to it; because the doctrine of al-Jubba'i and Abu Hashim and many of their investigators – and it is the choice of their later scholars – is that major sins only nullify obedience and necessitate entry into the fire if their punishment exceeds their reward, and knowledge of that is entrusted to Allah; so whoever mixes good deeds with bad deeds, and the preponderance of sins is not known – he is not judged to enter the fire, rather if the reward exceeds, he is judged that he does not enter the fire at all. (1) And they disagreed about when reward and punishment are equal, and they stated that this is according to revelation, and as for reason, it is permissible to forgive all major sins (2) (3) except according to al-Ka'bi. (3) And he said in another place: (Abu Ali and Abu Hashim disagreed: Abu Ali claimed that the lesser is nullified and nothing of the greater is nullified, and the nullification of the lesser is punishment if the nullified was reward, and reward if the nullified was punishment, and this is pure nullification (al-ihbat al-mahd). And Abu Hashim said: The lesser is nullified and what is equivalent to it from the greater is nullified; for example, someone who has one hundred units of punishment and acquires one thousand units of reward, then...
Source pages p. 550

Commentary
This passage is a quotation from al-Taftazani that presents internal Mu'tazila views. It begins by clarifying that the well-known Mu'tazila stance of eternal punishment for unrepentant sinners is only the position of some; the preferred view among many, including al-Jubba'i and Abu Hashim, is that major sins nullify obedience but only necessitate Hell if the punishment outweighs the reward; if the reward outweighs, the person does not enter Hell at all. There is disagreement when reward and punishment are equal; they judge by revelation, but rationally forgiveness is permissible except for al-Ka'bi. Then Taftazani reports a second disagreement on the nature of nullification (ihbat) between Abu Ali and Abu Hashim: Abu Ali holds that only the lesser amount is nullified and nothing of the greater is affected; the nullified amount becomes punishment if it was reward, and vice versa. Abu Hashim holds that the lesser is nullified and an equal amount of the greater is also nullified, illustrated by an example with 100 parts punishment and 1000 parts reward.

Key Terms
ثواب
عقاب
الجبائي
أبو هاشم
الكعبي
إحباط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All Mu'tazila believed in eternal punishment for any major sin without repentance.
Correction: Taftazani shows that many Mu'tazila scholars, including al-Jubba'i and Abu Hashim, held that the punishment is not eternal if reward outweighs sin.

Checkpoint
According to Taftazani, what determines whether a disobedient believer enters Hell according to al-Jubba'i and Abu Hashim?
A) The number of sins committed
B) Whether punishment outweighs reward
C) The type of major sin
D) Whether the person repents

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila had internal debates on the fate of sinners, with many scholars conditioning eternal punishment on the outweighing of sin over reward.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about your own record of deeds, do you ever assume your good deeds outweigh your sins? How does the Mu'tazila teaching that only Allah knows the balance challenge you to be more humble and less presumptuous about your standing?
?
The passage says knowledge of the weighing is entrusted to Allah. How does this affect your anxiety about the fate of loved ones who died with sins? Can you truly trust Allah's justice without needing to calculate the outcome yourself?
?
Al-Jubba'i and Abu Hashim conditioned eternal punishment on the outweighing of punishment over reward. Are you living with the constant awareness that your actions are being weighed? What specific sin or habit would you start addressing today if you took this teaching seriously?

Sects and Disagreements
advanced
5 min
Abu Ali vs. Abu Hashim on Ihbat
Taftazani reports the disagreement on ihbat between Abu Ali and Abu Hashim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two competing theories of nullification (ihbat) held by Abu Ali al-Jubba'i and his son Abu Hashim.

Core Idea
Nullification of lesser good deeds can turn them into punishment, according to Abu Ali; Abu Hashim adds that an equal portion of greater deeds is also nullified.

This passage dives into a technical dispute within the Mu'tazila school about how good and bad deeds interact. The concept of ihbat (nullification) is central to their soteriology. Taftazani reports the positions of Abu Ali and his son Abu Hashim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scholars and their disagreement
Abu Ali (al-Jubba'i) and Abu Hashim (his son) had conflicting views on how nullification works.
This is a nuanced theological technicality.
2
Understand Abu Ali's view
Abu Ali held that only the lesser amount of reward or punishment is nullified, and nothing of the greater is affected. The nullified amount becomes its opposite (reward becomes punishment, etc.).
This is called 'pure ihbat' (al-ihbat al-mahd).
3
Understand Abu Hashim's view
Abu Hashim held that the lesser is nullified, and an equal amount from the greater is also nullified. He gave an example with 100 parts punishment and 1000 parts reward.
Here, 100 parts from the reward would be nullified alongside the 100 parts punishment.
4
Consider the implications
These different mechanisms lead to different outcomes for the believer's ultimate fate.
Think about the severity of punishment or reward remaining.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال التفتازاني : ( ونحنُ نقولُ : ينبغي أنْ يكونَ مَا اسْتَهرَ عَنِ المعتزلة مِنْ خلودِ العاصي غيرِ التائبِ في النارِ مذهبَ بعضهم ، والمختار لهم : خلافُهُ ؛ لأنَّ مذهب الجبائي وأبي هاشم وكثيرٍ مِنْ محققيهم - وهو اختيار المتأخرين منهم - : أنَّ الكبائرَ إِنَّما تُسقِط الطاعةَ ، وتُوجِبُ دخول النارِ إذا زادَ عقابها على ثوابها ، والعلم بذلك مُفوَّضٌ إلى الله تعالى ؛ فمَنْ خلط الحسناتِ بالسيئاتِ ، ولم تُعلَمْ غلبه الأوزارِ .. لم يُحكَمْ عليهِ بدخولِ النارِ ، بل إذا زادَ الثوابُ يُحكَمُ بأَنَّهُ لا يدخلُ النارَ أصلاً (١) واضطربوا فيما إذا تساوى الثواب والعقاب ، وصرَّحوا بأنَّ هذا بحسَبِ السمعِ ، وأمَّا بحسَبِ العقلِ فيجوزُ العفو عن الكبائر كلها(۲) (۳) إلا عند الكعبي ((٣) وقال في موضع آخر : ( اختلف أبو علي وأبو هاشم فزعم أبو علي : أنَّ الأقل يسقط ولا يسقط مِنَ الأكثر شيء ، وسقوطُ الأقلّ يكونُ عقاباً إن كانَ الساقط ثواباً ، وثواباً إنْ كانَ الساقط عقاباً ، وهذا هو الإحباط المخضُ وقال أبو هاشم : الأقلُّ يسقط ويسقط مِنَ الأكثرِ ما يقابله ؛ مثلُ مَنْ لَهُ مئةً جزءٍ مِنَ العقابِ واكتسب ألفَ جزءٍ مِنَ الثوابِ مثلاً ؛ فإِنَّهُ
Al-Taftazani said: (And we say: It should be that what is famous from the Mu'tazila about the eternity of the disobedient one who does not repent in the fire is the doctrine of some of them, and the preferred view for them is contrary to it; because the doctrine of al-Jubba'i and Abu Hashim and many of their investigators – and it is the choice of their later scholars – is that major sins only nullify obedience and necessitate entry into the fire if their punishment exceeds their reward, and knowledge of that is entrusted to Allah; so whoever mixes good deeds with bad deeds, and the preponderance of sins is not known – he is not judged to enter the fire, rather if the reward exceeds, he is judged that he does not enter the fire at all. (1) And they disagreed about when reward and punishment are equal, and they stated that this is according to revelation, and as for reason, it is permissible to forgive all major sins (2) (3) except according to al-Ka'bi. (3) And he said in another place: (Abu Ali and Abu Hashim disagreed: Abu Ali claimed that the lesser is nullified and nothing of the greater is nullified, and the nullification of the lesser is punishment if the nullified was reward, and reward if the nullified was punishment, and this is pure nullification (al-ihbat al-mahd). And Abu Hashim said: The lesser is nullified and what is equivalent to it from the greater is nullified; for example, someone who has one hundred units of punishment and acquires one thousand units of reward, then...

Commentary
This passage is a quotation from al-Taftazani that presents internal Mu'tazila views. It begins by clarifying that the well-known Mu'tazila stance of eternal punishment for unrepentant sinners is only the position of some; the preferred view among many, including al-Jubba'i and Abu Hashim, is that major sins nullify obedience but only necessitate Hell if the punishment outweighs the reward; if the reward outweighs, the person does not enter Hell at all. Abu Hashim holds that the lesser is nullified and an equal amount of the greater is also nullified, illustrated by an example with 100 parts punishment and 1000 parts reward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ihbat means all sins are canceled by good deeds.
Correction: Ihbat specifically refers to the nullification of the lesser amount of good or bad deeds, not complete cancellation; the scholars disagreed on whether the greater is affected proportionally.

Checkpoint
According to Taftazani, what did Abu Ali say happens when the lesser amount is nullified?
A) It becomes punishment if it was reward, and reward if it was punishment.
B) It simply disappears.
C) It is transferred to the other person's account.
D) It is divided equally.

Key Takeaway
Abu Ali and Abu Hashim differed on whether nullification affects only the lesser deeds or also an equivalent portion of the greater deeds.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider a good deed you performed recently that you fear may be nullified by a subsequent sin. Abu Ali says the nullified reward becomes punishment. What specific action will you take today to seek Allah's forgiveness and protect your remaining good deeds?
?
If nullification can turn punishment into reward (as per Abu Ali), how does this impact your hope in Allah's mercy? Write one concrete habit you will adopt to turn your past misdeeds into opportunities for reward.

Sects and Disagreements
beginner
4 min
Cross-Madhhab Hisba: Hanafi and Shafi'i Examples
Sanusi gives a cross-madhhab example from al-Muhit al-Hanafiyya on hisba between Hanafis and Shafi'is.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how hisba applies across different madhahib, using specific examples from the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools cited by Sanusi.

Core Idea
Hisba can be performed across madhahib based on each school's own rulings.

Sanusi cites the Hanafi work al-Muhit al-Hanafiyya to illustrate that hisba is not limited to one's own madhhab. Rather, a Hanafi may enjoin or forbid a Shafi'i in matters considered sinful in the Hanafi school, and vice versa. This passage gives concrete examples of such cross-madhhab hisba, showing practical application of the principle.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Note the two sets of examples: Hanafi vs Shafi'i and Shafi'i vs Hanafi.
2
Identify the four specific cases
List the actions: eating hyena and omitting basmalah intentionally (Hanafi against Shafi'i), drinking al-muthallath and marriage without guardian (Shafi'i against Hanafi). Understand why each is considered sinful in the respective school.
These are matters of legal disagreement between the two schools.
3
Reflect on the principle
Consider how this shows that hisba is not restricted to one's own madhhab. A Hanafi can enjoin a Shafi'i based on Hanafi ruling, as long as it is a valid matter of hisba. This demonstrates the practical scope of hisba in a multi-madhhab context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر في محيطِ الحنفيَّةِ » : أنَّ للحنفي أن يحتسب على الشافعي في أكل الضبع ، ومتروكِ التسمية عمداً ، وللشافعي أن يحتسب على الحنفي في شرب المثلث ، والنكاح بلا ولي (٣) .
And it is mentioned in 'al-Muhit al-Hanafiyya' that a Hanafi may perform hisba against a Shafi'i regarding eating of hyena, and [eating] meat omitted of the basmalah intentionally, and a Shafi'i may perform hisba against a Hanafi regarding drinking of al-muthallath, and marriage without a guardian.
Source pages p. 561

Commentary
This passage cites the Hanafi work 'al-Muhit al-Hanafiyya' to illustrate the practical application of cross-madhhab hisba. According to this source, a Hanafi may command or forbid a Shafi'i concerning matters considered sinful in the Hanafi school but permissible in the Shafi'i school, such as eating hyena (al-dab') or meat on which the basmalah was intentionally omitted (matruk al-tasmiyya 'amdan). Conversely, a Shafi'i may do the same to a Hanafi regarding drinking al-muthallath (a type of date wine) and marriage without a guardian (nikah bila wali). This shows that, in matters of disagreement, each school may act based on its own ruling, as long as it is within the permissible bounds of hisba.

Key Terms
احتسب
الضبع
متروك التسمية
المثلث
النكاح بلا ولي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That cross-madhhab hisba is forbidden or constitutes interference.
Correction: This passage shows that it is permissible for a Hanafi to enjoin a Shafi'i on matters considered sinful in the Hanafi school, and vice versa, based on each school's own rulings.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is one thing a Hanafi may perform hisba against a Shafi'i for?
A) Drinking al-muthallath.
B) Marriage without a guardian.
C) Eating hyena.
D) Divorce without witnesses.

Key Takeaway
Cross-madhhab hisba is permissible; a Hanafi may enjoin a Shafi'i on matters prohibited in the Hanafi school, and a Shafi'i may enjoin a Hanafi on matters prohibited in the Shafi'i school.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Would you ever correct a fellow Muslim for something that is not wrong in their madhhab but is in yours, even if it might strain the relationship? Are you willing to risk that for the sake of what you believe is right?
?
If someone from a different school corrected you on a matter you follow your own scholars on, would your first reaction be defensiveness or sincere reflection? What does that reveal about your heart?
?
The examples in this lesson require real courage to enact—could you, right now, name one issue where you would act as a Hanafi or Shafi'i toward someone from another school? If not, what is stopping you?
